2.30. Weapons and Ammunition.
   2.30.1. The IDO will determine the number of small arms/light weapons required to support
   an installation's maximum simultaneous deployment capability on an annual basis.
   2.30.2. The IDO, in coordination with the Munitions Accountable Systems Officer (MASO),
   will use AFI 21-201 to determine the authorized quantities of ammunition to be stocked and
   stored on the installation to support deployment capability on an annual basis.
   2.30.3. MAJCOMs will provide guidance for requirements computation and coordination
   such as in the case of Institutional Forces.
   2.30.4. As noted in AFI 31-207, commanders may arm deployable forces to support
   contingency, wartime, or training operations.
      2.30.4.1. IDOs and units will consult OPLANs and CONPLANs that the installation is
      tasked to support for specifics describing the type of small arms/light weapons required,
      the arming mission, the anticipated tasks armed members will perform, and the command
      and control elements.
      2.30.4.2. Tasking messages (or reporting instructions) will also describe arming
      requirements for current operations.
   2.30.5. As a minimum, the number of weapons required will be determined by summing all
   the DW and AW counters within a unit.
      2.30.5.1. J-suffix coded UTCs may not be required to have small arms/light weapons
      unless directed by the owning command.
      2.30.5.2. IDOs and units will consult AFCAT 21-209 Volume 1, Chapter 3, and AFI 21-
      201 to determine ammunition quantities authorized to be stocked and stored at the base to
      support deployment requirements.
      2.30.5.3. Unit commanders are responsible for the procurement, establishment of
      accounts, documentation, transportation and maintenance of weapons and ammunition
      IAW AFI 21-201.
      2.30.5.4. (Added-USAFE) In USAFE-AFAFRICA, designated aggregation bases
      (Aviano, Mildenhall, Spangdahlem, and Ramstein) will include a 5% overage to their
      minimum number of weapons required. This will accommodate short notice taskings
      from origins with difficulties moving weapons without proper lead time. Aggregation
      bases must document issue, receipt, and turn-in procedures in their IDPs or installation
      reporting instructions.
2.31. Medical Requirements.
   2.31.1. The Medical Group, with the IDO’s assistance, will develop a process to ensure
   deploying personnel receive pre-deployment medical threat/countermeasure briefing and
   complete all pre-deployment medical requirements. Medical deployment requirements are
   outlined in Attachment 20.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        89


      2.31.1.1. DELETED
      2.31.1.2. DELETED
   2.31.2. Force Health Protection Prescription Products (FHPPPs) will be managed IAW AFI
   44-102, Medical Care Management.
      2.31.2.1. FHPPPs are comprised of such products as atropine and/or 2-Pam chloride
      auto-injectors, certain antimicrobials, anti-malarias, and pyridostigmine bromide (PB
      Tabs).
      2.31.2.2. FHPPP requirements must be on CED orders before FHPPP can be dispensed
      to a deploying member.
   2.31.3. The LRS/Plans and Integration Section will provide an updated UDM listing to the
   MTF (PH/FHM) quarterly or as changes occur.
   2.31.4. DELETED

Section 2E—Installation Deployment Plan (IDP)

2.32. Installation Deployment Plan (IDP) development.
   2.32.1. The host Installation/Wing Commander, through the IDP, defines local processes,
   procedures, infrastructure, and resources used to deploy forces.
      2.32.1.1. The IDO develops the IDP for the host Installation/Wing Commander.
      2.32.1.2. The IDO must analyze inputs from all assigned or attached units (including
      collocated, GSU, tenant, Institutional, and transient units) and develop local operations
      guidance on how units will deploy from the installation. Include processes for executing
      all contingencies, exercises, and other deployments.
      2.32.1.3. (Added-USAFE) The creation of an IDP is mandatory at all USAFE-
      AFAFRICA MOBs (Aviano, Incirlik, Lakenheath, Mildenhall, Spangdahlem, and
      Ramstein). IDPs must include deployment planning and execution procedures and
      processes for assigned GSUs, remote sites or other isolated areas, and NATO supported
      personnel within the USAFE-AFAFRICA AOR.
   2.32.2. The IDP must describe who, what, when, where, and how the installation meets each
   basic deployment requirement.
   2.32.3. As the deployment process owner, the host Installation/Wing Commander must
   ensure the IDO and the deployment planning and execution community are in step with his
   or her direction.
   2.32.4. The IDO/IRO will conduct an annual IDP briefing to the host Installation/Wing
   Commander and senior staff in order to review the status of the IDP and all requirements as
   listed in Attachment 12. Briefing attendance and content will be documented in writing and
   maintained by the IDO.
   2.32.5. The IDO will analyze all applicable planning documents to ensure the IDP addresses
   the full range of military operations the installation is identified to support.
      2.32.5.1. DELETED
90                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


     2.32.5.2. DELETED
     2.32.5.3. IDPs for forward presence forces should include HN resources available to
     successfully execute deployment and redeployment operations.
         2.32.5.3.1. HN agreements, such as status-of-forces agreements and multinational
         and/or bilateral agreements negotiated before crisis situations arise facilitate needed
         access to HN resources.
         2.32.5.3.2. HNs may provide a variety of services through their national agencies in
         support of deployment and redeployment execution.
  2.32.6. To mitigate risk, the IDP will continually consider ORM throughout the deployment
  planning and execution process, taking advantage of the expertise at their local safety offices
  and the tools and techniques contained in publications.
     2.32.6.1. The IDO, in coordination with the Wing Anti-Terrorism Officer (ATO) and
     Threat Working Group (TWG), will determine if there is an increased threat to, and the
     criticality of, mass forces staging for deployment(s). This is to ensure the IDP identifies
     any/all necessary AT capabilities and resources IAW AFI 10-245, Antiterrorism, and AFI
     31-101, Integrated Defense, as appropriate in terms of air, space and information
     operations, plans and requirements.
     2.32.6.2. Proper FP flexibility is necessary to ensure the ability to meet minimum DOD
     and AF AT Program requirements in order to properly manage higher AT program risks.
  2.32.7. Once the maximum simultaneous deployment capability is documented, preparation
  or modification of facilities can occur, personnel training will be required, acquiring
  appropriate equipment will begin, and creation or adjustments to processes will be practiced
  and codified.
  2.32.8. As a minimum, the IDP must address the following areas:
     2.32.8.1. Deployment roles and responsibilities
     2.32.8.2. Pre-execution procedures
     2.32.8.3. Deployment work-center organization and facilities
     2.32.8.4. Unit personnel and equipment assembly areas
     2.32.8.5. Cargo marshaling yards
     2.32.8.6. Installation-level passenger and cargo processing facilities/locations
     2.32.8.7. Execution procedures
     2.32.8.8. Weapons and ground safety concerns (including ORM mitigation procedures)
     2.32.8.9. Deployment training requirements
     2.32.8.10. Deployment process flowcharts
     2.32.8.11. Pre-processing procedures.
  2.32.9. The IDP must clearly define:
     2.32.9.1. Processes for individual issue and mass issue of mobility bags
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                          91


     2.32.9.2. IPE
     2.32.9.3. Weapons and ammunition
     2.32.9.4. Storage, inventory, and maintenance responsibilities for mobility bags,
     weapons, ammunition, insect vector control measures (e.g. DEET), and first aid kit
     requirements.
     2.32.9.5. (Added-USAFE) The IDP will outline the process for ensuring proper
     weapons handling and storage requirements for USAFE-AFAFRICA originating
     passengers when authorized leave in conjunction with CONUS based training prior to
     deployment.
         2.32.9.5.1. (Added-USAFE) The IDP will outline the process for ensuring proper
         weapons handling and storage requirement for transient passengers.
  2.32.10. The IDP will identify how the wing will:
     2.32.10.1. Use all components of IDS, to include a backup process when IDS is
     unavailable. These procedures will address timelines and receipt/production of personnel
     and cargo files for manifesting, ICODES files for load planning, LOGMOD and
     CMOS/GATES interfaces for ITV, and RFID tag requirements.
     2.32.10.2. Include and identify procedures associated with file transfer activities when
     the location serves as an “AGGREGATION BASE/HUB” in the AEF rotation.
     2.32.10.3. Use Tanker Airlift Control Center (TACC) designated aggregation locations
     X-MAN file procedures in lieu of requesting or expecting CMOS (*.PAX) files from
     multiple locations. Correct X-MAN file format can be found at the AMC/A4T portal
     page                                                   (https://www.my.af.mil/gcss-
     af/USAF/AFP40/d/1074111948/Files/a4t/a4ti/itvinfo/hello.html). X-MAN provides
     IDOs the greatest flexibility to collect, manage and account for inbound personnel
     arriving at their designated aggregation base.
     2.32.10.4. Use normal IDS file transfer procedures when units are deploying directly
     from home station to the AOR FOL.
  2.32.11. The IDP must:
  2.32.12. Identify how the installation, to include tenants, Institutional Forces, and associate
  units, will work within the AEF construct. It must also answer force projection related
  questions such as:
     2.32.12.1. How taskings are received.
     2.32.12.2. Who receives the tasking.
     2.32.12.3. Who is notified.
     2.32.12.4. How taskings are validated.
     2.32.12.5. Validation timelines.
     2.32.12.6. Sourcing and shortfalls
     2.32.12.7. How shortfalls are processed (Refer to Attachment 4 for typical process
     flowcharts).
 92                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


   2.32.13. The IDP will reflect mass and individual processing procedures. It will include
   interface procedures to receive, process, and deploy individuals and independent units
   departing by airlift or surface to an APOE or from the installation when designated an
   aggregate APOE.
   2.32.14. IDP minimum contents are specified in Attachment 13.
   2.32.15. The IDO, as a minimum, will revise the IDP every 4 years IAW AFI 33-360.
   2.32.16. Additionally, IDOs will revise the IDP within 6 months after any of the following:
      2.32.16.1. Activation of a new unit with a deployment commitment.
      2.32.16.2. A major change in manpower or equipment authorizations that result in
      changes to installation deployment policy or processes.
      2.32.16.3. A unit move or Mission Design System (MDS) change by a tenant or
      subordinate unit.
      2.32.16.4. Receipt of newly published deployment guidance or changes from AF/A4LX.
      2.32.16.5. A significant change to the installation’s deployment processes and/or
      procedures.
   2.32.17. The IDP must identify process and physical choke points and provide guidance on
   how to eliminate them or reduce the impact of them on deployment operations.
   2.32.18. Tenant units will deploy IAW host IDP. The host IDO determines specific support
   requirements based on tenant unit requirements, taskings and available resources.
   2.32.19. (Added-USAFE) See reference 2.2.5 and 2.2.5.1 for IDP development for:
   NATO, GSUs, and minor installations.

Section 2F—Logistics Plans Development and Management

2.33. Integrated Deployment System (IDS).
   2.33.1. Preparation for deployment includes tailoring, task organizing, and echeloning forces
   and materiel for deployment as well as documenting the sequence of deployment and
   movement requirements on the appropriate TPFDD.
   2.33.2. IDS is the AF system for task organizing, tailoring/echeloning forces and materiel,
   and sequencing movement requirements.
      2.33.2.1. The use of IDS is mandatory for all deployments.
      2.33.2.2. IDS is the automated family of systems used for wing-level deployments and
      contingency operations.
      2.33.2.3. IDS includes the following: LOGMOD, DCAPES, CMOS, GATES and
      ICODES.
   2.33.3. Deploying unit cargo information is consolidated in LOGMOD and passed via file
   transfer to CMOS/GATES by the Plans and Integration Section within the IDRC/DCC to
   provide ITV to IGC.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        93


  2.33.4. Deploying passenger information is consolidated in LOGMOD and passed via file
  transfer to DCAPES and subsequently to CMOS/GATES to provide ITV.
     2.33.4.1. EXCEPTION: Institutional Forces, Outside the AF, and extended deployments
     – formerly known as Intermediate TDY (ITDY) taskings, are received from AFPC with
     the name already in system; consolidating passenger data in LOGMOD of attached or
     supported Institutional Forces outside of the Host’s organizational structure is not
     required.
     2.33.4.2. IDS passenger manifests are not required for commercially ticketed passengers.
  2.33.5. Failure to use the full capabilities of IDS hinders an installation/wing’s ability to
  achieve timely ITV and will reduce CCDR’s visibility to track force closure.
  2.33.6. The IDO will direct Logistics Plans and Manpower offices to develop LOGMOD
  and DCAPES planning files for use in the IDS as required.
  2.33.7. The installation/wing IPR uses DCAPES to maintain the Personnel Information File
  (PIF), personnel assignments, and execution deployment requirements. IPR will provide a
  personnel refresh file (*PRF.) to the Plans and Integration Section on a weekly basis, for
  import into LOGMOD, to ensure accurate visibility of unit assigned personnel.
  2.33.8. At a minimum, the LOGMOD Administrator will develop and maintain the
  following LOGPLAN files (in LOGMOD) to support contingency and crisis action planning
  movement of UTC cargo.
     2.33.8.1. A master LOGPLAN file containing all UTCs listed as available for tasking as
     reflected in UTA.
         2.33.8.1.1. Multiple copies of the same UTC is not required.
         2.33.8.1.2. The master LOGPLAN file will consist of the standard LOGDET for
         every cargo UTC postured against the installation.
         2.33.8.1.3. UTCs will not be tailored to deviate from the standard UTC LOGDET
         established by the Pilot Unit. However, these UTCs must be modified by the
         appropriate UDMs and/or Unit Cargo Increment Monitors to identify LRS validated
         suitable substitute National Stock Numbers (NSN), actual weights and dimensional
         data (LxWxH), accurate Load Planning Data (LPD) and DD Form 1384,
         Transportation Control and Movement Document, (TCMD) are completed and unit
         commander have coordinated/approved increment movement priorities.
     2.33.8.2. A separate LOGPLAN file for each AEF rotation, OPLAN, or CONPLAN
     upon receipt of an execution tasking received and validated by the IDO/IDRC via
     DCAPES.
         2.33.8.2.1. LOGPLAN execution files will be created by copying existing cargo
         UTC information contained within the master LOGPLAN file.
         2.33.8.2.2. UTCs will be tailored by UDMs and/or Unit Cargo Increment Monitors
         based on CCDR documentation denoting pre-positioned UTC cargo for use by the
         unit upon arrival and MAJCOM FAM approval.
94                                        AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


        2.33.8.2.3. Each AEF File must be developed using an AF approved Pseudo Plan ID
        (PID). MAJCOM A4s will provide their installations with command unique Pseudo
        PIDs where there is no AF approved Pseudo PID.
     2.33.8.3. DELETED
  2.33.9. OPLAN and Pseudo PIDs.
     2.33.9.1. Units will maintain deployment planning data unique to their unit UTC tasking
     in the LOGPLAN module of LOGMOD.
     2.33.9.2. Individual LOGPLAN PIDs will be created for each tasked OPLAN with a
     maintained TPFDD, CONPLAN with TPFDD, UTC Availability, and/or notional tasking
     such as an AEF.
     2.33.9.3. Units will use only HAF approved Pseudo PIDs in LOGPLAN in lieu of actual
     OPLAN PIDs for contingency planning to minimize the risk of classifying LOGMOD.
     2.33.9.4. Units tasked under specific OPLANs will build each LOGPLAN PID using an
     approved corresponding AF-approved Pseudo PID (EXAMPLE: WOT**).
     2.33.9.5. In the Schedule module of LOGMOD, units will maintain the same
     corresponding information.
     2.33.9.6. A list of AF-approved Pseudo PIDs will be obtained from the MAJCOM
     LOGMOD Manager or downloaded from AF/A5XW SIPR Webpage.
     2.33.9.7. Specific instructions regarding the passing of data from the LOGMOD
     Schedules are identified in Attachment 8. NOTE: Use proper OPSEC procedures and
     exercise caution when associating Pseudo PIDs to real-world PIDs as it could cause a
     real-world security violation resulting in cascading affects.
     2.33.9.8. Under no circumstances will units classify their LOGMOD database by loading
     actual classified PIDs or Plan Titles in LOGMOD (LOGPLAN or LOGMOD Schedule).
     2.33.9.9. Avoid identifying the AOR or exact location, geographical location (GEOLOC)
     code, and/or International Civil Aviation Organization (ICAO) code for deployments in
     the LOGMOD Schedule ID Title or Destination Data Field of the LOGMOD Schedule
     ID Header Record. Guidance on JOPES data element classifications can be found in
     CJCSM 3122.01, Joint Operation Planning and Execution System Volume I (Planning
     Policies and Procedures) and CJCSM 3150.16b, Volume 2, Joint Planning and Execution
     System Reporting Structure (JOPESREP).
  2.33.10. The starting point for determining deploying unit equipment is the standard
  LOGDET found in LOGFOR. The LRS Plans and Integration Section will copy UTCs from
  LOGFOR into LOGPLAN to build LOGPLAN PIDs.
     2.33.10.1. On a semi-annual basis, LOGMOD Administrators will:
        2.33.10.1.1. Conduct a review of all contingency and crisis action planning UTCs (in
        LOGMOD) to ensure their UDMs have updated their respective UTCs to accurately
        reflect:
            2.33.10.1.1.1. Deployment Echelon Codes (see AFI 10-401).
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                         95


            2.33.10.1.1.2. Increment Numbers (refer to LOGFOR UTC).
            2.33.10.1.1.3. Increment Types (see LOGMOD Help).
            2.33.10.1.1.4. Functional Account Codes (FAC).
            2.33.10.1.1.5. Titles (see FM Data Quality Service, via AF Portal).
            2.33.10.1.1.6. Cargo Category Codes (CCC) (see Attachment 6).
            2.33.10.1.1.7. TCMD (see LOGMOD Help).
            2.33.10.1.1.8. LPD (see LOGMOD Help).
            2.33.10.1.1.9. NSNs (see DLA FLIS website).
        2.33.10.1.2. Will ensure all UTC increments of cargo depict a movement priority
        code IAW contingency load plans.
        2.33.10.1.3. Notify UDMs, in writing, of deficient UTC data and advised to take
        immediate corrective actions to update their UTC data within 4-duty days of
        notification.
  2.33.11. Tailoring UTC Logistics Detail in LOGPLAN.
     2.33.11.1. Tailoring is the process by which base-level units make a generic capability fit
     a specific purpose, region, supported or supporting command instruction.
     2.33.11.2. MAJCOM FAMs are the approval authority for any significant tailoring
     action such as addition or deletion of UTC personnel and/or mobility equipment that will
     otherwise impact the overall mission or movement of a UTC.
     2.33.11.3. Tailoring must either be directed by the MAJCOM FAM in writing or based
     on an approved planning document (OPLAN/CONPLAN TPFDD, AEF
     planning/execution conference, Expeditionary Site Plans (ESP), Exercise Support Plans,
     Site Surveys, etc.).
        2.33.11.3.1. Tailoring out cargo is permitted if authoritative documents reflect
        deploying/ required assets are in-place and available at the deployed location for the
        deploying units use such as pre-positioned WRM UTCs or assets identified in other
        WRM authorization documents (WCDO, ESP, and/or OPLAN TPFDDs).
        2.33.11.3.2. Tailored weights will be based on the gross incremental weight of each
        item and adjusted in the appropriate TPFDD. Units will tailor their LOGPLAN UTCs
        by adding, deleting, and modifying applicable increments, items, and suffix items.
        2.33.11.3.3. AEF lead wings in collaboration with supporting wings/units will use
        LOGMOD’s LOGPLAN Module to tailor equipment for AEF deployments.
        LOGPLAN files can be easily passed to the lead wing, the wing/units currently
        deployed, and to the various supporting wings to assist in the collaborative process to
        ensure the right capability is provided at the right time in the right way to meet the
        mission and to refine/reduce the deployment footprint.
        2.33.11.3.4. Tailoring must not change the mission capability of a UTC as described
        in the UTC MISCAP.
96                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


     2.33.11.4. Adding equipment items to LOGPLAN is prohibited unless the item has been
     added to the standard UTC by its Pilot Unit and approved by the HAF FAM and
     LOGDET Manager for that UTC or is contained in an approved Allowance Standard
     (AS) for that UTC.
        2.33.11.4.1. For CE, no equipment item can be added to a standard UTC unless it is
        identified on the Equipment and Supply List (ESL) as well as contained in applicable
        AS.
        2.33.11.4.2. Deployable equipment items added to a UTC are considered Use Code
        “A” as reflected in an AS by an Allowance Source Code (ASC).
        2.33.11.4.3. Non-equipment items may be added to LOGPLAN if they are required
        to directly support the mission specified in the MISCAP for the UTC.
     2.33.11.5. Tailoring must not cause the gross movement weight of the LOGPLAN UTC
     to exceed the standard LOGFOR UTC. USTRANSCOM and AMC currently plan airlift
     requirements based on the standard LOGFOR UTC weight and cube reported to JOPES.
     2.33.11.6. If units bulk-ship small arms weapons, small arms ammunition,
     deployment/mobility bags and expendables, then they may add these weights to the
     LOGPLAN file.
        2.33.11.6.1. Do not count the weight of these items against the UTC when comparing
        the gross transportation weight to the LOGFOR UTC.
        2.33.11.6.2. Report these differences in the respective TPFDD during crisis action
        planning when importing unit LOGPLAN/LOGMOD Schedule files into DCAPES.
     2.33.11.7. Make every effort to bulk ship mobility bags and weapons.
        2.33.11.7.1. Units will also determine if pre-deployed weapons, ammunition, and
        mobility bags that are centrally managed and distributed within certain AORs at
        Expeditionary Theater Distribution Centers (ETDC) during their tailoring efforts.
        2.33.11.7.2. Units may only tailor out these assets when the planning documents
        and/or theater directives make it clear that these assets are available for a specific unit
        or UTC’s use.
     2.33.11.8. On a semi-annual basis, LOGMOD Administrators will compare all
     LOGPLAN UTC weights (in all LOGMOD planning and execution PIDs) against the
     approved LOGFOR UTC weight to ensure unit paring and tailoring has not exceeded the
     gross movement weight of the approved LOGFOR UTC.
        2.33.11.8.1. This review will be documented, signed by the IDO, maintained in the
        LRS Plans and Integration Section, and a copy of the results provided to the
        applicable MAJCOM LOGDET Manager(s).
        2.33.11.8.2. See Attachment 8 for unit-level UTC reporting process.
     2.33.11.9. If there is a requirement to exceed standard UTC equipment weights, the
     MAJCOM A4Rs must contact the supported commander to ensure the additional weight
     is accounted for before validation occurs between supported commander and
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                           97


       USTRANSCOM. This should only occur in unique circumstances such as environmental
       requirements (i.e. additional AGE requirements) or other such factors.
       2.33.11.10. Units will maintain documentation (memo for record) on equipment that has
       been tailored (added or deleted) from their LOGPLAN UTCs for historical and
       compliance inspection purposes until UTCs have been officially changed IAW AFI 10-
       401, Chapter 5.
          2.33.11.10.1. Units will provide Logistics Planners in the LRS Plans and Integration
          Section copies of all documentation.
          2.33.11.10.2. If non-pilot units have to add items to their LOGPLAN UTC(s) in
          order to meet mission requirements, the pilot unit and MAJCOM FAM will be
          notified in case a change to the LOGDET is required for all like units.
2.34. Pre-Planned Load Plans.
   2.34.1. Preparation of pre-planned load plans is highly recommended to expedite initial
   deployment operations.
   2.34.2. Pre-planned load plans should be accomplished in ICODES using C-17s as the
   standard planning aircraft.
       2.34.2.1. (Added-USAFE) The deploying unit’s anticipated initial deployment package
       must be segmented and built to be air transportable on any potential air force transport
       aircraft. This includes C-5, C-17, C-130, KC-135 and KC-10 aircraft.
   2.34.3. Pre-planned load plans should be based on a prioritized flow of personnel and
   equipment needed to generate and provide immediate AF combat and/or support capability
   upon arrival at the deployed location.
       2.34.3.1. (Added-USAFE) Pre-load plans are required for USAFE-AFAFRICA units
       and will be maintained strictly at the prerogative of the IDO. All pre-load plans will be
       forwarded to HQ USAFE-AFAFRICA/A4RTO to include: Unit Line Numbers (ULN),
       Hazardous Diplomatic Clearance (HAZDIP), and short tons. This requirement will be
       included in Wings’ IDPs.
   2.34.4. DELETED
       2.34.4.1. DELETED
       2.34.4.2. DELETED
2.35. Cargo Prioritization.
   2.35.1. Echeloning is organizing units for movement.
       2.35.1.1. It is a pre-deployment activity that establishes a priority for movement within a
       capability (UTC), unit, or wing.
       2.35.1.2. Proper sequencing of forces into the AOR and/or JOA promotes the rapid
       buildup of capabilities that permit the supported CCDR to seize the initiative and conduct
       successful decisive operations as early as possible.
   2.35.2. Units will maintain LOGPLAN files for their tasked OPLANs/CONPLANs. The
   OPLAN/CONPLAN TPFDD priority flow must be reflected in each LOGPLAN PID.
98                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


     2.35.2.1. Units will prioritize the out-movement of equipment using both Deployment
     Echelon codes (See JCS Pub 6, Volume V, Part 4; AFI 10-401; MEFPAK; LOGMOD
     System Help files; and LOGMOD Users Guide) and the Movement Priority fields in
     LOGPLAN.
     2.35.2.2. Use Deployment Echelon codes in contingency planning and use movement
     priority fields during crisis action to reflect changing requirements at execution. These
     are mandatory entries in LOGPLAN that improve connectivity between LOGMOD and
     other IDS components.
     2.35.2.3. TCMD/ICODES data is required for LOGPLAN files.
  2.35.3. Deployment echelon codes and increment numbers identified in the LOGPLAN
  standard UTCs will not be modified without written authorization from the MAJCOM FAM
  or HHQ approval.
     2.35.3.1. Standard UTCs are developed based on the UTC MISCAP, weapon/non-
     weapon system AS, 30-day sustainment, re-supply at 31+ days and a bare-base (austere)
     environment.
     2.35.3.2. Cargo movement prioritization will reflect the minimum equipment needed to
     regenerate/weapons load aircraft (for aviation UTCs) and/or establish base operations
     (i.e. FP, rapid runway repair, communications, lodging/food preparations, etc.) to be
     deployed on the first available support airlift to Forward Operating Locations (FOL).
     2.35.3.3. Pilot units prioritize the out-movement of equipment using deployment
     echelons and increment numbers. Refer to AFI 10-401 for additional information on
     UTC development.
     2.35.3.4. If non-pilot units have differing opinions as to what equipment will be
     deployed first, second, and third, they are required to identify their prioritization
     requirements using the movement priority field for each increment of cargo within the
     LOGPLAN Module of LOGMOD.
  2.35.4. For contingency and crisis action planning, units will use the LOGPLAN movement
  priority field to identify when UTCs and/or increments within a UTC will deploy.
  Movement priority is based on TPFDD C-day requirements, DOC statement response times,
  or HHQ guidance. In LOGMOD, the movement priority field defaults to a zero. Zero is not
  an acceptable value to use when prioritizing movement priorities for UTCs or increments
  within a UTC.
  2.35.5. Two of the most efficient ways of utilizing the movement priority field in LOGMOD
  are “by UTC” or “within a UTC.”
     2.35.5.1. Prioritizing “by UTC” means organizing flow of capabilities by ULN based on
     TPFDD movement dates such as available to load date (ALD), ready to load date (RLD),
     or required delivery date (RDD). This is done by using the movement priority field to
     indicate the date an action is scheduled to occur within the TPFDD.
     2.35.5.2. Prioritizing “within a UTC” means units will prioritize each increment within a
     UTC using the movement priority field to identify the sequence increments should be
     deployed in.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                          99


          2.35.5.2.1. DELETED
          2.35.5.2.2. DELETED
2.36. AF 463L Pallets/Containers.
   2.36.1. AF 463L pallets are the mandatory cargo-packing platform for the AF standard
   LOGDET because they are the most versatile for aircraft load planning.
      2.36.1.1. Internal Airlift/Helicopter Slingable-Container Unit (ISUs) will not be used in
      any portion of a Pilot Unit report or AF standard UTC IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 5.
      However, pallets with container attached/palletized container or ISU can be used as a
      suitable substitute for 463L pallets in unit LOGPLAN development, providing the UTC
      will not exceed the weight of the approved standard UTC.
      2.36.1.2. Pallets with container attached or palletized containers (i.e. ISUs) must be
      purchased at unit expense.
   2.36.2. Not all types of ISUs will fit on all types of military or commercial aircraft. Units
   will ensure that purchased ISUs will fit on all AMC/commercial type aircraft, including MD-
   11s, DC-8s, KC-10s, KC-46s and KC-135s.
   2.36.3. Units designed to move on their own organic airlift may plan their types of ISU
   purchase/use on that, but it does not relieve them of the requirement to maintain 463L pallets
   and nets in sufficient numbers to meet the determined requirement.
   2.36.4. DELETED
      2.36.4.1. DELETED
      2.36.4.2. Units must maintain and account for pallets and nets used for standard UTC
      requirements.
      2.36.4.3. The IDO must consolidate installation deployment pallet and net requirements
      and forward to the WPNM.
      2.36.4.4. IDOs and units must consider their maximum simultaneous deployment
      capability when determining their operational pallets and nets requirement and will
      identify any shortages or excesses to the WPNM so that assets can be redistributed, as
      required.
      2.36.4.5. (Added-USAFE) The Wing Installation Pallet and Net Manager (WPNM) will
      work in conjunction with the IDRC to develop Wing pallet and net requirements. It is the
      responsibility of the UDM to compute unit requirements. The IDO may compute and
      compile the pallet and net numbers for each unit and present the requirements to the
      WPNM in a format agreed upon locally. The WPNM will be responsible for submitting
      compiled numbers to the MAJCOM pallet and net manager.
   2.36.5. Organization/unit Pallet and Net Managers will monitor, inspect, and report
   operational pallet and net assets IAW DTR 4500.9-R, Part VI, Management and Control of
   Intermodal Containers and System 463L Equipment.
      2.36.5.1. DELETED
      2.36.5.2. DELETED
100                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      2.36.5.3. If containers or palletized containers are used, units must be able to meet airlift
      constraints and must not exceed the weight and cube of the standard UTC LOGDET.
      Units with a minimum amount of equipment should continue to use 463L pallets.
  2.36.6. LOGMOD automatically assigns standard planning information (weights,
  dimensional data, and quantities) to items 01, 02, and 03 when pilot/non-pilot units develop
  pallet increment types.
      2.36.6.1. The overall dimensions of a 463L pallet are 88 inches by 108 inches, by 2 1/4
      inches thick. However, the usable dimensions of the upper surface are 84 inches by 104
      inches. This allows for two inches around the periphery to attach straps, nets, or other
      restraint devices. An empty 463L pallet weighs 290 pounds (355 pounds with nets) and
      has a maximum, netted load capacity of 10,000 pounds.
      2.36.6.2. The desired load capacity is 7,500 pounds (to help prolong pallet life).
      2.36.6.3. ISUs, Cadillac Bins, Brooks & Perkins containers, and married pallets/pallet
      trains are not considered LOGMOD Pallet Type Increments and will not be loaded as
      such in the LOGFOR module of LOGMOD.
  2.36.7. Pilot/non-pilot units will load pallet dunnage as Item 04 for all pallet increments
  using the following movement characteristics: Length 88, Width 4, Height 4, Weight 30
  pounds, with a quantity of three. Pilot/non-pilot units will use the appropriate NSNs for
  dunnage obtained through the LRS Materiel Management Flight Customer Service.
      2.36.7.1. Dunnage (e.g. lumber or timber) is placed under 463L pallets to prevent
      damage to the lower pallet surface and to aid in transportation with a forklift.
      2.36.7.2. The minimum dimensions of a piece of dunnage are 3x3x88 inches long. Use
      three pieces to support each loaded 463L pallet while on the ground. Many different
      materials can be used as dunnage.
      2.36.7.3. All 463L pallets will be shipped with dunnage. This is both required for
      deployment and redeployment and must be provided by the user (see T.O. 35D33-2-2-2
      and T.O. 35D33-2-3-1).
      2.36.7.4. Wood Packaging Material (WPM) to include dunnage departing or returning to
      the United States must be stamped or marked with an approved International Standards
      for Phytosanitary Measures 15 or DOD Pest Free Certification Stamp by trained and
      certified DOD personnel IAW AFI 24-203.
  2.36.8. Pilot units will ensure ISUs, Cadillac Bins, or Brooks & Perkins containers are not
  loaded in lieu of, or as a substitute for 463L pallets and nets within standard AF LOGDETs.
      2.36.8.1. Possession of ISUs does not relieve a unit of their responsibility/requirement to
      maintain 463L pallets and nets in sufficient numbers to meet the determined requirement.
      2.36.8.2. EXCEPTION: IAW AFI 25-101, BEAR Order of Battle (BOB) UTCs are
      exempt from this guidance because BEAR must be shipped in Internal Slingable Unit
      (ISU) containers (air shipping configuration) and intermodal containers (surface shipping
      configuration).
      2.36.8.3. MEFPAK Responsible Agency LOGDET Managers will identify all
      LOGDETs that contain ISUs to the pilot unit for immediate corrective action.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        101


   2.36.9. Pilot units will ensure the palletized increments within the standard UTC LOGDET
   do not exceed 10,000 pounds. Non-pilot units will ensure palletized increments within the
   LOGPLAN Module of LOGMOD do not exceed 10,000 pounds.
   2.36.10. Pilot units will physically build, weigh, and measure each increment of cargo when
   developing and maintaining standard UTC LOGDETs IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 5.
2.37. Manpower and Personnel Data.
   2.37.1. The MO (IPR for ARC units) will use DCAPES base-unique PIDs as identified by
   MAJCOM DCAPES Sub-FMs to build all UTC requirements available for taskings found in
   the MAJCOM provided UTA listing. This information will be provided to the IDO, UDM,
   and MPF at least on a quarterly basis or when a specific plan is updated (information will be
   available in DCAPES for IDOs and UDMs).
   2.37.2. OPLAN manpower (personnel) taskings are provided by the MAJCOM,
   disseminated by the IDO, and maintained separately by the installation MO (IPR for ARC).
      2.37.2.1. Recommended changes to these requirements will be coordinated through the
      IDO, UDM and MPS.
      2.37.2.2. Tailoring of personnel requirements must follow AFI 10-401, Chapter 10
      guidance.
   2.37.3. MO uses DCAPES to link MANFOR details and the UTA in order to pass the tasked
   UTC to the wings/units.
   2.37.4. At least annually, MO will coordinate with the IDO, and in some cases will conduct,
   a UMD to UTC tasking validation to determine if MAJCOM FAM taskings exceed wing/unit
   UMD.
   2.37.5. At least annually, MO, in coordination with the LRS Plans and Integration Section
   and all affected units, validates UTC(s), AFSC(s), Functional Account Code(s) (FAC), and
   Personnel Accounting Symbol (PAS) codes with tasked unit(s) and will coordinate corrective
   action(s) required with the unit and/or designated UTC Pilot Units.
   2.37.6. MO will receive the deployment echelon and movement priority sequence
   (deployment sequence) from the Plans and Integration Section/IDO to build the contingency
   DCAPES plans data if TPFDDs are available.
      2.37.6.1. If TPFDDs are not available, the Plans and Integration Section will provide
      PID(s), UTC(s), ULN(s), RDD(s), deployment echelon(s) and deployment sequence
      number(s).
      2.37.6.2. At the discretion of the IDO, MO will coordinate with tasked units’ UDMs to
      validate remaining DCAPES data elements and will coordinate any/all required changes
      as needed through designated UTC Pilot Units.
   2.37.7. The UDMs will:
      2.37.7.1. Validate DCAPES UTC data to ensure tasked AFSCs are assigned against the
      correct PAS and FAC codes, and will coordinate movement priority requirements
      through the LRS Plans and Integration Section/IDO as needed.
 102                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


       2.37.7.2. Ensure their unit taskings do not exceed their UMD and will coordinate
       corrective action through the MO for resolution.
   2.37.8. ANG and AFRC units are not authorized a MO; therefore, the IPR performs these
   responsibilities. NOTE: These procedures are documented in AFI 36-3802 and AFI 38-205.

Section 2G—Deployment Organizational Structure.

2.38. Deployment Organizational Structure.
   2.38.1. The IDO will:
       2.38.1.1. Define an effective and efficient organizational structure to meet all command
       and control, cargo, and personnel processing requirements for the installation’s maximum
       simultaneous deployment capability.
       2.38.1.2. Establish a DCC to serve as the installation’s focal point for deployment C2
       requirements beyond the normal IDRC capabilities.
       2.38.1.3. Ensure the IDRC is subsumed into the DCC, PDF and CDF as appropriate.
       2.38.1.4. Identify requirements for the DCC, PDF and CDFs to appropriate base agencies
       for staffing and infrastructure support.
       2.38.1.5. Be responsible for standing up the DCC, CDF, PDF, and UDCCs (in
       coordination with owning unit commanders) to meet the requirements of a given
       deployment scenario.
       2.38.1.6. To meet AEF rotation requirements, establish procedures for interfacing with
       the LRS Traffic Management functions responsible for booking passengers commercially
       will also be established. While the IDO may or may not choose to stand up the
       deployment work centers, he or she will ensure the functions of those work centers are
       accomplished for every deployment regardless of the number of personnel or short tons
       deploying. The IDO will accomplish these actions IAW the IDP.
   2.38.2. Deployment Control Center (DCC).
       2.38.2.1. The DCC is the installation/wing focal point for all deployment C2 operations,
       including identifying, verifying and distributing tasking information before, during and
       after execution.
       2.38.2.2. The IDO, through the LRS/Plans and integration Section, will review and
       monitor applicable classified newsgroups, DCAPES PIDs and the AF Tasking
       Notification Tool (TNT) - formerly AF Verification Process within DCAPES to verify
       receipt, acceptance, and shortfalling of taskings.
       2.38.2.3. MAJCOMs will identify which PIDs their wings are responsible for
       monitoring.
       2.38.2.4. The DCC will initiate unit cargo and personnel shortfall procedures IAW AFI
       10-401, this instruction, the AFPC/DPW RPT User manual, supported MAJCOM, and
       the installation/Wing IDP.
          2.38.2.4.1. For AFRC units located on bases where the host is different than their
          gaining MAJCOM, personnel and/or equipment LIMFAC/shortfalls must be
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                       103


        submitted through appropriate personnel channels that will identify these
        requirements to that unit’s gaining MAJCOM.
        2.38.2.4.2. For associate units, tenants and/or Institutional Forces, shortfalls and/or
        shortfall mitigation utilizing associate units must be coordinated through applicable
        components or MAJCOM A4L/A4Rs.
     2.38.2.5. RPT automates the reclama process with a web-based application that allows
     multi-user inputs, automated validation and immediate visibility of shortfall conditions.
        2.38.2.5.1. Shortfalls for requirements sourced by AFPC/DPW are transmitted into
        RPT.
        2.38.2.5.2. It serves to communicate to senior leadership a unit’s inability to meet a
        CCDR operational requirement.
        2.38.2.5.3. New users will contact AFPC/DPW to obtain a RPT account.
     2.38.2.6. The IDO will stand-up the DCC when deployment requirements cannot be
     executed by the IDRC. NOTE: Many factors are weighed in this determination, such as,
     timing, number of UTCs, personnel and equipment tasked, support airlift, etc.
     2.38.2.7. The DCC is responsible for coordinating all transportation actions required to
     deploy the force, coordinating/staffing equipment and personnel shortfalls, controlling
     the overall integration of the PDF, CDF and UDCCs, informing the wing’s CAT of
     process bottlenecks and effectiveness, and coordinating with HHQ, USTRANSCOM, and
     C-NAFs for support when required.
     2.38.2.8. The DCC is responsible for contacting TACC and providing them with the
     required information for all contingency movements involving the movement of
     hazardous UTC cargo, via military or military contracted aircraft, for an approved and
     validated TPFDD requirement. Installations tasked to deploy hazardous UTC cargo (by
     strategic airlift) will complete the following:
        2.38.2.8.1. Develop preliminary load plans, denoting the type of airlift being
        requested, and identify how the hazardous cargo will be positioned on the aircraft.
        2.38.2.8.2. Tasked units will complete a Hazardous Cargo Aircraft Clearance
        Request Worksheet that denotes all hazardous material information being deployed
        for DCC coordination with TACC.
        2.38.2.8.3. Submit primary load plan(s) and applicable Hazardous Cargo Aircraft
        Request     worksheet(s)    to    TACC       (Diplomatic      Clearance      Branch),
        tacc.tadip@scott.af.mil, within 48-hours of notification to deploy in order to ensure
        the adequacy of proposed aircraft and mission plans prior to the movement of
        hazardous cargo from home station.
            2.38.2.8.3.1. Installation/wings will follow the same requirements for real-world
            contingency movements during DEPLOYEX at home stations.
            2.38.2.8.3.2. EXCEPTION: Submission of these documents will be provided to
            the wing inspection team vice TACC, within 48-hours of notification to deploy in
            order to ensure adequacy of proposed aircraft and mission plans.
104                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      2.38.2.9. DCC Manning.
         2.38.2.9.1. DCC functions include the IDO, Logistics Plans, Personnel, Distribution
         Representative, LOGMOD Schedule monitors, Materiel Management, Admin, and
         selected unit representatives.
         2.38.2.9.2. Training for each of the work centers will include a thorough knowledge
         of this instruction, the local IDP, and functional expertise in their respective
         AFSC/function.
         2.38.2.9.3. All DCC personnel require a SECRET clearance.
      2.38.2.10. DCC Requirements.
         2.38.2.10.1. Robust communications in the DCC are essential for positive control.
         Minimum IDS communications requirements include:
             2.38.2.10.1.1. Access to SIPRNET.
             2.38.2.10.1.2. Non-secure Internet Protocol Router Network (NIPRNET).
             2.38.2.10.1.3. Secure and unsecured telephones.
             2.38.2.10.1.4. Access to unsecured facsimile (fax) machines.
         2.38.2.10.2. DCC personnel require an adequate number of SIPRNET terminals to
         access JOPES, DCAPES, BaS&E, LOGFAC, LOGMOD, classified newsgroups,
         secure web sites, collaborative decision support tools, and other planning aids.
         2.38.2.10.3. DCC key staff should be provided with land mobile radios (LMR) and
         cell telephones, when available.
         2.38.2.10.4. Additional requirements include uninterrupted power and classified
         storage.
         2.38.2.10.5. Video surveillance of marshaling yards and aircraft loading operation
         areas is optional, but desired if direct line of sight of these areas is not available from
         the DCC.
         2.38.2.10.6. LOGMOD requires, as a minimum, T-1 LAN connectivity to all UDM
         facilities and a wide area network.
  2.38.3. Cargo Deployment Function (CDF).
      2.38.3.1. The CDF is responsible for all actions necessary to receive, in-check, inspect,
      marshal, load plan, manifest, and supervising loading cargo aboard deploying aircraft or
      vehicles (see Attachment 4 for cargo processing flowcharts) - the LRS Deployment &
      Distribution Flight Commander is integral to the effectiveness of the CDF process.
      2.38.3.2. The host LRS, or APS/AMS is responsible for providing CDF training, which
      will include this instruction, local deployment management documents and, more
      importantly, functional expertise in their CDF duties.
      2.38.3.3. Final Load Planner.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                       105


        2.38.3.3.1. Complete final load plans to ensure maximum utilization of aircraft
        Allowable Cabin Load (ACL), ease of cargo on/offload, and safety of flight
        standards.
        2.38.3.3.2. Load planner augmentees will be trained IAW with AFI 10-403,
        Attachment 5.
        2.38.3.3.3. Final load plans are required to be certified and validated by a
        certified/qualified load planner or loadmaster/boom operator.
     2.38.3.4. Quality Control (QC).
        2.38.3.4.1. Ensures all documentation is correct, adequate, posted, protected, and
        processed properly and that equipment/materiel is properly configured for transport.
        2.38.3.4.2. Documentation includes cargo and passenger manifests, load plans,
        hazardous material inspection, and special handling documentation.
     2.38.3.5. Controllers.
        2.38.3.5.1. Manage status of cargo.     Update completion times in the LOGMOD
        Schedule.
        2.38.3.5.2. Identify potential bottlenecks and work with CDF personnel, units, and
        DCC to ensure cargo is processed on time.
     2.38.3.6. Cargo In-Check. Responsible for verifying that equipment has been received
     for processing, ensure it is properly marked and packaged, and meets safety and in-transit
     visibility requirements for transport.
     2.38.3.7. Cargo Joint Inspection (JI).
        2.38.3.7.1. Inspect equipment/cargo with the owning unit representative(s) and/or
        cargo terminal representative(s) (or loadmaster, if necessary) before the load is
        accepted.
        2.38.3.7.2. JI duties should be limited to 1A2 (Aircraft Loadmaster), 2T0 (Traffic
        Management) and 2T2 (Air Transportation) career fields.
        2.38.3.7.3. Joint Inspectors must complete AMC approved JI training IAW AMCI
        24-101, V22 Attachment 4.
     2.38.3.8. Cargo Marshaling. Responsible for the placement of cargo in load plan
     sequence by chalk, normally according to chalk departure times, in preparation for JI.
     2.38.3.9. Cargo Manifesting and Documentation.
        2.38.3.9.1. Responsible for verifying cargo documentation is correct and for passing
        information to load planners.
        2.38.3.9.2. Accurate data in CMOS/GATES, along with correct documentation IAW
        the DTR and AFI 24-203, are critical to ensure proper ITV.
        2.38.3.9.3. Produces updated and accurate DD Form 1387s, Military Shipping Label
        (MSL), or CMOS/GATES-generated shipping placards to attach to cargo prior to
        aircraft loading.
106                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


         2.38.3.9.4. Equipment that is required in support of flight line operations and have
         permanently installed metal deployment placards will still require a CMOS/GATES
         deployment placard.
         2.38.3.9.5. Permanently installed metal deployment placards are not acceptable, as
         they do not comply with DTR guidance.
         2.38.3.9.6. Ensures in-transit visibility through the creation, updating, and affixing to
         cargo of RFID tags IAW AFI 24-203 and the IDP.
      2.38.3.10. Wing personnel will be designated and trained to transport, load, and secure
      cargo on aircraft or other vehicles for deployment.
         2.38.3.10.1. DELETED
         2.38.3.10.2. DELETED
      2.38.3.11. Ramp Coordinator (RAMPCO).
         2.38.3.11.1. Ensures effective coordination of all aircraft and vehicle loading
         operations for the CDF OIC/NCOIC and IDO.
         2.38.3.11.2. Passes aircraft commander package to aircraft commander/loadmaster
         and briefs them on special cargo handling requirements.
      2.38.3.12. If the IDO determines full CDF augmentation/stand-up is not required, the
      LRS Deployment & Distribution Flight will ensure all required CDF responsibilities are
      fulfilled as applicable (dependent on mode/source of transportation). NOTE: For AMC
      bases with an APS, the CDF is the responsibility of the APS.
      2.38.3.13. CDF Requirements.
         2.38.3.13.1. As a minimum, the CDF should have: suitable MHE (K-loaders,
         forklifts, tow vehicles, etc.), fixed or portable scales, RFID tags and required support
         equipment (when available), portable lighting, marking equipment for classified and
         hazardous equipment holding areas, uninterrupted power (generator), robust
         communications (including telephones and LMRs, as required) and the correct ADP
         Equipment (ADPE) to include access to SIPRNET terminals for classified e-mail
         capability.
         2.38.3.13.2. Minimum T-1 LAN connectivity is required to support applicable
         components of IDS.
  2.38.4. Personnel Deployment Function (PDF).
      2.38.4.1. DELETED
      2.38.4.2. Is a multi-functional entity consisting of representatives from distribution, force
      support, chaplain, medical, legal, finance, etc. organized as a processing activity designed
      to ensure deploying personnel are properly accounted for and prepared for deployment?
      2.38.4.3. Serves as the installation’s focal point for monitoring all personnel processing
      activities to include eligibility screening, pre-deployment briefings, orders preparation
      and production, passenger manifesting, passenger baggage handling, and passenger
      loading.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        107


     2.38.4.4. PDF Responsibilities.
        2.38.4.4.1. Advises commanders when personnel selected for deployment are
        ineligible to deploy according to this instruction; AFI 10-401; AFI 36-2110,
        Assignments; AFI 36-3802 and the reporting instructions/processing guidance issued
        by the Supported Command. Although the ultimate responsibility for deployment
        eligibility rests with the unit commander, the PDF serves as the wing’s last set of eyes
        ensuring all personnel are eligible for deployment, waivered for deployment
        according to the governing guidance, or replaced when found ineligible. The PDF:
        2.38.4.4.2. Ensures personnel (military and civilian) have appropriate CAC, passport,
        and visas, if required.
        2.38.4.4.3. Ensures personnel selected for deployment have enough retainability to
        complete the established TDY tour length according to AFI 10-401, AFI 36-2110 and
        AFI 36-3802.
        2.38.4.4.4. Maintains accountability of deploying personnel from the time they arrive
        at the PDF processing line until they leave home station.
        2.38.4.4.5. When directed by the IDO, provides services (by exception only) for
        emergency data documentation (vRED/DD Form 93), ID card, Geneva Convention
        card, immunizations and ID (Dog) Tag updates. NOTE: PDF line will be used only
        as a last resort in providing these items prior to the member deploying from home
        station.
        2.38.4.4.6. In coordination with Anti-Terrorism/Force Protection (AT/FP), Counter
        Intelligence Awareness Reporting (CIAR), and Foreign Clearance Guidance (FCG)
        program OPRs:
            2.38.4.4.6.1. Ensure deploying members are briefed on FCG requirements, DoD
            Travel Security Advisories, and country threats IAW AFI 16-606, Foreign
            Clearance Program.
            2.38.4.4.6.2. Ensure completion of the Anti-Terrorism/Force Protection (AT/FP)
            awareness training and any other training requirements identified in the Supported
            Command reporting instructions/processing guidance or DRMD line remark IAW
            DODI 2000.16, DOD Antiterrorism (AT) Standards, DODD 5240.06, Counter
            Intelligence Awareness and Reporting (CIAR), AFI 10-245, Anti-Terrorism (AT),
            AFI 71-101V4, Counterintelligence, and other applicable guidance.
        2.38.4.4.7. At execution, coordinates unit personnel replacement actions with the
        DCC and UDMs, to include, monitoring personnel shortfalls with the DCC to ensure
        100% accountability of UTC personnel taskings.
        2.38.4.4.8. Uses DCAPES to produce CED orders according to this instruction, AFI
        36-3802, Supported Command reporting instructions/processing guidance, and any
        applicable DRMD line remarks. Produces CED orders for all deployments in support
        of real-world contingencies, exercises, deployments, and unit moves involving
        deployment of personnel.
        2.38.4.4.9. Provides updates for LOGMOD or changes to requirement information as
        they occur. Processes LOGMOD personnel assignment data into DCAPES for
108                                        AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      issuing orders. Provides the Transportation representative a CMOS file for electronic
      manifesting once all processing of the chalk is complete.
      2.38.4.4.10. Selects and appoints a Troop Leader for each deploying chalk. Briefs
      Troop Leader on his/her responsibilities for accounting for the troops until they are
      received by the Personnel Processing facility in the AOR.
      2.38.4.4.11. Prepares a Personnel Accountability Kit (PAK) for the deploying troop
      leader according to AFI 36-3802 and supported component command reporting
      instruction/processing guidance.
      2.38.4.4.12. Instructs all deploying personnel to report to the deployed Personnel
      Processing facility (normally led by a PERSCO team) for in-processing and deployed
      accountability.
      2.38.4.4.13. Works with the IPR ensuring all deployed personnel’s duty status is
      updated reflecting their deployment and departure from home station.
      2.38.4.4.14. The IDO, in coordination with the FSS OPSO:
         2.38.4.4.14.1. Establishes a PDF IAW this AFI and AFI 36-3802.
         2.38.4.4.14.2. Establishes a formal PDF processing line provides the most
         effective means to check personnel eligibility and readiness.
         2.38.4.4.14.3. However, special circumstances (such as resource availability, etc.)
         might not warrant standing up a full processing line. If the IDO deems a full
         stand-alone PDF processing line is not required, every effort will be made to
         incorporate some functions of the line in the processing.
      2.38.4.4.15. When the full services of a PDF line are not available, deploying
      personnel must be provided a deployment checklist that ensures they receive the same
      processing and services afforded in a formal PDF line.
         2.38.4.4.15.1. Once established, the PDF will fully staff the Identification and
         Medical Stations to determine deployment eligibility.
         2.38.4.4.15.2. Have the manpower and resources necessary to conduct continuous
         personnel processing 24-hours a day.
      2.38.4.4.16. Furthermore, depending on the timeliness and scope of the deployment,
      the PDF will establish the following processing stations (see Attachment 3,
      Deployment Checklists, for detailed processing station information):
         2.38.4.4.16.1. Emergency Data Station. For changes to emergency data, vRED
         (information is updated via vMPF; however, PDF reps can pull an updated copy
         from MPS), and to Servicemen’s Group Life Insurance (SGLI).
         2.38.4.4.16.2. Identification Station: ID Tags & military/civilian ID/CAC cards,
         Geneva Convention cards, Isolated Personnel Report (ISOPREP) Card - DD Form
         1833, (if necessary), passports & visas, etc.
         2.38.4.4.16.3. Finance Station.
         2.38.4.4.16.4. Legal Station.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                      109


            2.38.4.4.16.5. Chaplain Corps Station.
            2.38.4.4.16.6. Airman and Family Readiness Station.
            2.38.4.4.16.7. Force Support (ground support meals) Station.
     2.38.4.5. PDF Requirements. As a minimum, the PDF requires: uninterrupted power
     (generator), robust communications (telephones and LMRs, as required), correct ADPE
     and unclassified and classified LAN connectivity to support applicable components of
     IDS, DCAPES, GCCS and secure web sites; classified storage, adequate briefing and
     passenger holding facilities, and adequate baggage handling facilities.
  2.38.5. Air Passenger Terminal.
     2.38.5.1. When processing passengers for airlift from home station or when designated
     as an aggregation APOE, the PDF will also establish the Air Passenger Terminal (APT)
     to:
         2.38.5.1.1. Manifest passengers.
         2.38.5.1.2. Build baggage pallets and coordinate belly loads

         Aviation Administration (FAA), Transportation Security Administration (TSA), and
         DTR requirements.
     2.38.5.2. The FSS is in charge of the processing line within PDF operations and, as
     applicable, will coordinate with LRS Transportation Functions for training and personnel
     expertise to manage, integrate, and/or execute APT operations.
     2.38.5.3. The following materials must be available at the APT during operations:
         2.38.5.3.1. AFI 10-403, with all supplements and IDP.
         2.38.5.3.2. DTR 4500.9-R, Part III, Appendices T and BB.
         2.38.5.3.3. CMOS/GATES systems.
         2.38.5.3.4. Portable pallet scales (1 set).2.40.5.6.5. 10K forklift(s), 463L pallets,
         plastic covers, nets and straps to conduct baggage build-up.
         2.38.5.3.5. Baggage Handling Station. A baggage handling station is manned with
         an adequate amount of personnel in order to take possession, palletize and/or loosely
         handle personnel deployment bags.
         2.38.5.3.6. American Red Cross Station.
         2.38.5.3.7. Amnesty Box Station.
  2.38.6. Unit Deployment Control Center (UDCC) Responsibilities.
     2.38.6.1. The UDCC is responsible for coordinating all unit level deployment activities
     to include receipt of taskings and preparation of cargo and personnel for deployment.
     2.38.6.2. Once activated on direction of the IDO, the UDCC will not deactivate without
     prior coordination with the IDO and the DCC.

       2.38.6.3. UDCC staff will include at least two trained and qualified UDMs, and must be
       able to successfully perform 24-hour operations when required.
       2.38.6.4. Recommended UDCC Infrastructure Requirements.
          2.38.6.4.1. Uninterrupted power (generator).
          2.38.6.4.2. Robust communications (telephones and LMRs, as required).
          2.38.6.4.3. Correct ADPE and Local Area Network (LAN) connectivity to support
          applicable components of IDS.
          2.38.6.4.4. Access to facsimile machine.
          2.38.6.4.5. Access to Secure Telephone Unit-Third Generation (STU III) and/or
          equivalent
          2.38.6.4.6. Classified storage capability. SIPRNET is desirable for channeling
          secure information between HHQs, FAMs, and installation/wing-level agencies.

Section 2H—Deployment Training and Education.

2.39. Deployment Training and Education.
   2.39.1. The IDO has overall responsibility to establish local deployment training and
   education program to ensure all deployment workcenter personnel fully understand the
   process, are properly trained to function as work center augmentees, and are aware of proper
   procedures for preparing unit personnel and equipment for deployment.
       2.39.1.1. (Added-USAFE) The IDO will document the required training as identified in
       paragraphs 2.38.2.9.2, 2.38.3.2., 2.39., Attachment 5, and local IDPs.
   2.39.2. Deployment Education and Training Requirements. The deployment training and
   education program must address the following areas (see Attachment 5 for training classes
   and timeline requirements):
   2.39.3. IDO will provide initial training to the Installation/Wing Commander and all newly
   assigned host and tenant commanders, within 90 days of their assignment. At a minimum,
   training will include:
       2.39.3.1. IDO roles and responsibilities.
       2.39.3.2. IDO lines of authority and chain of command.
       2.39.3.3. IDRC roles and responsibilities/impact on commander’s unit.
       2.39.3.4. Unit status information.
       2.39.3.5. Unit UTC posturing review (via UTA).
       2.39.3.6. Unit commander and UDM expectations.
       2.39.3.7. Baseline training on ART
       2.39.3.8. UTA/UTC posturing.
       2.39.3.9. Tempo banding.

     2.39.3.10. AEF.
     2.39.3.11. Institutional Forces.
     2.39.3.12. AEF debriefs.
     2.39.3.13. Deployment discrepancies.
     2.39.3.14. Shortfall/reclama procedures.
     2.39.3.15. Name in System (NIS) timelines.
     2.39.3.16. Waiver requirements and procedures.
     2.39.3.17. LOGMOD requirements and procedures.
     2.39.3.18. Deployment exercise requirements.
  2.39.4. Training attendance and content will be documented in writing and maintained by
  the IDO.
  2.39.5. Establish formal training for UDMs, work center augmentees, unit personnel with
  responsibility for handling cargo, to ensure members understand the procedures for personnel
  and cargo preparation and the overall deployment process.
  2.39.6. Establish a formal training program for use of IDS.
     2.39.6.1. Use IDS, CBT, and other applicable materials to support the wing/unit initial
     and recurring training programs.
     2.39.6.2. Accomplish and document IDS training by using scenario-based, hands-on
     desktop exercises led by the IDO and Plans and Integration Section for UDMs, Logistic
     Readiness (Traffic Management, Air Transportation) representatives, Manpower
     representatives, and Personnel representatives once each AEF schedule at a minimum.
     2.39.6.3. MAJCOM A4s will determine if local OREs/CUI Phase I & 2 or RIs qualify as
     hands-on training. If approved, it will be documented in the installation/wing IDP.
     2.39.6.4. IDS training classes are conducted as a shared responsibility of the IDO, Wing
     LOGMOD Administrator, and CMOS/GATES operators (Refer to AFI 24-203).
     2.39.6.5. Classes will be provided to all tenant units and host-wing supported GSUs.
  2.39.7. Establish formal training for deployment work center supervisors and augmentees to
  ensure personnel understand the deployment process and their work center responsibilities.
  2.39.8. A 2-month pre-deployment preparation period to focus unit activities on AOR-
  specific events required (if known) and/or training exercises such as Red Flag and Silver
  Flag. ECS units will be prepared to validate readiness via deployment to Eagle Flag during
  that 2-month pre-deployment preparation period. Do not wait until this period to accomplish
  warrior skills or other normal deployment training requirements, as listed in Chapter 1.
  2.39.9. Ensure specialized training normally associated with the deployment process are
  identified, documented, and addressed in training.
  2.39.10. The IDO, in conjunction with other essential agencies, should provide quarterly
  deployment training statistics to the host Installation/Wing Commander. At a minimum, the
  update will include:

      2.39.10.1. Total number of deployment work center training classes that were conducted
      (see Attachment 5) during the past quarter.
      2.39.10.2. Number of work center personnel (and augmentees) trained.
      2.39.10.3. Number of no-shows (by organization), thereby denoting the overall readiness
      of the installation’s deployment Augmentation Duty program.
      2.39.10.4. Training attendance and content, for classes taught, will be documented in
      writing and maintained by the IDO.
      2.39.10.5. (Added-USAFE) The quarterly deployment training status will also report all

      training information may be reported to the Wing Commander through functional
      channels (i.e. Security Forces reporting small arms training) as required by functional Air
      Force Instructions. The IDO, in conjunction with other agencies, will attempt to
      consolidate as many training events into the deployment training report as feasible.

                                          Chapter 3

                               DEPLOYMENT EXECUTION

Section 3A—Deployment Planning Overview

3.1. General.
   3.1.1. This chapter will provide general background information related to deployment
   planning processes, TPFDD sourcing (crisis action/rotational AEF), receipt/verification of
   deployment taskings, execution of IDP processes/procedures, deployment reporting, and post
   deployment documentation.
   3.1.2. AFI 10-401 is the primary AF source document and provides detailed guidance for AF
   operations planning and execution to include deployment planning and execution processes
   and procedures. NOTE: AFI 10-401 guidance references will be annotated in parenthesis at
   the end of each paragraph when applicable.
3.2. Deployment Planning Processes.
   3.2.1. Deployment planning is a continuous, iterative, and highly structured process that
   allows for an orderly transition from peace to war and post-hostilities operations.
   3.2.2. Deployment planning ensures the systematic deployment, employment, sustainment,
   and redeployment of U.S. Forces to meet commander requirements across the Range of
   Military Options (ROMO).
   3.2.3. The Joint Planning and Execution Community (JPEC) uses two general planning
   processes: crisis action and deliberate planning. (AFI 10-401, Chapter 3.)
       3.2.3.1. Crisis action planning is driven by current events in real time and normally
       occurs in emergencies and in the context of time-sensitive situations.
       3.2.3.2. Deliberate planning is accomplished in the absence of an active crisis in
       response to scenarios and threats identified by combatant commanders and in national
       guidance such as the JSCP.
   3.2.4. Currently, crisis action and deliberate planning use different pre-deployment planning
   cycles however the execution processes and ADP used to support deployment operations are
   generally the same.
   3.2.5. The major difference during crisis action and rotational (AEF) deployment execution
   is timing. Deployment operations/execution in support of:
       3.2.5.1. Crisis action operations are initiated by SecDef/CJCS Warning, Planning, Alert,
       Deployment, Prepare to Deploy, and/or Execution Orders.
       3.2.5.2. Rotational (AEF) operations timing is based on a pre-determined AEF rotation
       schedule which supports the Joint Global Force Management (GFM) schedule.
3.3. Crisis Action Planning.
   3.3.1. Deliberate/Crisis Action Planning.
114                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      3.3.1.1. Combatant commanders, their components, and supporting commands
      accomplish deliberate planning during peacetime conditions. Planners use scenarios and
      threats identified in national guidance, such as the JSCP, along with the combatant
      commander's evaluation of their AOR, to develop a series of plans that span a wide range
      of operations. See AFI 10-401, Chap. 3 for additional information related to deliberate
      and crisis action planning.
      3.3.1.2. This formal process develops responses to potential crises, determines forces
      required to achieve objectives, prepares deployment plans, and continually evaluates
      selected courses of action (COAs). This process results in a series of formal plans within
      each theater that contain lists of apportioned forces and their time-phased deployment
      schedules.
      3.3.1.3. The process for deliberate planning is cyclic and continual and is almost
      identical whether the resulting operation plan is a fully developed OPLAN, CONPLAN,
      or FUNCPLAN. Operations plans remain in effect until canceled or superceded by
      another approved plan. While in effect, they are continuously maintained and updated.
  3.3.2. Crisis Action Planning.
      3.3.2.1. Crisis action planning is driven by current events in real time and normally
      occurs in emergencies and in the context of time-sensitive situations. Planners base their
      efforts on the actual circumstances that exist when crisis action planning occurs. Detailed
      guidance and instructions are located in the APEX Family of Documents (see CJCS
      Guide 3130, Enclosure C).
      3.3.2.2. Each MAJCOM must establish complementary procedures and must ensure
      adequate procedures exist for subordinate command and agency use.
      3.3.2.3. These procedures must be periodically exercised during joint, Service
      component (C-MAJCOM/C-NAF) and installation/wing level exercises to ensure the
      required capability is available.
      3.3.2.4. The JPEC‘s Global Force Management (GFM) process developed policy and
      procedures in support of designated Joint Force Provider/Coordinator (JFP/JFC)
      allocation actions.
         3.3.2.4.1. Commander, Air Combat Command (COMACC), is delegated as the AF
         force provider (AF FP) and supports JS J31 in its role as Global Conventional JFC .
         3.3.2.4.2. Commander, Air Mobility Command (COMACC), is the AF component
         command for USTRANSCOM and acts as the AF FP for mobility forces.
         3.3.2.4.3. Commander, Air Force Special Operations Command, is the AF air
         component for USSOCOM and acts as the AF FP for special operations forces.
         3.3.2.4.4. MAJCOM and AFPC/DPW roles in sourcing crisis requirements will be
         accomplished IAW AFI 10-401 to determine sourcing recommendations and issues
         related to risk to sourcing other requirements, sustainability assessment and issues
         identified by other combatant commanders.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                         115


          3.3.2.4.5. AFPC/DPW and each MAJCOM must establish complementary
          procedures for sourcing crisis requirements and ensure adequate procedures exist for
          subordinate units.
      3.3.2.5. The AF FP, in coordination with the designated JFP:
          3.3.2.5.1. Determines AF sourcing solutions that satisfy validated combatant
          command requests for capability/forces (RFC/RFF) of conventional forces.
          3.3.2.5.2. Coordinates and recommends actions to sustain the level of capabilities or
          globally available forces to respond to validated combatant commander requirements.
3.4. Force Rotation (AEF) Planning.
   3.4.1. Force rotational plans support the GFM requirement of an immediate executable
   schedule. The AEF construct is the Air Force methodology of meeting existing and emerging
   worldwide CCDR requirements as depicted in the SecDef-approved GFMAP.
   3.4.2. CJCS orders to the supported commander, supporting commanders, and Services
   initiate such operations. These orders define plan details and requirements to accomplish the
   mission and authority to deploy forces. In accordance with CJCSM 3122.02C, such orders
   will specify weapons systems and a description of the ECS capability needed to sustain the
   operation.
      3.4.2.1. Additional orders will need to be issued when an operation becomes a rotational
      mission and the Air Force, as a Service, or all force providing combatant commanders are
      not identified to support.
   3.4.3. The supported component headquarters, in coordination with AFPC/DPW, is
   responsible for preparing the force rotation plan and ensuring the plan is time-phased to meet
   the AEF battle rhythm.
      3.4.3.1. The component headquarters will coordinate with AFPC/DPW to identify UTC
      capabilities from the AETF force modules and UTC Availability necessary to sustain the
      crisis operation and transition from crisis to rotational operations.
      3.4.3.2. A CJCS DEPORD and ensuing AF EXORD will be used to task and deploy AF
      forces for each AEF rotation.
      3.4.3.3. The supported component headquarters will not source a requirement identified
      in the force rotation TPFDD IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 9.
   3.4.4. ARC Participation.
      3.4.4.1. During each AEF vulnerability period, the deploying AEFs will have force
      elements provided by AFRC and ANG units. These units fill the applicable rotation by
      teaming (when feasible) units and personnel and rainbowing equipment.
      3.4.4.2. Specific methodology for meeting this objective is managed by the AFRC and
      ANG. ARC force volunteerism is maximized by providing rotation and tour duration
      flexibility. Component headquarters will consider the appropriate rotation policy and tour
      length with the goal of maximizing ARC volunteerism.
 116                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


Section 3B—Sourcing Overview

3.5. TPFDD Sourcing.
   3.5.1. To assist with the identification of TPFDD requirements for AEF sourcing,
   AFPC/DPW establishes force modules (FMs) for new and rotational requirements which are
   disseminated via the AFPC/DPW AEF Operation’s AEF Rotation Sourcing Plans and Tasks
   message. See AFI 10-401, Chapter 9 for additional information related to TPFDD sourcing
   processes and procedures.
   3.5.2. FMs allow the supported component headquarters to quickly identify and
   communicate valid requirements for Air Force sourcing. The component headquarters will
   place requirements reviewed and accepted in a designated FM during planning for each AEF
   ‘s rotation. Force providing organizations delegated authority to write to the supported
   commanders TPFDD must adhere to these guidelines.

Section 3C—Verification Overview

3.6. TPFDD Verification.
   3.6.1. Verification is the process whereby MAJCOMs/DRUs/FOAs/Service Components
   accomplish JOPES requirements to finalize the sourcing process. See AFI 10-401, Chapter 8
   for additional information related to TPFDD verification.
       3.6.1.1. During the verification process, every responsible agency ensures the sourced
       UTC/UIC has the required complements to meet the requirement; the applicable forces
       are available and ready; forces have been alerted for deployment; and the cargo is tailored
       to level-4 detail, if applicable. Verification completes the sourcing process.
       3.6.1.2. Air Force planners and FAMs at all levels must ensure that the TPFDD
       accurately reflects and is consistent with actual resources that units will deploy.
       3.6.1.3. Failure to accomplish this verification could result in misstating planned airlift
       requirements and possibly delaying the execution of a combatant commander‘s plan.
       3.6.1.4. Component headquarters will source requirements from their in-theater assets to
       the maximum extent possible before initiating an RFF/RFC to their CCDR.
       3.6.1.5. AFPC/DPW will work closely with the component headquarters and force
       providers to efficiently source and ensure timely verification by the Force Provider of
       UTC that will be available as postured in the UTC Availability in DCAPES and reported
       as ready in the AEF UTC Reporting Tool (ART).
