   3.6.2. Crisis Action Sourcing.
       3.6.2.1. Component headquarters planners will determine and input requirements into the
       applicable CCDR TPFDD.
       3.6.2.2. Force providers will first source requirements from Air Force forces assigned to
       the CCDR/CCMD TPFDD.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        117


          3.6.2.2.1. Component headquarters should not source assigned forces tasked in the
          current FY GFMAP if the tasking will interfere with the subsequent SECDEF-
          ordered tasking.
          3.6.2.2.2. All emergent CCDR requirements that cannot be met with assigned forces
          should generate an RFF/RFC in accordance with CJCSM 3122.01A.
      3.6.2.3. Once an RFF/RFC has been submitted and validated by the Joint Staff, the
      RFF/RFC will be vetted through the JFP to the AF FP IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter. 1.
      3.6.2.4. AF FPs will collect inputs from their respective HAF and/or MAJCOM FAMs
      and AFPC/DPW to develop a recommended sourcing solution.
          3.6.2.4.1. If a standard Air Force capability within existing resources can meet the
          requirement, then AF FPs recommend a standard sourcing solution.
          3.6.2.4.2. If a standard Air Force capability cannot meet the requirement, AF FPs, in
          conjunction with applicable HAF FAMs, evaluate the RFF/RFC for possible non-
          standard sourcing solutions in accordance with paragraph AFI 10-401, Chapter 2 and
          Table 2.1.
          3.6.2.4.3. The AF internally refers to non-standard force sourcing solutions as Joint
          Expeditionary Taskings (JET).
          3.6.2.4.4. AEFC/DPW sources forces IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 8.
          3.6.2.4.5. Force providers verify to the component headquarters the readiness of
          sourced forces IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 8 to include the ability to meet the TPFDD
          timelines.
   3.6.3. For rotational (AEF) TPFDDs, AFPW/DPW will:
      3.6.3.1. Place AEF sourcing that requires verification in a designated FM, in accordance
      with the AEF rotation sourcing plans and tasks message.
      3.6.3.2. Post FM requiring verification in an accompanying newsgroup to establish the
      verification suspense.
      3.6.3.3. Ensure verification is completed in accordance with timelines depicted in AFI
      10-401, Table 8.5.
      3.6.3.4. After the AFPC/DPW sourcing and verification FM has been suspensed,
      verifying agencies do not have to wait for release of the subsequent verification FMs to
      apply verification.
      3.6.3.5. MAJCOMs FAMs and/or war planners will ensure IDRCs are informed of wing
      AEF sourcing by use of DCAPES and Tasking Notification Tool (TNT).
3.7. MAJCOM Verification.
   3.7.1. Reclama procedures will be processed in accordance with AFI 10-401, Chapter 10.
   3.7.2. Newly sourced requirements will be placed in a verification FM and force providers
   must verify within timelines depicted in AFI 10-401, Table 8.5.
   3.7.3. Equipment Requirements and Sourcing
 118                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


       3.7.3.1. The force provider will identify sourcing solutions to AFPC/DPW for
       equipment-only UTCs not directly tied to a unit (e.g., vehicles) postured in the AEF
       Tempo Bands or Enabler force. UTCs that contain both MANFOR and LOGFOR detail
       will be sourced by AFPC/DPW using the same procedures and priorities as personnel-
       only UTCs IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 9.
       3.7.3.2. Due to the sensitivity of AFSOC's SOF mission and AMC's global MAF
       support, these mission requirements will continue to be sourced by the respective
       MAJCOMs. HQ AMC will source unique theater requirements for mobility support.
       3.7.3.3. The ECS SIPT is the focal point for coordinating all issues and concerns relative
       to equipment sourcing.
3.8. Tasking Notification Process.
   3.8.1. AFPC/DPW provides oversight of the tasking notification process for all TPFDDs
   sourced using AEF scheduled assets IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 9.
       3.8.1.1. It is responsible for controlling visibility for these TPFDDs and will provide
       automated support using DCAPES to base-level IDRC, manpower and personnel
       readiness offices, PERSCO teams, and central sites.
       3.8.1.2. AFPC/DPW provides visibility after coordination with and receiving the
       approval of the supported component headquarters.
   3.8.2. Assigning names to requirements in DCAPES is critical to the entire deployment
   process.
       3.8.2.1. Deploying members must be identified and updated in system IAW AFI 36-3802
       to ensure name visibility of members projected to deploy, to facilitate any advance
       training requirements, and schedule an appropriate airlift mission to meet the supported
       commander‘s DRI/RDD.
       3.8.2.2. AEFC/DPW will provide a bi-weekly nameless ULN report to the MAJCOMs
       for further processing with the MAJCOM FAMs and appropriate wing staffs.
       Additionally, at least 45 – 60 days following an AEF rotation, AEFC/DPW will publish
       metrics data depicting the percentage of names received in a specific window for the
       MAJCOM AEF Debriefs. Applicable window range covers 45+ days prior to the RDD,
       31-44 days prior to the RDD, 0-30 days prior to the RDD or names received after the
       RDD has passed as of the report date.

Section 3D—Employment Overview

3.9. Employment.
   3.9.1. The AEF employment objective is to meet a supported combatant commander‘s needs
   through the COMAFFOR with relevant UTC capabilities-based AETF packages (AEWs and
   AEGs) in accordance with validated theater mission requirements, as identified by the
   TPFDD. Planning must focus on sustained execution in the area of operations for the AEF
   execution period by integrating AEW, AEG, and AES command, operations, and support
   elements into an integrated, cohesive force. (AFI 10-401, Chapter 9)
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                          119


   3.9.2. AEF on-call forces will maintain the capability to rapidly transition from normal day-
   to-day operations to crisis response operations. Unit posture will increase consistent with the
   issuance and receipt of CJCS Warning/Planning/Alert/Deployment Order, Prepare to Deploy
   Order, and/or Execution Order
   3.9.3. Theater combatant commander mission requirements dictate response-timing
   constraints.
      3.9.3.1. In general, CONOPS should allow for a stair-step of response timing to reduce
      alert requirements. Service components must prepare to deploy forces, particularly ECS
      forces, during the initial phases of contingencies.
      3.9.3.2. Personnel will deploy only after receipt of valid contingency, exercise, and
      deployment (CED) orders and validation by the installation deployment officer (IDO)
      that the unit line number (ULN) has been validated in the TPFDD by the supported
      commander.

Section 3E—Shortfall/Reclama Overview

3.10. Shortfall and Reclama Procedures.
   3.10.1. Air Force active duty, AFRC, ANG, MAJCOMs, wings, groups, and units will make
   every effort to meet all taskings.
      3.10.1.1. Generally, relief will only be sought when a wing or tasked unit does not
      possess sufficient or qualified personnel to support a tasking or the tasking is impossible
      to meet or will shut down critical elements of the home station mission, as determined by
      the wing commander or equivalent.
      3.10.1.2. Filling shortfalls in one UTC could mean moving a person from another UTC
      as long as the individual(s) are within the same AEF vulnerability period.
      3.10.1.3. Units will immediately update ART to reflect the status of the UTC(s).
      3.10.1.4. IDOs will submit reclamas to their MAJCOM if no other installation/Wing
      resources are available to fill shortfalls. (See AFI 10-401 for details on processing
      reclamas and UIC Changes via RPT)
3.11. AEF Construct.
   3.11.1. The AEF is the USAF‘s construct for meeting global CCDR requirements.
      3.11.1.1. Employing forces via the AEF construct to meet non-CCDR requirements (e.g.
      Service-unique requirements, MAJCOM manning assist, etc.) reduces the ability to meet
      the global CCDR contingency requirement.
      3.11.1.2. Using the AEF construct to meet non-CCDR requirements will be approved by
      AF/A3/5 on a case-by-case basis.
   3.11.2. The supported organization requesting use of AEF forces will submit deviation
   request through their owning MAJCOM. MAJCOMs will coordinate with AF/A1 and
   sponsoring HAF DCS (if applicable) prior to seeking A3/5 approval.
   3.11.3. AFPC/DPW will build ULNs in a 08-series PID and source requirements IAW AFI
   10-401, Chapter 9 using only SECAF-retained and/or supported MAJCOM-owned forces.
 120                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


   Note: The use of 08-series PIDs is for accounting purposes only; USTRANSCOM will not
   assign lift against Service PIDs.

Section 3F—Installation/Wing/Unit Level Deployment Operations(Rotational AEF)

3.12. Installation/Wing/Unit Deployment Operations (Rotational AEF Operations).
   3.12.1. Tasking information will flow from JOPES through DCAPES to tasked
   installations/units.
   3.12.2. To preclude delaying tasking notifications to appropriate Airmen, IDOs and the
   IDRC will monitor DCAPES (at least twice a day) for new, modified, and/or deleted
   taskings. In addition, it is imperative that other sources of tasking information be constantly
   monitored such as SIPRNET web pages, DCAPES, Web-Hoc Query, and Newsgroups.
   Establish dialogue with MAJCOM, NAF, or component CAT Cells or Operations Centers.
   3.12.3. Unit commanders will review taskings and identify LIMFAC/shortfalls and update as
   required. The Plans and Integration Section will review the LIMFAC/shortfalls of the
   affected units so any problems expected are known ahead of time.
3.13. Tasking Receipt.
   3.13.1. Once the base receives a deployment tasking, the base implements its deployment
   process IAW the IDP.
       3.13.1.1. Tasking information flows continually throughout the AEF vulnerability
       period.
       3.13.1.2. The IDO must establish a system of notification to the Installation/Wing
       Commander and key senior leadership of each tasking.
       3.13.1.3. As a minimum, the IDO will notify key personnel within the IDRC (in the
       absence of the IDRC, notify IPR and LRS Plans & Integration personnel) and respective
       units of each tasking within 24-hours of receipt of tasking.
   3.13.2. Upon direction from the IDO:
       3.13.2.1. The IDRC will load the personnel levy flow file into LOGMOD.
       3.13.2.2. The UDM will load tasked personnel in LOGMOD for transfer back to
       DCAPES.
       3.13.2.3. Institutional Force and extended deployment taskings are received from AFPC
       with the name already in system; consolidating passenger data in LOGMOD of attached
       or supported Institutional Forces outside of the host organizational structure is not
       required.
3.14. Tasking Verification.
   3.14.1. Verification confirms the sourced data reflects actual data provided by the base or
   unit.
       3.14.1.1. During the verification process (see Attachment 4 for wing verification
       process), every responsible agency after the MAJCOM validation, starts with the IDRC
       confirming the sourced UTC/UIC has the required element(s) to meet the requirement;
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                           121


     applicable forces are available and ready; forces have been alerted for deployment; and
     the cargo is tailored to level-4 detail, and passenger line-level detail is tailored to match
     level-2 detail, if applicable.
     3.14.1.2. ANG units will verify taskings IAW with ANG MAJCOM supplement.
  3.14.2. MAJCOM AEF Cells in conjunction with MAJCOM FAMs initiate the verification
  process by confirming unit capability to fill UTC taskings. NOTE: Contacting tasked units is
  not required in every case e.g. if a unit is reporting Green in ART there is no need for contact
  except when the tasking requirement is short notice (30 days or less to first movement).
  3.14.3. MAJCOMs must notify units directly to meet short notice alerts/taskings received
  during non-duty days that require immediate attention. In support of AEF rotations, Log
  Plans, IPR, or Manpower Office personnel in the IDRC will check DCAPES at least twice
  daily during normal duty hours for new, changed or deleted taskings.
  3.14.4. When a new tasking or change to an existing tasking is received, the IDRC will
  verify it within (2) duty days (or within 24-hours for short-notice taskings i.e. within 45-days
  of first movement) of receipt before forwarding to the appropriate unit(s). NOTE: ANG
  units will follow their higher headquarters guidance on verification procedures. Verification
  includes:
     3.14.4.1. IDRC Manpower (IPR in the ARC) personnel ensure the UIC for the tasking is
     appropriate. If not, the IDO will contact the sourcing agency (e.g. MAJCOM FAM) for
     re-sourcing to the appropriate UIC. NOTE: UIC change requests are accomplished in
     RPT, if UIC is known.
     3.14.4.2. The tasked unit, in coordination with the IDRC, ensures the required AFSC
     exists in the tasked unit and it is postured in the appropriate AEF block, unless surge
     operations are approved.
     3.14.4.3. Research MISCAP substitution rules and consult with the applicable UDMs for
     possible tasking resolution. If not properly postured, communication between the IDRC,
     tasked unit, MAJCOM FAM and AFPC/DPW is required for clarification.
     3.14.4.4. If no capability exists at the installation/base, reclama the tasking to the tasking
     source IAW this instruction and AFI 10-401.
     3.14.4.5. Individual (by name) deployment taskings sourced via MilPDS for institutional
     forces or 365-day extended deployments are processed IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 10.
     3.14.4.6. Ensures the LAD/RDD specified for the GEOLOC is feasible and attainable.
     Taskings should allow lead time at base level to allow for completion of Just-in-Time
     (JIT) training, equipment preparation, en route training, flight arrangements, etc.
         3.14.4.6.1. If the RDD is not feasible, the IDRC’s IPR will contact the deployed
         PERSCO or deployed commander IAW this AFI and AFI 36-3802 with a delayed
         reporting request/notification.
         3.14.4.6.2. Request for RDD adjustments through the supported command will only
         be made to comply with the timeline standard for verification in AFI 10-401, unless a
         more stringent timeline is stated in the DEPORD. If the RDD cannot be met due to
         completion of JIT training, equipment preparation, or flight arrangements, contact the
 122                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


          deployed PERSCO or deployed commander IAW this AFI and AFI 36-3802 with a
          delayed reporting request/notification.
       3.14.4.7. Identify any incomplete or missing data (i.e. incomplete or unlisted
       line/command remarks). The sourcing agency will be contacted to clarify any
       inconsistencies.
       3.14.4.8. If the tasking does not require any corrections, the IDO will accept the tasking
       in DCAPES. If required, corrections will be submitted via a reclama and/or UIC Change
       via RPT IAW AFI 10-401 using the instructions in the RPT User Manual.
   3.14.5. The IDRC will upload the tasking into LOGMOD or other locally approved tasking
   notification method as identified in the IDP and forward to the tasked unit/UDM. The
   notification to the unit will be NLT (1) duty day after receipt of tasking.
   3.14.6. Units will provide equipment and personnel info back to the IDRC to fulfill taskings
   IAW Chapters 4 and 5, respectively, or provide shortfall documentation
   3.14.7. The IPR updates DCAPES with tasked personnel information IAW the timelines
   established in AFI 36-3802. NOTE: Automatic rule sets in DCAPES will be used to verify
   personnel deployment eligibility. If the system flags a condition preventing assignment to
   the UTC, and an approved waiver is not already on file, SSN(s) will be returned to the UDM
   for waiver and/or reclama processing actions.
   3.14.8. Within (1) duty day of the IDRC receiving validation of deployment eligibility from
   the UDM, the IDO in coordination with TMO will ensure appropriate mode of transportation
   is available to meet TPFDD ALD for personnel moves.
   3.14.9. On behalf of the IDO, the IDRC will verify requirements can be supported to the
   MAJCOM AEF Cell, MAJCOM planners and/or FAMs will complete tasking notification
   and initiate TPFDD verification actions IAW AFI 10-401 and JOPES processes contained in
   CJCSM 3122.02.
3.15. Requirements Validation.
   3.15.1. The validation process begins once the FP has verified the sourcing. During
   execution, movement data within a TPFDD must be validated in order to schedule
   appropriate strategic transportation or book channel missions in GATES. “Validate” in this
   context is defined in Joint Publications as: “Execution procedure used by combatant
   command components, supporting CCDRs, and providing organizations to confirm to the
   supported commander that all the information records in a TPFDD are not only error-free,
   but also accurately reflect the current status, attributes (lower level personnel and cargo data),
   and availability of units and requirements.”
   3.15.2. AF planners and FAMs must ensure timelines established to support the sourcing,
   verification, and validation process are followed. The standard timeline for completing
   sourcing will be IAW respective TPFDD Letters of Instruction (LOIs). Wings/installations
   will follow this instruction, AFI 10-401, and AFI 36-3802 timelines for filling or shortfalling
   requirements.
   3.15.3. The 6-month (Bands B-E) on-call/deployment period is based on a rotational
   environment where all requirements are known and can be met with the forces allocated
   within AEF Bands in the AEF vulnerability period or Enablers.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                           123


      3.15.3.1. Individuals and equipment allocated to UTCs within the current AEF rotation
      must not participate in any activity that directly impacts their availability to deploy
      during this period.
      3.15.3.2. Scheduled leaves during the deployment/on-call period will be scrutinized to
      ensure member’s ability to respond quickly, if required.
      3.15.3.3. Transportation arrangements into the AOR are influenced by availability of
      airlift, which is influenced by world events and subject to change prior to actual lift date.
3.16. Travel Requirements Verification.
   3.16.1. The IDO and IDRC personnel must work closely together to ensure individuals and
   equipment meet deployment timing and mode of travel as specified in the PID/TPFDD
   tasking for personnel/equipment leaving their installation. In order to best help IDRC, PDF,
   and/or CDF personnel plan movement, the IDO first needs to make some decisions based on
   an analysis of the TPFDD ALDs/RDDs against the strategic lift airflow will provide the
   priority for UTC movement and will ask the following questions:
      3.16.1.1. What is the APOE for the personnel/equipment leaving the base?
      3.16.1.2. Is the origin the APOE or will movement to an APOE be required?
      3.16.1.3. If moving to an APOE, is the appropriate transportation being used? Is ground
      transportation, commercial airline, Group Operational Passenger System (GOPAX),
      aggregated passengers using CONUS to CONUS Contingency movement (CCPAX) used
      where appropriate?
      3.16.1.4. Is the APOE a military installation or international airport?
      3.16.1.5. If it is a military installation, does deploying members have their reporting
      instructions/equipment preparation requirements from their respective IDO and/or base
      Transportation Officer?
      3.16.1.6. What is the Mode/Source for the personnel departing the base? If the
      Mode/Source is “AC - Air via supporting commander channel (AMC or Service) aircraft,
      does the IDO ensure the IDRC makes appropriate arrangements to ensure passengers
      meet their RDD at the end destination?
      3.16.1.7. If the Mode/Source is “AK - Air via strategic (AMC, AMC-contract) aircraft,
      does the IDO ensure the TACC has made travel arrangements to ensure passengers meet
      their RDD at the end destination?
   3.16.2. DELETED
   3.16.3. If the APOE is not home station, the IDO will ensure the IDRC makes appropriate
   arrangements to meet the APOE ALD e.g. commercial airlines, buses, organic or commercial
   trucks, or GOPAX through the Tanker/Airlift Control Center (TACC).
3.17. Movement Flow Schedule.
   3.17.1. The IDRC will coordinate with its MAJCOM, or component headquarters, who will
   then coordinate with 618 AOC, TACC, for airflow and/or surface movement information
   during normal rotations in support of Combat Air Forces/Mobility Air Forces (CAF/MAF)
 124                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


   strategic airlift support. Airlift support for ECS will be coordinated with TACC by the
   component headquarters and verified for validation to USTRANSCOM.
   3.17.2. For visibility of airflow, the IDRC will access DCAPES, Global Decision Support
   System (GDSS), SMS and/or IGC. If airlift is not visible after the USTRANSCOM (USTC)
   Status Codes in the TPFDD shows lift is allocated (“A”), then the IDRC should contact their
   MAJCOM AEF Cell who will then contact the TACC for status.
   3.17.3. Monitor Status. A designated POC in each work center should provide status of
   deployment issues to the IDO/IDRC, who is responsible for status reporting to the CAT.
   Also, POCs will report LIMFAC/shortfalls status. LOGMOD Schedule screens, status
   boards, and other electronic media are helpful management tools for tracking deployment
   status.
   3.17.4. Monitor Tasking Changes. Due to dynamic situations, taskings and priorities may
   change. Beddown sites, number and type of aircraft required, aircraft configurations, and so
   on, can cause extensive changes to unit deployment efforts. In addition, DPW or FAMs at
   the MAJCOMs could determine a particular unit tasking has higher priorities than others.
   Units will monitor the situation closely and tailor their actions to reflect any changes in
   priorities.
   3.17.5. Units will prioritize the movement of cargo and passengers as directed in DCAPES
   (or, at a minimum, LOGPLAN) to meet the RDD specified by the Supported Command. The
   primary method of scheduling personnel and cargo is the LOGMOD Schedule.
3.18. Waivers.
   3.18.1. DELETED
   3.18.2. DELETED
   3.18.3. Tasking Waivers. Prior to submitting a reclama, the tasked commander, through IPR
   and deployed PERSCO, will request the deployed Group Commander waive any restriction
   (e.g. line remarks, SEI, grade, skill level, etc.) or permit substitutions through the waiver
   process contained in AFI 10-401 and AFI 36-3802.
   3.18.4. Unit commanders will:
       3.18.4.1. Submit reclamas for personnel and equipment shortfalls via RPT IAW AFI 10-
       401.
       3.18.4.2. Ensure they have thoroughly reviewed all reclamas to ensure that every option
       regarding AFSC or equipment substitution (IAW UTC MISCAP, functional guidance,
       etc.), risk mitigation, etc. have been considered for their respective unit prior to
       submitting a reclama.
       3.18.4.3. DELETED
   3.18.5. The IDO will:
       3.18.5.1. Provide personnel shortfalls to the IDRC (IPR and MO representatives will
       consider substitutions IAW UTC MISCAPs, line remarks, or as approved by the
       deployed commander.)
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                             125


      3.18.5.2. Provide equipment shortfalls to the LRS Equipment Accountability Office
      (EAO).
      3.18.5.3. The IDRC and LRS EAO will use functional resources to confirm the unit
      shortfall and scrub available wing resources for fill actions.
      3.18.5.4. DELETED
      3.18.5.5. Use equipment with the same national stock number (NSN) and/or a suitable
      substitute as approved by MEFPAK Responsible Agency FAMs for applicable
      LOGDET. Suitable replacements and/or further reclamas must be IAW AFI 10-401,
      Chapter 10.
      3.18.5.6. The IDO will monitor reclama status via secure RPT available through the AEF
      Online Portal at the following website: https://aef.afpc.randolph.af.smil.mil/default.aspx.
   3.18.6. The IDRC IPR will:
      3.18.6.1. Review chain-of-command resources to see if individuals with the required
      AFSCs are located elsewhere within the wing or wing equivalent on the base in the same
      MAJCOM in the same AEF (not required for Institution Forces or extended
      deployments).
      3.18.6.2. Check for individuals matching the allowable substitutions identified in the
      UTC MISCAP, line remarks, or approved AFSC waiver from the deployed commander.
      NOTE: IDRC is responsible for coordinating replacement actions.
      3.18.6.3. Fill that role if the DCC is not activated.
      3.18.6.4. Identify substitutions to their MAJCOM for resourcing to correct unit.
      3.18.6.5. Submit a shortfall, if the installation/wing cannot support the tasking or the
      AFSC is not on base.
   3.18.7. See AFI 10-401, Chapter 2 for use of Institutional Forces.

Section 3G—Installation/Wing/Unit Level Deployment Operations (Crisis Action)

3.19. Installation/Wing/Unit Deployment Operations (Crisis Operations).
   3.19.1. During a crisis or in the build up to a response to a crisis, units should expect to see a
   warning order (WARNORD), planning order (PLANORD), alert order (ALERTORD),
   and/or PTDO prior to receipt of the EXORD and/or DEPORD.
      3.19.1.1. While these orders are normally sent only to MAJCOM headquarters and not
      directly to the wings, applicable MAJCOMs, NAFs or equivalent CAT(s) are responsible
      for retransmitting the order(s) to affected wings. This requires prompt action since timely
      receipt of these orders may not occur.
      3.19.1.2. MAJCOMs/NAFs receive information via secure telephone, message traffic, or
      GCCS newsgroups and pass related information to subordinate units using similar
      methods.
      3.19.1.3. Tasking information will flow from JOPES through DCAPES to the tasked
      installations/units. Further, there will often be information flow before an official order.
126                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      3.19.1.4. Upon receipt of applicable orders, the host installation/wing command post will
      immediately notify, at a minimum, the IDO and host installation commander. See JP 5-0,
      Joint Operation Planning, Figure II-10, for a description of types of orders.
  3.19.2. The order may not contain any specific taskings for a specific weapon system.
  Compare available plans and details of the WARNORD, PLANORD, and/or ALERTORD
  for clues as to what may be coming.
      3.19.2.1. If the message contains actual UTCs or weapon systems identification, actual
      preparatory movement actions may begin.
      3.19.2.2. Unless the pending action is in an area with no plan on the shelf, it may be
      necessary to read over the current plan for the AOR in question. Read the plan’s
      summary, LOI, basic plan, annexes C & D, and other applicable functional annexes.
  3.19.3. Once the IDO receives the applicable orders (or other indications of an imminent
  deployment), the IDO should host a meeting to:
      3.19.3.1. Review the tasking(s).
         3.19.3.1.1. Prioritize tasked UTCs.
         3.19.3.1.2. Identify LIMFACs/shortfalls.
      3.19.3.2. Establish a concept of operations and concept of logistics support (if enough
      detail is available).
      3.19.3.3. DELETED
      3.19.3.4. Members at this meeting will include, at a minimum:
         3.19.3.4.1. IDO.
         3.19.3.4.2. Logistics Plans representative.
         3.19.3.4.3. IPR representative.
         3.19.3.4.4. MO representative.
         3.19.3.4.5. LRS (Supply) representative.
         3.19.3.4.6. LRS (Transportation) representative.
         3.19.3.4.7. UDMs with possible tasked UTCs.
  3.19.4. To preclude delaying tasking notifications to appropriate Airmen, the DCC will:
      3.19.4.1. Monitor DCAPES (DMR Change Logs) twice a day for new, modified, or
      deleted taskings.
      3.19.4.2. Monitor other sources of tasking information such as SIPRNET web pages,
      Web-Hoc Query, and Newsgroups.
      3.19.4.3. Establish dialogue with MAJCOM, NAFs, or component CAT Cells and/or
      operations centers.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        127


3.20. Standby Personnel.
   3.20.1. Place personnel on standby IAW MAJCOM directives. The requirement for standby
   (recall, if required) varies from MAJCOM to MAJCOM. Make personnel available if a
   known tasking is coming. Placing personnel on standby will allow maximum flexibility in
   responding to whatever tasking is received.
   3.20.2. Follow the MAJCOM and Installation/Wing Commander’s direction for placing
   personnel on stand-by.
   3.20.3. At a minimum, the DCC staff will be recalled or notified when the Installation/Wing
   Commander is notified.
   3.20.4. The IDO will alert the FSS Commander of the potential need to activate the PDF and
   the LRS/LGRD (or APS at CONUS AMC strategic aerial port) of the potential to activate the
   CDF.
3.21. Crisis Action Taskings.
   3.21.1. The command post will provide tasking messages to the Installation/Wing
   Commanders and the IDO immediately upon receipt.
       3.21.1.1. The IDO will notify the DCC staff immediately if CAT validation results in
       changes.
       3.21.1.2. Simultaneously, the IDO will notify deployment workcenters and tasked units
       of message receipt and actions required.
       3.21.1.3. A DEPORD or EXORD message date/time group establishes the Reference
       Start Time (RST). NOTE: RST is the date and time from which all execution efforts
       begin.
   3.21.2. If directed by the wing/installation commander, the IDO will provide a concept brief
   to senior leadership, unit commanders, deployment workcenter supervision and UDMs.
   3.21.3. The concept briefing sets the tone for the deployment and ensures all deploying and
   support units understand the tasking, the deployment schedule, and critical employment site
   information that could affect the mission, health, and safety of deploying personnel.
   3.21.4. IDOs will ensure applicable data is briefed to ensure successful deployment
   execution. Refer to Attachment 7 for a recommended Deployment Concept Brief outline.

Section 3H—Installation Deployment Plan (IDP) Execution

3.22. IDP Execution.
   3.22.1. Once the base receives a DEPORD or EXORD, the installation implements its
   deployment process IAW the IDP.
   3.22.2. Implementing the IDP will help to ensure all augmentees are available and will assist
   in activating the required work centers with needed equipment and supplies to conduct 24-
   hour operations, as needed.
 128                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


3.23. Deployment Workcenters Activation.
   3.23.1. Deployment management requires all agencies responsible for deployment actions to
   work together to ensure they meet all taskings. Usually the installation/wing’s deployment
   organization is not fully activated until an installation receives a tasking to deploy.
   3.23.2. Time requirements for activating work centers are not dictated, so each installation
   must determine when to activate their work centers according to the situation at hand. The
   following paragraphs explain the purpose and suggested activation priority supporting the
   wing deployment process.
       3.23.2.1. CAT Activation.
          3.23.2.1.1. Early in a crisis, the focus is on gathering and disseminating accurate
          information. Command and control is critical to important agencies such as the base
          command post, CAT, and the DCC.
          3.23.2.1.2. Although each command and unit has its own CAT activation procedures,
          generally expect CAT activation in stages. As action by the unit becomes more
          likely, CAT director should activate the full team.
          3.23.2.1.3. CATs positively affect deployment processes by monitoring and engaging
          with the following: tracking of shortfalls until relieved by HHQ; confirming
          transportation requirements against actual airlift provided; questioning bottlenecks in
          personnel/equipment processes; validity of personnel personnel/equipment tailoring
          actions based on mission/location; involvement of unit commanders with the
          presentation of UTCs for processing; responsiveness to HHQ messages and
          installation/wing responses; and safety.
       3.23.2.2. DCC Activation.
          3.23.2.2.1. Activate the DCC in time to allow representatives the necessary time
          needed to translate the DEPORD/EXORD, establish communications with HHQ, and
          prepare the LOGMOD Schedule.
          3.23.2.2.2. The IDO will activate other work centers in enough time to begin
          accepting cargo and personnel for processing based on the LOGMOD Schedule.
          3.23.2.2.3. When activated, the DCC serves as the focal point for all deployment C2
          actions on an installation and reports to the CAT.
          3.23.2.2.4. The IDO must establish lines of communication between higher
          headquarters, the CAT, deployment work centers, and the DCC, and between the
          DCC and tasked units. All information essential to deployment operations will pass
          through the DCC.
          3.23.2.2.5. The IDO will use approved command and control systems such as
          DCAPES and LOGMOD to ensure everyone is informed of installation/wing TPFDD
          taskings.
       3.23.2.3. Cargo Deployment Function (CDF) Activation.
          3.23.2.3.1. Activate the CDF when directed by the IDO.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                            129


          3.23.2.3.2. The CDF OIC/NCOIC will ensure all required resources are readily
          available to properly transport, receive, inspect, marshal, and load cargo to meet
          support transportation requirements.
          3.23.2.3.3. The CDF will develop clear procedures if both air and surface operations
          are required.
      3.23.2.4. Personnel Deployment Function (PDF) Activation.
          3.23.2.4.1. The IDO, in coordination with the FSS OPSO, activates the PDF.
          3.23.2.4.2. The PDF OIC/NCOIC will ensure all required resources are readily
          available to properly account for, process, manifest and load deploying personnel for
          transportation requirements.
      3.23.2.5. Unit Deployment Control Centers (UDCC) Activation.
          3.23.2.5.1. Unit commanders will activate UDCCs upon direction of the CAT or IDO
          (24-hour operations, if needed).
          3.23.2.5.2. UDMs will gather work center members and brief them on all the
          deployment information and advise them when to set up the cargo/unit assembly
          areas.
          3.23.2.5.3. UDCCs will deactivate after approval by the IDO. Personnel deployment
          eligibility will be constantly monitored by UDMs to ensure required deployment
          positions can be filled by qualified individuals at all times.
          3.23.2.5.4. Units will attempt, as early as possible, to identify potential personnel
          eligibility problems in order to allow the PDF maximum time to try to find qualified
          personnel from installation/wing resources.
              3.23.2.5.4.1. If qualified personnel are not available on the installation, notify the
              DCC so they can elevate the requirement to higher headquarters and/or
              AFPC/DPW.
              3.23.2.5.4.2. In many cases, commanders can waive eligibility factor problems.
              3.23.2.5.4.3. When they cannot waive them, commanders will elevate those
              personnel issues or shortfall IAW applicable reclama and shortfall implementing
              guidance.
3.24. Tasking, Requirement, and Movement Validation/Verification.
   3.24.1. The tasking verification process for crisis response surge operations will follow the
   same procedures as identified in AFI 10-401, Chapter 8 with the following exceptions:
   3.24.2. IDRC becomes the DCC, and any additional deployment workcenter personnel
   required by the IDO are notified that the DCC has been activated.
   3.24.3. Accelerate all timelines for ASAP completion.
   3.24.4. . Requirement Validation. The requirement validation process for crisis response
   operations will follow the same procedures as identified in AFI 10-401, Chapter 9 with the
   exception that timelines will likely be accelerated based on real-world events that is driving
   the deployment.
130                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


  3.24.5. Movement Flow Schedule.
      3.24.5.1. The DCC will coordinate with its MAJCOM, supported component
      headquarters and TACC concerning airlift.
      3.24.5.2. The supported CCDR will coordinate movement with USTRANSCOM during
      crisis action.
      3.24.5.3. For visibility of airflow, the DCC will access DCAPES, IGC, Global Decision
      Support System (GDSS), and/or Single Mobility System (SMS).
      3.24.5.4. A designated POC in each work center will provide status of deployment issues
      to the IDO, who is responsible for status reporting to the CAT. Also, POCs will report
      LIMFAC/shortfalls status. Schedule screens, status boards, and other electronic media
      are helpful management tools for tracking deployment status.
      3.24.5.5. Due to dynamic situations, taskings and priorities will probably change daily,
      or even hourly.
         3.24.5.5.1. Beddown sites, number and type of aircraft required, aircraft
         configurations, and so on, can cause extensive changes to unit deployment efforts.
         3.24.5.5.2. In addition, DPW or MAJCOM FAMs could determine that a particular
         unit tasking has higher priorities than others.
         3.24.5.5.3. Units will monitor the situation closely and tailor their actions to reflect
         any changes in priorities.
3.25. LOGMOD Schedule.
  3.25.1. The LOGMOD Schedule is the authoritative document within the wing that
  orchestrates the movement of cargo and personnel (see Chapters 4 and 5 for specific cargo
  and personnel processing procedures, respectively). Accuracy must be carefully ensured.
  3.25.2. Reference AFPAM 10-1403, Air Mobility Planning Factors, the LOGMOD Users
  Guide, system help files, and sample schedules with recommended event times for more
  detailed information.
  3.25.3. Prioritizing and Monitoring Movement Outflow.
      3.25.3.1. The IDO is responsible for managing the outflow of cargo and personnel based
      on these guidelines:
      3.25.3.2. The IDO will create the schedule to flow through the installation deployment
      process based on the Supported Command TPFDD RDD movement priority of
      equipment and/or personnel, strategic airlift arrival/departure times and aggregate
      transportation requirements. The schedule and initial aircraft load plans will be developed
      concurrently to ensure efficiency.
      3.25.3.3. Units will prioritize equipment and personnel to the UTC increment and
      personnel line number detail based on the Supported Command TPFDD RDDs.
      Reference AFI 10-401 for prioritizing UTCs.
      3.25.3.4. IDOs will ensure an adequate backup method for LOGMOD Schedule
      preparation when required.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                   131


           3.25.3.4.1. When the primary method of LOGMOD is unavailable, other automated
           systems may be used.
           3.25.3.4.2. If automated systems aren’t available, use AF Form 2511, Deployments
           Schedule of Events – Cargo; AF Form 2511A, Deployment Schedule of Events -
           Personnel; and AF Form 2512, Deployment Schedule of Events - Loading Schedule
           (see Attachments 9, 10, and 11).
           3.25.3.4.3. All work centers must complete scheduled events by times depicted on
           these forms. When creating LOGMOD Schedules, IDOs will use the following table
           of events nomenclature for applicable events utilized:

Figure 3.1. Applicable Events LOGMOD Schedule Nomenclature
Cargo Events                                  Personnel Events
Cargo Unit Assembly Complete                  Pax Unit Assembly Complete
Cargo Incheck Start                           Pax Mobility Bags Start
Cargo Incheck Complete                        Pax Mobility Bags Complete
Cargo JI Start                                Pax Process Start
Cargo JI Complete                             Pax Process Complete
Cargo Manifest Comp lete                      Pax Orders Complete
Cargo QC Complete                             Pax Manifest Complete
Cargo A/C Pkg Complete                        Baggage Load Start (Pax MSNs Only)
Cargo Load Start                              Baggage Load Complete (Pax MSNs Only)
Cargo Load Complete                           Pax Load Start
Transmit manifest to IGC                      Pax Load Complete

   3.25.4. LOGMOD Schedule Distribution.
       3.25.4.1. Provide completed or published schedules to the CAT, key deployment
       workcenters and affected units expeditiously.
       3.25.4.2. Use either the LOGMOD remote LOGMOD Schedule viewer capability or a
       distribution method that works best for an installation and include this in the IDP.
   3.25.5. Tracking Schedule Actions. Use the LOGMOD system or hard-copy LOGMOD
   Schedules to track the actions required (as described in Chapters 4 and 5).
   3.25.6. Updating the Schedule. Any change to timing, events, aircraft information,
   personnel and equipment requires a published change to the LOGMOD Schedule. Capture
   reasons for changes in the remarks section. The DCC will publish LOGMOD Schedules and
   provide to all affected deployment workcenters immediately.
 132                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


Section 3I—Deployment Reporting/Data Collection

3.26. Deployment Reporting.
   3.26.1. The DCC must keep the installation’s senior leadership up to date during deployment
   operations as specified by local requirements.
   3.26.2. Use LOGMOD remote LOGMOD Schedule viewer, if available, to support this
   requirement.
   3.26.3. Specific base reporting requirements will be identified in the IDP.
   3.26.4. UDMs will prepare reclamas IAW AFI 10-401, AFPC/DPW RPT User Manual
   procedures, IDP rule-sets, and other applicable instructions.
   3.26.4.1. Updates to senior leadership that requests the IDOs physical presence must not
   impede mission accomplishment.
3.27. JOPES Deployment UTC Data.
   3.27.1. Units will electronically transfer tailored LOGPLAN/Schedule files to the gaining
   MAJCOM for review and for processing into JOPES through DCAPES in support of the
   CJCS requirement to develop a sourced TPFDD for the first (7) days within 72-hours..
   3.27.2. The tasking source specifies how and when to send the information (reference
   Attachment 8).
3.28. Post Deployment Data Documentation.
   3.28.1. MAJCOM/A4s are responsible for implementing policy for deployment data
   retention/collection.
       3.28.1.1. At a minimum, CJCS directed exercises and national level exercises will be
       recorded IAW this instruction, and maintained and disposed of IAW AFMAN 33-363,
       Management of Records, and AFI 33-364, Records Disposition - Procedures and
       Responsibilities.
       3.28.1.2. The IDO is the installation POC for deployment data. The IDO will:
          3.28.1.2.1. Ensure deployment processes include collection and maintenance of the
          following as minimum documentation for deploying aircraft:
          3.28.1.2.2. . Passenger manifest.
          3.28.1.2.3. Cargo manifest.
          3.28.1.2.4. Equipment listings.
          3.28.1.2.5. Hazardous cargo waivers.
          3.28.1.2.6. Load plans,
          3.28.1.2.7. Other documents identifying equipment and personnel aboard deploying
          aircraft,
          3.28.1.2.8. Shippers Declarations for Dangerous Goods.
          3.28.1.2.9. LOGMOD load and packing lists.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                      133


         3.28.1.2.10. DD Form 2133, Joint Airlift Inspection Record.
  3.28.2. Include documentation for both host and tenant units.
  3.28.3. If LOGMOD is not available or functional for the purpose of generating these
  products, AF Form 2518, Deployment Packing List, will be manually generated (see
  Attachment 14).
  3.28.4. DELETED
  3.28.5. In LOGMOD, archive a copy of the Logistics Plan file and the Schedule file.
  3.28.6. In CMOS/GATES, archive the cargo and passenger manifest data. This data is of
  historical significance, required for trend analysis and process improvement, and maintained
  IAW AFMAN 33-363, Management of Records, and disposed of in accordance with the Air
  Force RDS located at https://www.my.af.mil/afrims/afrims/afrims/rims.cfm.
  3.28.7. Deployment, contingency, and lesser contingency operations records, will be
  identified and retained if MAJCOM/A4s deem the results beneficial for collection under Air
  Force Records Information Management System (AFRIMS) Records Disposition Schedule
  (RDS) located at https://www.my.af.mil/afrims/afrims/afrims/rims.cfm.
  3.28.8. As the installation OPR for deployment data, the IDO will compile and analyze data
  for trends to identify ways of improving the deployment process.
  3.28.9. Deploying unit commanders will also document deployment data to ensure
  comprehensive deployment analysis to improve unit deployment procedures.
  3.28.10. During deployments, the DCC is responsible for collecting and documenting
  deployment activity data. This is essentially handled by each deployed system and by unit
  logs.
  3.28.11. Installations will accomplish documentation of lessons learned using the AF lessons
  learned program IAW AFI 90-1601, Air Force Lessons Learned Program, , MAJCOM after-
  action reporting requirements, and AEF after-action reporting IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 3.
     3.28.11.1. (Added-USAFE) Due to the nature of the documents required to be collected
     and maintained, IDRCs will build a continuity binder at the completion of each operation,
     exercise, and AEF rotation. Documents included in the continuity binder may either be
     printed on paper, or scanned and stored electronically in a location referenced in the
     binder.
 134                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


                                          Chapter 4

                         DEPLOYMENT EXECUTION (CARGO)

Section 4A—-General

4.1. General.
   4.1.1. The unit commander, or designated representative, oversees all unit equipment and
   cargo preparation in support of deployments.
   4.1.2. Commander must ensure units prepare and handle their cargo IAW DTR 4500.9-R,
   Part II - Cargo Movement and Part III - Mobility; AFI 24-203; AFMAN 24-204(I); AFMAN
   24-306(IP), Manual for the Wheeled Operator; Title 49, Code of Federal Regulations, and is
   responsible for such documentation to be accurate.
   4.1.2.1. Convoy Deployments. Units that deploy by convoy must follow the specific cargo
   preparation requirements in AFI 24-301 and DTR 4500.9-R, Part III, Appendix F.

Section 4B—Equipment Management

4.2. Authorized Equipment.
   4.2.1. UTCs will only be filled with equipment assigned to the tasked unit.
       4.2.1.1. Exceptions to this policy require a waiver IAW AFI 10-401.
       4.2.1.2. Fragmentation could occur where one unit provides the manpower requirement
       and another provides the equipment, or if one unit provides manning augmentation to
       another unit.
       4.2.1.3. Typically, fragmenting UTC records will only be allowed in cases where the two
       units are formally linked in DOC statements or other functional area documents.
   4.2.2. No authorization will be counted against more than one UTC record unless a waiver is
   granted by USAF/A5XW (e.g. USSTRATCOM supported UTCs). Additionally, each UTC
   record will be placed into only one AEF Capability Library per cycle.
   4.2.3. If a unit can no longer support a postured UTC, the unit must coordinate with the
   respective MAJCOM war planner and FAM.
   4.2.4. Personnel in deployable UTCs must be equipped or have access to equipment to
   maintain the UTC capability.
   4.2.5. ART must be updated to reflect status of equipment for each standard deployable UTC
   IAW AFI 10-244.
4.3. Standardized UTC Equipment.
   4.3.1. Pilot/non-pilot units will identify cargo increments, within LOGMOD, using the
   proper increment types, deployment echelon codes, and functional account codes.
   4.3.2. Units will assign Unit Cargo Increment Monitors to manage a given set of cargo
   increments from each deploying unit.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                          135


      4.3.2.1. The monitors will ensure they provide inputs/updates to their UDMs, who will
      ensure the LOGMOD database is updated.
      4.3.2.2. When preparing for deployment, UDMs and/or Unit Cargo Increment Monitors
      will refer to the squadron or shop LOGPLAN material list (in LOGMOD) to ensure they
      have the minimum authorized and required UTC cargo. NOTE: LOGPLAN material lists
      will be kept accurate and deploying equipment marked in advance (if possible) for all
      deploying UTC cargo e.g. palletized, rolling-stock, hand-carried, or floor-loaded.
   4.3.3. Refer to the installation/wing LOGMOD administrators and help file for proper use of
   deployment echelon codes, increment numbers, increment types, FACs and titles, CCCs,
   TCMD, LPD, movement priority codes and NSNs.
4.4. Equipment Sourcing.
   4.4.1. The force provider will identify sourcing solutions to AFPC/DPW for equipment-only
   UTCs not directly tied to a unit (e.g. vehicles) postured in the AEF tempo bands or Enabler
   force.
      4.4.1.1. UTCs that contain both MANFOR and LOGFOR detail will be sourced by
      AFPC/DPW using the same procedures and priorities as personnel-only UTCs.
      4.4.1.2. Due to the sensitivity of AFSOC’s SOF mission and AMC’s global MAF
      support, these mission requirements will continue to be sourced by the respective
      MAJCOMs.
          4.4.1.2.1. HQAMC will source unique theater requirements for mobility support.
          4.4.1.2.2. The ECS SIPT is the focal point for coordinating all issues and concerns
          relative to equipment sourcing.
   4.4.2. Generic equipment-only UTCs will be placed in the enabler library IAW AFI 10-401,
   Chapter 7.
   4.4.3. For sourcing purposes, all equipment-only UTCs placed in the UTC Availability are
   available for deployment.
   4.4.4. AFPC/DPW will nominate equipment-only UTCs from the installations in the on-call
   AEF deployment window as identified by the ECS SIPT-approved Target Base Alignment
   Template.
   4.4.5. Aeromedical Evacuation (AE) UTCs will be sourced irrespective of on-call AEF
   deployment window.
   4.4.6. Once sourced, and at the direction of the parent MAJCOM, units/wings will
   electronically pass their equipment (DCAPES Plan export) information to their MAJCOM
   FAM via SIPR. Units/Wings must indicate ULN data and whether the equipment detail is
   from a UTC that contains both equipment and personnel or an equipment-only UTC. NOTE:
   Refer to AFI 10-401, Chapter 10 for tailoring guidance.
   4.4.7. Use of WRM is restricted to ensure sufficient capability is available to support theater
   starter or swing stock requirements.
      4.4.7.1. WRM assets should not be used solely to support ongoing rotational operations.
 136                                            AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


       4.4.7.2. Prior to using WRM, requesting organizations will make every effort to satisfy
       the requirement using alternative means of support.
       4.4.7.3. If still required, the requesting organization must follow procedures for indirect
       mission support IAW AFI 25-101 and applicable MAJCOM supplement.

Section 4C—Cargo Preparation

4.5. Cargo Preparation/Identification.
   4.5.1. General.
       4.5.1.1. This process ensures all equipment/cargo is properly identified, prepared, and
       documented (including appropriate customs documentation and diplomatic clearance)
       before marshaling (see Attachment 4 for equipment processing process flowcharts).
       4.5.1.2. This is a unit responsibility that is usually completed in the unit area.
       4.5.1.3. As early as possible, units will identify equipment/cargo tasked for deployment
       and start all documentation (particularly hazardous materials (HAZMAT)) required.
       4.5.1.4. All mobility/contingency cargo movement records (air or surface) will be
       prepared by the CDF and maintained by the Deployment and Distribution Flight IAW
       with DTR 4500.9, Parts II & III, AFMAN 24-204 (IP), AFI 24-203, and AFI 33-360.
       NOTE: Attachment 17 provides additional guidance for maintaining aircraft station files.
   4.5.2. Deployed Accountability.
       4.5.2.1. Before execution, UDMs, through the LRS Materiel Management Flight
       Customer Service and/or Vehicle Management Flight, will identify deployment
       equipment and ensure the assignment of the correct use codes (reference AFMAN 23-
       110, Vol. 2, Part 2, Chapter 3, Attachment 3A-1, Data Elements and Definitions) and
       UTCs.
       4.5.2.2. Upon receipt of tasking, the UDM or Vehicle Control Officer/NCO
       (VCO/VCNCO) will identify deploying equipment or vehicles, and appropriate support
       kits, and report them to the LRS Materiel Management Flight Customer Service and/or
       Vehicle Management Flight.
       4.5.2.3. LRS will prepare a deployed CA/CRL and will then update their systems.
   4.5.3. When preparing for deployments, units will refer to the squadron or shop LOGPLAN
   materiel list to ensure they have the required equipment.
       4.5.3.1. LOGPLAN materiel lists will be kept accurate and deploying equipment marked
       in advance (if possible).
       4.5.3.2. For cargo preparation, use LOGMOD to produce load and packing lists.
   4.5.4. Vehicles. Units will:
       4.5.4.1. Prepare OPLAN or AEF-tasked vehicles IAW AFI 24-302, Vehicle
       Management.Units will:
       4.5.4.2. End users are responsible for vehicle processing tasks for deployment.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                          137


       4.5.4.3. Ensure vehicles that require Limited Technical Inspections (LTI) for acceptance,
       shipping, disposition actions and repairs meet processing times and are placed in the
       proper condition prior to shipment. UDMs or VCOs/VCNCOs will schedule an LTI
       appointment with the LRS Vehicle Management Flight as soon as possible to ensure the
       LTI is completed in sufficient time to meet the LOGMOD Schedule cargo marshalling
       start time.
       4.5.4.4. Coordinate with LRS Vehicle Management Flight for deployability assessment
       and Temporary Mission Support Kits (when required) before processing assets through
       the CDF.
4.6. Hazardous Materials Identification/Documentation.
   4.6.1. Units will:
       4.6.1.1. Maintain and provide a current sample Shipper’s Declaration for Dangerous
       Goods form for each hazardous item
       4.6.1.2. Include a HAZMAT certification authorization letter signed by the unit
       commander or a designated representative, to the LRS/APS/AMS.
   4.6.2. Transportation HAZMAT specialists will physically inspect cargo to ensure Shipper’s
   Declaration of Dangerous Goods forms are prepared accurately.
   4.6.3. The LRS/APS/AMS will review the forms for accuracy.
   4.6.4. Sample Shippers Declarations will be kept by the unit to provide to the CDF as
   required.
   4.6.5. Ensure hazardous materials are prepared and ready for shipment:
       4.6.5.1. Prepare and move hazardous material shipments IAW AFMAN 24-204(IP) (49
       CFR for surface shipments) and MIL-STD-129P, DOD Standard Practice, Military
       Marking for Shipment and Storage.
       4.6.5.2. Ensure applicable Competent Authority Approvals (CAA), Department of
       Transportation (DOT) Special Permits, Certifications of Equivalency (COE), Air
       Transportation Test Loading Agency (ATTLA) certification, and packaging or
       compatibility waivers accompany shipments.
       4.6.5.3. Ensure classified or signature service hazardous materials are identified by using
       a DD Form 1387-2, Special Handling Data/Certification, in addition to a Shipper’s
       Declaration of Dangerous Goods.
       4.6.5.4. Ensure packaging, marking,        and documentation capability exists          for
       redeployment to home station.
       4.6.5.5. Ensure hazardous cargo information is located in the TCMD located in
       LOGMOD LOGPLAN files. Tasked units load hazardous cargo information via the
       Planning menu of LOGMOD.
4.7. Sensitive Cargo.
   4.7.1. To ensure classified cargo is prepared and ready for shipment, units will:
 138                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


       4.7.1.1. Handle and ship classified material IAW DOD 5200.1-R, Information Security
       Program Regulation, and AFI 31-401.
       4.7.1.2. All deploying units with classified material must appoint classified cargo
       couriers to accompany/receipt for classified materials.
       4.7.1.3. AFI 31-401 gives specific guidance on how to account for deployed classified
       material.
   4.7.2. To ensure arms, ammunition, and explosives are prepared and ready for shipment,
   units will:
       4.7.2.1. Ensure escort and bulk shipment criteria of arms, ammunition, and explosives
       (AA&E) for carrier load/off-load and base surface movements is accomplished IAW AFI
       24-203, Chapter 5.
       4.7.2.2. When using military ground transportation for movement off base to field
       locations, deployments, etc. refer to AFI 31-101 or contact the local Security Forces for
       procedures.
       4.7.2.3. Ensure accountability is accomplished IAW AFI 21-201.
4.8. Equipment/Cargo Documentation.
   4.8.1. Each increment of equipment/cargo must carry specific documentation IAW cargo
   preparation directives identified in the following paragraphs. Units must include these
   minimum forms of documentation/identification with each increment.
   4.8.2. Military Shipment Label (MSL).
       4.8.2.1. Each palletized load or non-palletized piece of cargo must have an authorized
       MSL and will be attached for air shipment IAW DTR 4500.9-R, Part III, and MIL-STD-
       129P.
       4.8.2.2. Use CMOS/GATES to produce MSLs to ensure the full use of ITV-capabilities
       throughout the transportation network.
       4.8.2.3. At a minimum, the following elements of information will be provided on the
       MSL:
          4.8.2.3.1. TCN (Transportation Control Number) with embedded ULN (up to the full
          seven digits).
          4.8.2.3.2. Origin (to include Stock Record Account Number/DOD Account Activity
          Code (SRAN/DODAAC)).
          4.8.2.3.3. APOE.
          4.8.2.3.4. APOD, Destination (to include SRAN/DODAAC).
          4.8.2.3.5. Cube.
          4.8.2.3.6. Dimensions.
          4.8.2.3.7. Weight.
          4.8.2.3.8. Unit POC.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        139


  4.8.3. Whenever possible MSLs should be produced from an automatic system so that linear
  or 2D barcodes are shown for the TCN, destination/consignee, and piece number blocks so
  automatic identification technology can be used to process unit move shipments through the
  terminals expeditiously.
  4.8.4. Temporary LOGMOD deployment shipping placards will be used by UDMs for
  shipment/equipment identification purposes from the deploying unit to the CDF to facilitate
  the in-check process for deployments, exercises, and unit moves. Deploying force/owning
  unit is required to produce and place pallet placards on two adjacent sides of a pallet IAW
  DTR 4500.9-R, Part III.
     4.8.4.1. UDMs may produce manual DD Form 1387s in place of LOGMOD placards
     during periods of LOGMOD inoperability.
     4.8.4.2. Currently LOGMOD deployment shipping placards do not meet DTR
     requirements (bar coding) and therefore cannot be used for actual deployments, exercises,
     or unit moves.
  4.8.5. The CDF will produce a CMOS/GATES MSL after the joint inspection (JI) to ensure
  accurate weight and dimensional data.
         4.8.5.1. If CMOS/GATES is not available to produce authorized MSLs, then the
         CDF/units will manually complete a DD Form 1387 IAW DTR 4500.9-R, Part III,
         MIL-STD-129P and/or AFI 24-203, utilizing the Logistics Web Forms Processor
         (LWFP): https://lsotools.wpafb.af.mil.
         4.8.5.2. Units are responsible for producing an automated or manual load and
         packing lists for all deploying UTC cargo (e.g. palletized, rolling-stock, hand-carried
         and/or floor-loaded) IAW the LOGMOD Schedule.
         4.8.5.3. If a DD Form 1387 is utilized, ensure blocks 1, 9, and 16 are legible for
         down line stations to update the advance movement data file and produce updated
         automated MSLs with bar codes, if capable.
         4.8.5.4. CDF/units will place labels in a waterproof envelope and securely attach the
         envelope to the deploying increment.
         4.8.5.5. If LWFP is used, users will generate TCMDs and MSLs for shippers. This
         web-based system includes electronic versions of DD Form 1384s and DD Form
         1387s. The system also includes data validation for all shipment types and sends
         advanced warning to POEs.
  4.8.6. Load and Packing Lists.
     4.8.6.1. LOGMOD is the source system for generating Deployment Cargo Load and
     Packing lists.
     4.8.6.2. If LOGMOD is not available or functional for the purpose of generating these
     products, an AF Form 2518, Deployment Packing List, will be manually generated (see
     Attachment 14).
     4.8.6.3. Items loaded onto increments (containers onto pallets or rolling-stock) will be
     marked/stenciled in a waterproof manner. Minimum markings will consist of:
140                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


         4.8.6.3.1. Line One: UTC/Unit of assignment (e.g. 890 FS).
         4.8.6.3.2. Line Two: Deployment echelon/Increment number/Item number (e.g. C1-
         1004-01).
         4.8.6.3.3. Apply packing/shipping markings and labels IAW equipment technical
         orders. Additional unit markings are authorized.
      4.8.6.4. Load and Packing lists must be accurate and be attached in weatherproof pouch
      with the pallet/container.
      4.8.6.5. Accurate load and packing lists are critical to ensure unit equipment is not
      delayed by customs at entry into other countries.
      4.8.6.6. Failure by units to create accurate documentation can delay equipment arrival to
      the beddown location and seriously affect the mission.
      4.8.6.7. Pen and ink changes are authorized.
      4.8.6.8. All containers (except as otherwise identified herein) will have a LOGMOD
      packing list affixed with detailed list of all suffixed items within the container.
      4.8.6.9. When a suffixed item in the container is a container itself with more than one
      item, the inside container will additionally have an AF Form 2518 attached.
      4.8.6.10. Locally developed electronic forms are authorized if they include, as a
      minimum, the same data fields as the AF Form 2518.
      4.8.6.11. Medical units will use Defense Medical Logistics Standard Support (DMLSS)
      packing lists and logistics readiness units may use SBSS listings (R-43, etc.) for Mobility
      Readiness Spares Package (MRSP) packing lists.
      4.8.6.12. Civil Engineer units will use Equipment and Supply Listing (ESL).
         4.8.6.12.1. Standard configuration for equipment is identified in the ESL.         The
         contents of individual kits are further defined in the ESL.
         4.8.6.12.2. Printed copies of pertinent ESL information will be placed on or within
         individual kits.
      4.8.6.13. Units will not use manual Deployment Load and Packing lists except under the
      most unusual of circumstances (i.e. LOGMOD system failure).
      4.8.6.14. The packing list, (ESL for CE only), will contain the contents (suffix items) for
      items identified as containers and include NSN, nomenclature, tasked quantities,
      hazard/special handling indicator codes, sensitive/controlled items, and ASCs of suffix
      items. The following exceptions apply:
         4.8.6.14.1. Do not list contents for MRSP except those that are hazardous or Use
         Code “A” (Allowance Standard asset).
         4.8.6.14.2. Do not list the contents for Consolidated Tool Kits (CTKs) except those
         that are hazardous or Use Code “A.”
         4.8.6.14.3. Do not list miscellaneous administrative supplies (pens, pencils, paper,
         etc.) except those that are hazardous or Use Code “A”.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                             141


          4.8.6.14.4. Do not list medical supplies except those that are hazardous or Use Code
          “A” (EXCEPTION: Medical UTCs will list medical supplies).
          4.8.6.14.5. Do not list individual CE kits except those that are hazardous or Use Code
          “A”.
       4.8.6.15. LOGMOD is not designed for making frequent changes to fluctuating
       quantities of such expendables as pencils, forms, hand tools, or narcotics.
       4.8.6.16. Inventory and Deployment Packing lists for CTKs and miscellaneous
       administrative supplies are the responsibilities of the owning unit.
       4.8.6.17. Units will maintain shoring material for the unit’s equipment and identify this
       material within their load and packing lists to account for the additional weight of this
       material.
   4.8.7. Pallet Identifiers (DD Form 2775/automated equivalents). Deploying force and/or
   owning unit is only required to produce and place the pallet identifiers on two adjacent sides
   of a pallet IAW DTR4500.9-R, Part III when multiple TCNs are consolidated on a pallet,
   ISU, etc. for shipment. A pallet identifier is optional for shipments containing a single TCN
   as the MSL has all data related to the shipment.
   4.8.8. Deployment Transportation Control Number (TCN).
       4.8.8.1. If LOGMOD is not operational, the deployment TCN can be manually
       constructed by following instructions in DTR 4500.9-R, Part III, Appendix H.
       4.8.8.2. The TCN will include the ULN (use full seven-digit ULN when fragmented),
       Deployment echelon, and increment number (automatically generated in LOGMOD
       Schedule module).
   4.8.9. For contingency exercises and deployments, include:
       4.8.9.1. DD Form 1387-2, Special Handling Data/Certification (for cargo requiring any
       special handling instructions e.g. classified, sensitive, keep away from magnetized
       material, etc)
       4.8.9.2. Commercial bills of lading; and a truck manifest (TCMD data.
       4.8.9.3. DD Form 1385, Cargo Manifest, or equivalent), prepared by the transportation
       function or deploying unit, as appropriate.
       4.8.9.4. Cargo that is both sensitive and hazardous (such as small arms ammunition)
       requires a Shipper's Declaration for Dangerous Goods and a completed DD Form 1387-2.
       4.8.9.5. During an actual deployment or contingency, the deploying unit must complete
       an original Shipper's Declaration for Dangerous Goods to certify all hazardous cargo (see
       AFMAN 24-204[I] for more details).
       4.8.9.6. DELETED
4.9. Pallet Build-up.
   4.9.1. Pallet profile for all aircraft (e.g. C-130, KC-10, and Civil Reserve Airlift Fleet (CRAF))
   will be considered when preparing cargo pallets. This may significantly reduce the possibility of
 142                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


   further modifications at the time of actual loading. Use the checklist in DTR 4500.9-R, Part III,
   Appendix O: http://www.transcom.mil/j5/pt/dtrpart3/dtr_part_iii_app_o.pdf.
   4.9.2. Palletize Baggage.
       4.9.2.1. For planning purposes, baggage will be palletized for all C-5 aircraft, 10 or more
       passengers on a KC-10 aircraft, and 20 or more passengers on all other airframes.
       4.9.2.2. C-17 baggage pallets will be loaded in the rear of the aircraft while KC-10 and
       KC-135 baggage pallets will be loaded towards the nose in order to expedite the
       download at the final destination.
       4.9.2.3. Baggage pallets will follow the same height and contour restrictions as other
       pallets.
       4.9.2.4. When 20 or more passengers are on a chalk, load planners must account for
       baggage pallets on the pre-load plan by using canned weights/heights (2500lbs/45) and
       the LOGMOD Scheduler will account for pallets in the LOGMOD schedule remarks
       section.
   4.9.3. Units deploying or redeploying are responsible for all cargo preparation to include
   providing special equipment operators, venting liquid oxygen (LOX) carts, providing de-icer
   drivers, etc. NOTE: Deploying units are required to install appropriate vent kit to the
   equipment. Aircraft maintenance will then connect to aircraft venting system.
   4.9.4. Any required shoring/dunnage will be provided by the unit and must be deployed with
   its associated equipment/pallet.
       4.9.4.1. Pallet dunnage will always accompany 463L pallets during movement.
       4.9.4.2. The following are general movement characteristics for pallet dunnage:
          4.9.4.2.1. Length: 88 inches.
          4.9.4.2.2. Width/height: 3 inches.
          4.9.4.2.3. Quantity: 3 each.
       4.9.4.3. Dunnage NSN information can be obtained from the IDO, Transportation
       Management personnel, AFI 10-401, or by using the Federal Logistics (FEDLOG)
       system.
4.10. Pre-deployment Cargo Movement.
   4.10.1. Cargo movement requirements/responsibilities will be documented in the local IDP.
   4.10.2. Deploying units will deliver all UTC cargo (e.g. palletized, rolling-stock, hand-
   carried, and/or floor-loaded) to the CDF in-check area as required by the LOGMOD
   Schedule.
   4.10.3. Units must arrange movement of cargo well in advance of required LOGMOD
   Schedule processing times to ensure on-time processing and availability of transportation
   assets.
       4.10.3.1. If required, units should first contact the DCC Transportation Representative.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                       143


      4.10.3.2. If required, and the DCC has not been activated, the unit should contact LRS
      Vehicle Management Flight to request support moving non-rolling stock cargo.
   4.10.4. Deploying non-local AF and non-AF units will:
      4.10.4.1. Provide a CD-ROM in electronic format (CMOS/GATES/Transportation
      Coordinators-Automated Information for Movements System II (TC-AIMS II), or new
      generation system) containing outbound air cargo information to the CDF, Aircraft
      Services, or Cargo Processing Section IAW published times contained in local
      LOGMOD Schedule to expedite processing of cargo into the airlift system.
      4.10.4.2. Provide approved electronic media with deploying passenger data to the PDF
      for input into IDS systems (CMOS/GATES) for manifest preparation, (Reference AFI
      24-203 for further guidance).
      4.10.4.3. DELETED
          4.10.4.3.1. DELETED
             4.10.4.3.1.1. DELETED
             4.10.4.3.1.2. DELETED
4.11. Cargo Processing.
   4.11.1. The CDF will:
      4.11.1.1. Be a controlled area and have the capability to weigh and measure equipment.
      EXCEPTION: For locations that have contracted Air Terminal Ground Handling
      Services (ATGHS), the IDP will capture these unique service contract relationships for
      Air Terminal Operations, JI and aircraft loading. Further, a copy will be sent the
      MAJCOM/A4s for transparency and consolidation.
      4.11.1.2. Determine and comply with any special requirements or procedures that will be
      required to inspect explosives (e.g. Explosive Ordnance Disposal (EOD)/SF loads usually
      require a separate holding area or “hot cargo pad” for meeting all safety requirements).
      4.11.1.3. Identify personnel to perform any “mobile” in-check requirements and ensure
      enough materials are available.
      4.11.1.4. Coordinate commercial surface movement through the LRS/Deployment and
      Distribution Flight and LRS Deployment & Distribution Flight Commander. NOTE: For
      AMC bases with an APS, the CDF is the responsibility of the APS.
      4.11.1.5. Make augmentees aware of hazards such as LOX carts and explosives.
      4.11.1.6. In-check, weigh and measure hand-carried and/or floor-loaded UTC cargo in
      the same manner as palletized or rolling-stock cargo. Upon completion of cargo
      processing and deemed safe, hand-carried cargo will be released to the deploying unit
      representative (e.g. cargo courier) for transportation loading IAW the LOGMOD
      Schedule.
   4.11.2. Cargo Marshaling.
      4.11.2.1. Marshaling is the orderly assembly of cargo (in load plan sequence by chalk, in
      preparation for JI) to a location called the staging or call forward area.
144                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      4.11.2.2. Identify these locations as sterile areas to ensure the equipment is not
      “tampered” with (adding or deleting pieces).
      4.11.2.3. The CDF controls entry into the marshaling yard.
      4.11.2.4. Identify these areas in the IDP.
  4.11.3. Joint Inspection (JI) of Cargo.
      4.11.3.1. JI is the final inspection with the owning unit and the joint inspector (or
      loadmaster, if necessary) before the load is accepted.
      4.11.3.2. The JI is accomplished IAW DTR 4500.9-R, Part III.
      4.11.3.3. If an item is not properly prepared or documentation is incorrect, it will be
      placed in the frustrated cargo area and the CDF OIC/NCOICs are notified immediately so
      that corrective actions will be taken.
      4.11.3.4. Ensure keys and combinations accompany cargo to in-check. Lack of keys or
      combinations will cause cargo to be frustrated.
      4.11.3.5. After the JI process is complete, equipment is ready for loading. In the event of
      discrepancies discovered after the JI is complete, ensure the CDF OIC/NCOIC is
      immediately notified to ensure an experienced unit representative is dispatched to remedy
      the discrepancy.
      4.11.3.6. Each unit will also have a representative (increment monitor) accompany the
      equipment to the in-check area that is familiar with the increment cargo to resolve
      discrepancies or at least communicate requirements to appropriate unit personnel until
      their cargo clears the JI. The tasked unit must have a team ready (quick-fix team) to
      immediately respond to resolve any discrepancies frustrating the cargo.
  4.11.4. Frustrated Cargo.
      4.11.4.1. Frustrated cargo is cargo that failed the CDF inspection at the in-check area,
      joint inspection, or any place after arriving the CDF and prior to loading the aircraft.
      4.11.4.2. Frustrated cargo will be set aside in a frustrated cargo area (within the CDF)
      until the owning unit replaces and/or fixes the assets.
      4.11.4.3. CDF will notify the DCC immediately of all frustrated cargo, so proper
      action(s) can be taken to resolve problems.
      4.11.4.4. Cargo frustration times are tracked to ensure issues are corrected as quickly as
      possible.
      4.11.4.5. Reliable communications between the DCC, CDF, and UDMs (to include
      quick-fix teams) is critical because failure to fix a frustrated piece of cargo in a timely
      manner can delay an entire deployment schedule and affect a unit’s overall capability.
      4.11.4.6. The IDP will identify a frustrated cargo holding area in the CDF for increments
      having discrepancies (documentation or improper preparation).
  4.11.5. Cargo Manifesting.
      4.11.5.1. Cargo manifests will be prepared for each chalk to ensure ITV from point of
      origin to final destination.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                         145


          4.11.5.1.1. Individuals assigned to this function will be extremely knowledgeable of
          the requirements of DTR 4500.9-R, Part II and AFI 24-203.
          4.11.5.1.2. Cargo load plans cannot be used as cargo manifests. Hand-carried and/or
          floor-loaded UTC cargo will be manifested in the same manner as palletized or
          rolling-stock cargo.
      4.11.5.2. CMOS or GATES will be used to generate the cargo manifest.
          4.11.5.2.1. If CMOS/GATES is not available to produce the cargo manifest, a DD
          Form 1385, Cargo Manifest, is used.
          4.11.5.2.2. Fax or email DD Form 1385 to AMC Data Processing Center
          (ORG.AMCA4-70@us.af.mil) for ITV purposes.
          4.11.5.2.3. UDMs are required to ensure TCMD data (e.g. transportation trailer data
          for HAZMAT, sensitive, classified, etc.) is accurate and meets DTR 4500.9-R, Part
          III requirements, and loaded in LOGMOD. For assistance with TCMD data,
          LRS/APS/AMS transportation specialists are the primary points of contact at the
          installation/wing level.
          4.11.5.2.4. Cargo information will transfer from LOGMOD to CMOS/GATES to
          IGC for ITV.
          4.11.5.2.5. CMOS/GATES manifest printout will accompany manifested cargo.

Section 4D—Load Plan Preparation

4.12. Load Plan Preparation.
   4.12.1. Load planners will use load planning IDS systems to prepare load plans. However,
   proficiency in using manual load planning methods must be maintained in the event the load
   planning system is not available.
   4.12.2. Pre- or initial load plans will be developed simultaneously with the LOGMOD
   Schedule to ensure proper sequencing of equipment and passengers based on TPFDD timing,
