   UTC priority flow, en route support, and force/equipment mix needed in order to achieve
   initial operating capability at the beddown location as soon as possible.
   4.12.3. Coordinate with the DCC before moving a piece of equipment/cargo from one load
   to another to ensure the move will not affect either en route support or operations at the
   beddown location.
   4.12.4. Ensure that cargo, personnel, aircraft, and load plan destinations are the same. Units
   will coordinate with logistics planners to ensure prioritization of cargo to meet the mission
   requirements at the deployed location.
   4.12.5. Avoid placing all critical initial operating support equipment and personnel on the
   same aircraft/mode of transportation to prevent loss of capability if the mode is delayed or
   destroyed.
   4.12.6. Increments within a single UTC that is too small to be palletized individually will be
   combined with other increments into the same UTC to reduce airlift requirements.
146                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      4.12.6.1. When combined, the unit will notify and coordinate with the DCC to designate
      a lead POC for processing the equipment.
      4.12.6.2. The DCC Scheduler will annotate the combined increments in the LOGMOD
      Schedule Remarks Field and any coordinating modifications with the load planners.
      4.12.6.3. Increments from different UTCs should not be combined unless ITV is
      achievable. If UTCs must be combined into single increments in LOGMOD, ITV will
      not be lost if the following steps are followed:
         4.12.6.3.1. Use the Chalk Remarks block on the LOGMOD Schedule, for the
         specified chalk, to reflect combined UTC Increments.
         4.12.6.3.2. Use the Chalk Remarks block to identify the lead increment (i.e. TCN)
         for all of the increments that have been combined and what deploying unit is overall
         responsible for packaging and generating deployment products for that lead
         increment.
         4.12.6.3.3. CMOS/GATES operators will use the LOGMOD Schedule Chalk
         Remarks field, for the specified chalk, to consolidate the combined UTC increments
         under a tab pallet header (capped pallet).
         4.12.6.3.4. Even though CMOS/GATES will reflect a lead TCN, all of the combined
         increments (i.e. subsidiary TCNs) will be associated to the lead TCN and will be
         visible in IGC.
         4.12.6.3.5. When physically combining increments of cargo, copies of the load lists,
         for each of the increments that are being combined, must be placed on the outside of
         the lead Increment. This allows CDF personnel to have access to all load list
         information at the time of JI/In-check.
         4.12.6.3.6. The lead increment load list will be placed on the outside of the increment
         packing envelope as to be the first document pulled by the CDF in-checker. This lead
         increment load list must be annotated to reflect the overall combined increment
         weights and dimensions. Pen and ink changes are authorized.
         4.12.6.3.7. The same procedures apply for Deployment Shipping Placards for
         combined increments.
  4.12.7. Load Plan Distribution.
      4.12.7.1. Once the final load plans are accomplished, load planners ensure all essential
      players receive them. The following people and agencies will receive the following
      number of copies of load plans:
         4.12.7.1.1. Aircraft commander (1-original).
         4.12.7.1.2. Load team chief (1).
         4.12.7.1.3. DCC (1).
         4.12.7.1.4. Station file copy (1).
         4.12.7.1.5. RAMPCO (1), if applicable.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                           147


      4.12.7.2. The load plan is NOT the same as the cargo manifest. The Cargo Manifest
      (DD Form 1385) or its automated equivalent is the official manifest IAW DTR 4500.9-R,
      Part II.

Section 4E—Aircraft/Cargo Loading

4.13. Aircraft/Cargo Loading.
   4.13.1. The Cargo Deployment Function. Loads unit equipment and baggage. For specific
   guidance on how to load aircraft, consult DTR 4500.9-R, Part III, and the applicable aircraft -
   9 Technical Order (TO).
      4.13.1.1. Load team chiefs will ensure all team members are familiar with the load plan
      and everyone on the team understands their specific responsibilities. Load team chiefs
      will check with the RAMPCO or OIC/NCOIC of the CDF if a load plan is not available
      at least 45 minutes before LOGMOD Schedule load start time. NOTE: Report load start
      and completion times to the DCC immediately.
      4.13.1.2. All cargo will be ready to load NLT 30 minutes before scheduled load start
      time or as spelled out in the IDP.
      4.13.1.3. Each load team will consist of a team chief and at least three handlers or
      operators. At the beginning of the shift, the team chief will conduct a safety briefing
      covering at least the following:
          4.13.1.3.1. Safe operation of MHE (e.g. speed limits, use of chocks, and need for
          spotters).
          4.13.1.3.2. Safe cargo handling (pallets pushed – not pulled, etc.).
          4.13.1.3.3. Safety equipment for all load team members, e.g. safety-toed work boots,
          gloves, reflective gear, light wands for hours of darkness, etc.
          4.13.1.3.4. Safety procedures during Engine-Running On/Offloads (EROs) and
          concurrent refueling (if applicable). NOTE: See T.O. 00-25-172, Ground Servicing
          of Aircraft & Static Grounding/Bonding, for more details on concurrent servicing
          operations.
      4.13.1.4. The deploying unit will furnish drivers for specialized equipment/vehicles (e.g.
      Rescue all-terrain transports (RATTs), all-terrain vehicles (ATVs), M-series vehicles,
      etc.). These drivers will load specialized equipment under the supervision of the
      loadmaster.
      4.13.1.5. The load team chief will follow safe loading procedures at all times, as well as
      ensure:
          4.13.1.5.1. Cargo is identified and segregated into loads according to the LOGMOD
          Schedule.
          4.13.1.5.2. The team has sufficient serviceable MHE to perform loading operations.
          4.13.1.5.3. The team loads the aircraft or vehicle according to the final load plan or at
          the direction of the aircraft commander or designated representative.
 148                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


          4.13.1.5.4. Cargo is visually checked for obvious leaks and discrepancies before
          loading. Notify the RAMPCO of any problems so corrective action can be taken.
          4.13.1.5.5. The loadmaster is briefed on the load configuration and special loading
          requirements. Have the team load the aircraft under the loadmaster's supervision.
          4.13.1.5.6. Cargo is properly loaded onto trucks with adequate tie-down, as directed
          by the vehicle operator. All items planned for the truck are loaded.
   4.13.2. Aircraft Loadmaster Briefing. The RAMPCO or load team chief will deliver
   deployment manifests and brief the Aircraft Loadmaster on the specifics of the load to
   include all hazardous material before loading.
   4.13.3. Ramp Coordinator (RAMPCO).
       4.13.3.1. Oversees and coordinates all aircraft and vehicle loading operations as outlined
       in the LOGMOD Schedule and works closely with the CDF and PDF to ensure all facets
       of airlift support are met. The RAMPCO acts as the eyes and ears of the CDF and,
       therefore, must closely monitor all aircraft ground handling operations while maintaining
       constant communication with the CDF and/or Air Terminal Operations Center (ATOC).
       4.13.3.2. Will carefully monitor their assigned loads from marshaling complete time
       until the aircraft or truck departs.
       4.13.3.3. At a minimum, visually check their load for any obvious discrepancies (leaks,
       missing placards, weights, etc.) prior to aircraft loading. In addition, they will be familiar
       with all the characteristics of the load (HAZMAT, documentation requirements, required
       waivers, etc.).

Section 4F—Intransit Visibility

4.14. In-Transit Visibility (ITV).
   4.14.1. Use of AF automated systems that comprise the IDS to deploy AF forces is
   mandatory. IDS components include LOGMOD, DCAPES, CMOS, GATES and ICODES.
   To achieve deployment ITV, pass cargo and passenger deployment files from LOGMOD and
   DCAPES (or other Service systems) to CMOS or GATES, which, in turn, pass movement
   data to IGC. Further guidance on the use of CMOS can be found in AFI 24-203, Chapter 15,
   and online at https://www.gunter.af.mil/il/ilr/ilrc.
   4.14.2. The IDO ensures cargo and passenger data is accurately entered into IDS
   components to maintain ITV within established time frames. Without exception, valid and
   full 7-character (if fragmented) ULNs from the applicable CCDR’s TPFDD are required for
   deployment cargo and personnel in order to relate these resources back to the force
   requirements in the TPFDD. Fictitiously entered ULNs will prevent cross-referencing this
   data back to the TPFDD (AFI 24-203, Chapter 18). Ensure CMOS/GATES operators
   transmit passenger and cargo manifest information to IGC NLT one hour after chalk
   departure for contingency and unit move deployments.
   4.14.3. ITV provides visibility of deploying cargo and personnel from home station, or
   origin, to destination.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                         149


     4.14.3.1. Supported/Supporting commanders use ITV to track the flow of capabilities
     and critical assets (e.g. munitions) from origin into an area of operations (AO).
     4.14.3.2. Transportation closure, as indicated by ITV, is critical as a gauge to predict
     when capabilities are in place to commence operations.
     4.14.3.3. Force closure cannot be ascertained through ITV alone. Only the deployed
     commander can declare force closure and operational capability (i.e. the force is ready to
     commence operations).
  4.14.4. IDS must be used to support the deployment process and enable/achieve ITV.
  CMOS/GATES houses aircraft manifest information; therefore, CD-ROMs will no longer be
  required to accompany missions to facilitate re-manifesting or continuation of ITV at en
  route and trans-load locations.
     4.14.4.1. CMOS/GATES users must pass the movement data, with valid ULNs, to IGC.
     4.14.4.2. CMOS training material is available via: https://www.gunter.af.mil/il/ilr/ilrc
     and GATES training material is available via: https://afkm.wpafb.af.mil/gates.
  4.14.5. Radio Frequency Identification (RFID) Tags.
     4.14.5.1. RFID tags are required for deploying cargo.
     4.14.5.2. The LRS designated transportation function will burn unit tags using shipment
     data imported to CMOS (GATES for CONUS AMC strategic aerial ports) from
     LOGMOD and ensure tags are attached to all end items before aircraft loading
     commences.
     4.14.5.3. IAW AFI 24-203, Deployment and Distribution Flights will order and maintain
     sufficient tags to support local exercise requirements as determined by the IDO.
         4.14.5.3.1. Tags will be ordered through base supply.
         4.14.5.3.2. The current tag is stock listed as Model 654 with 128KB RAM (NSN
         6350-01-532-1998); however, units will validate the current tag model/NSN with
         their respective MAJCOMs prior to ordering.
         4.14.5.3.3. Installations will order tags to support unit deployments from the central
         repository maintained by the AF automatic information technology (AIT) program
         management office (PMO) using the following procedures:
         4.14.5.3.4. Determine total tag requirement for deployments.
         4.14.5.3.5. Order tags no earlier than 45 calendar days prior to the projected
         deployment date. Request tags from 403 SCMS/GUEA, DSN: 787-7297, and/or
         Commercial: (937) 257-7297.
     4.14.5.4. Account for RFID tags during deployment planning and execution.
     4.14.5.5. Ensure adequate time is built into the LOGMOD Schedule to allow tags to be
     properly affixed to deploying cargo at the CDF.
     4.14.5.6. Installations/wings will establish local procedures to receive, store and maintain
     tags received at origin.
 150                                        AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


                                         Chapter 5

                      DEPLOYMENT EXECUTION (PERSONNEL)

Section 5A—General.

5.1. General.
   5.1.1. This chapter provides information concerning the processing of personnel, for pre-
   planning and execution, and the processing activities supporting the personnel deployment
   process.
   5.1.2. The DRMD; generated by DCAPES, dictates the personnel taskings the unit must be
   prepared to fill for a deployment and is an essential element of the Personnel and Manpower
   communities supporting total force accountability.

Section 5B—Personnel Deployment Planning/Execution

5.2. Personnel Authorizations.
   5.2.1. Postured UTCs will only be filled with authorizations from one unit (i.e. not
   fragmented). See AFI 10-401, Chapter 4, for exceptions and waiver procedures.
   5.2.2. Personnel in deployable UTCs must be trained and equipped, or have access to
   equipment, to maintain UTC capability. NOTE: ART must be updated to reflect status of
   personnel and equipment for each standard deployable UTC IAW AFI 10-244. This includes
   UTCs identified for home station or in-place UTCs.
   5.2.3. Personnel will be assigned to postured UTCs IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 7.
       5.2.3.1. DELETED
       5.2.3.2. DELETED
5.3. AF Personnel Deployment Planning/Execution Concept.
   5.3.1. AF unit deployments normally occur after a Movement Day (C-Day) is established.
       5.3.1.1. AMC’s Global Mobility Task Force as well as some other forces may move well
       before C-Day.
       5.3.1.2. Since planning assumptions, response options, and mobilization timing vary
       depending on the execution scenario, units may not move as a single UTC entity.
       5.3.1.3. Transportation constraints, reception capabilities and operational concepts
       dictate the final closure rate of the deploying force to the destination.
   5.3.2. Deployment Tasking Requirements.
       5.3.2.1. The DRMD provides the MAJCOM, supported component headquarters and
       wings the consolidated UTC personnel taskings for a particular deployment supporting
       ROMO and exercises requirements.
       5.3.2.2. AFI 36-3802 gives specific details on the data elements of the DRMD.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                     151


   5.3.3. Deployment Manning Requirements (DMR) will be transmitted to the base from the
   supported component command through the owning MAJCOM.
      5.3.3.1. MAJCOM FAMs will ensure IDRCs are informed of wing AEF sourcing
      utilizing DCAPES TNT.
      5.3.3.2. For ANG Wings, the IPR is responsible for the wing AEF sourcing and
      verification process.
      5.3.3.3. The DMR is the (space) to the personnel (face) that is generated to complete a
      DRMD.
   5.3.4. The DRMD has nine key and essential pieces of personnel deployment tasking
   information:
      5.3.4.1. PID.
      5.3.4.2. ULN, ULN position number.
      5.3.4.3. Position number suffix.
      5.3.4.4. AFSC.
      5.3.4.5. Unique qualifications (e.g. line remarks).
      5.3.4.6. Tasked PAS.
      5.3.4.7. RDD.
      5.3.4.8. Duty Location (DLOC).
      5.3.4.9. Attached PAS.
   5.3.5. DRMDs will be transmitted to the base from the MAJCOM AEF Cell using DCAPES
   TNT to the sourced installation/wing’s IDRC/DCC.
      5.3.5.1. The baseline process is that the OPLAN requirements are loaded in DCAPES.
      Before exporting plan data from DCAPES for input into other parts of the IDS system,
      the DCAPES operator uses published declassification procedures and software to ensure
      only unclassified data is passed from the classified system.
      5.3.5.2. The IDRC and tasked units review the key and essential pieces of the personnel
      deployment tasking and determine the proper course of actions (e.g. activating the wing
      deployment process).
      5.3.5.3. Tailoring and modifying the DRMD is managed IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter 10
      and AFI 38-205. Once this is complete, the unit must assign personnel to support the
      requirement. The UTC identifies the specific requirements including the AFSC, SEIs,
      security clearances, and grade needed by personnel selected to fulfill the tasking.
5.4. Matching (Assigning) Personnel to Requirements.
   5.4.1. Commanders will:
      5.4.1.1. Ensure personnel have their affairs in order.
      5.4.1.2. Have an AFDF which contains required deployment documentation.
      5.4.1.3. Ensure AFDFs are on file and maintained by the UDM.
152                                        AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


  5.4.2. IDRC Personnel and Manpower representative(s) will identify requirements by unit in
  order to facilitate distribution to the appropriate UDMs for fill actions. After all the
  requirements are received and reviewed, they will be made available to the tasked units.
  5.4.3. The unit is responsible for assigning a name for each requirement on the DRMD NLT
  the time required by AF guidance or as dictated by the IDO in order to meet the LOGMOD
  Schedule. (See Attachment 4 for flowchart of personnel processing process)
  5.4.4. Before an individual can be deployed, he or she must meet the training and
  deployment eligibility requirements according to this instruction, AFI 36-2110, and the UTC
  MISCAP statement.
  5.4.5. The MilPDS has a series of business rules identifying to unit commanders
  questionable deployment eligibility called DAV codes.
      5.4.5.1. Some DAV codes place a person into a questionable deployment availability
      status.
      5.4.5.2. Attachment 2 of this instruction explains all DAV codes affecting the
      deployment process.
  5.4.6. The IDRC and PDF will:
      5.4.6.1. Advise commanders when personnel are ineligible for deployment according to
      the governing directives.
      5.4.6.2. Ensure documentation is correct on personnel with waiverable DAV and duty
      status codes.
      5.4.6.3. Ensure DAV Code waiver requests are submitted to the appropriate policy
      owner or authority; i.e. legal, medical, personnel, etc.
      5.4.6.4. The use of IDS helps commanders in the unit deployment selection process by
      automating eligibility and waiver status of personnel.
  5.4.7. LOGMOD works with a Personnel file that is a snapshot in time of MilPDS, so some
  DAV/duty status codes might not apply. In these instances, close coordination between the
  unit and IPR/PDF must occur to ensure data systems reflect the proper status.
  5.4.8. Immediately upon receipt of the tasking, the UDM will notify the unit commander and
  accomplish the following:
      5.4.8.1. When a tasking is received by a unit, if the SSN is not filled in, then the
      commander identifies, tasks, and notifies the UDM with the name/SSN of deploying
      personnel.
      5.4.8.2. If the tasking is a non-unit postured UTC, the UDM will solicit names from the
      section/flight chief(s) and submit the name(s) for commander approval.
         5.4.8.2.1. Line and command remarks still must be met.
         5.4.8.2.2. UDMs will review AFDFs and other data sources to ensure selected
         personnel meet all requirements.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        153


         5.4.8.2.3. UDMs will recommend selected personnel to fill taskings who have not
         completed all necessary requirements, if these requirements can be accomplished
         prior to the deployment.
  5.4.9. If the unit has to shortfall any positions, submit shortfall IAW AFI 10-401, Chapter
  10.
     5.4.9.1. Even though units assess a UTC as “Green” in ART, line remarks may require
     capability beyond the unit’s capacity to fill either due to non-availability of assets with
     specific line remarks or due to other competing requirements.
     5.4.9.2. Prior to submitting a reclama, the tasked commander may be required to submit
     a waiver request IAW specific instructions in AFI's 10-401 and 36-3802.
     5.4.9.3. DELETED
     5.4.9.4. The tasked commander must keep the MAJCOM FAMs informed of all waiver
     requests, to include the final decision of the deployed commander. Listing of all personnel
     readiness POCs can be obtained at https://aef.afpc.randolph.af.mil/persco.aspx.
  5.4.10. The UDM will post the selected deploying individual(s) info (name and SSN) into
  LOGMOD or the official tasking memorandum and provide to the IDRC/DCC for tasking
  fill.
     5.4.10.1. UDMs must provide names to fill taskings, or shortfall the tasking(s) to the
     IDRC/DCC IAW timelines prescribed in AFI 10-401, Chapter 10.
     5.4.10.2. IDRC/IPR representatives will update DCAPES within timelines prescribed in
     AFI 36-3802 to show name fill and projected departure data.
     5.4.10.3. These updates support transparency in providing all echelons advance
     notification of projected arrivals and the expected delivery date.
  5.4.11. The unit commander/UDM will ensure in-person (i.e. face-to-face or phone)
  notification of tasking to Airmen within (4) duty days of tasking receipt by
  UDM/Commander. The notification may be done by the commander, UDM, or a supervisor.
  This timing will probably be compressed during crisis action or short notice taskings.
     5.4.11.1. Within (5) duty days of notification of tasking (rotational operations), the
     member will:
     5.4.11.2. Report to the UDM with their CAC for a comprehensive review of the entire
     AFDF. NOTE: This timing will probably be compressed during crisis action or short
     notice taskings.
     5.4.11.3. The UDM will notify the member of any scheduled training/appointments
     required for the tasking, review all applicable reporting instructions (CST, CAST, ECAC,
     APOE, AOR and Location specific) with the member, ensure FCG requirements are met
     or initiated and identify any adverse medical conditions that will prevent the member
     from deploying.
     5.4.11.4. Not earlier than (NET) 30-days prior to PDF processing, or as directed by the
     Commander, the UDM will:
154                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


         5.4.11.4.1. Initiate a final review of readiness status with the member prior to
         scheduling the member’s final out-processing appointment with the IPR.
         5.4.11.4.2. At the final out-processing appointment, the UDM will again review all
         applicable reporting instructions (CST, CAST, ECAC, APOE, AOR and location
         specific), FCG and medical readiness requirements (such as additional vaccinations)
         with the member.
         5.4.11.4.3. UDMs will brief deploying Airmen on the requirement to deploy with all
         mandatory items as outlined in the applicable Reporting/Routing Instructions and that
         failure to do so is a violation of Article 92 of the Uniform Code of Military Justice
         (UCMJ).
         5.4.11.4.4. Upon completion of the briefing, the UDM(s) and deploying individual(s)
         will complete, sign and date an AF Form 4005.
         5.4.11.4.5. A Prohibitive Items briefing will be conducted and documented in a
         signed and dated memorandum.
  5.4.12. If known, the UDM will inform the Airman of reporting times as reflected in the
  LOGMOD Schedule or TPFDD. NOTE: UDMs will schedule individuals for individual
  equipment and weapons requirements pickup through the LRS IPE or provide times they
  may do so on their own.
  5.4.13. The UDM will ensure deploying unit member(s) initiate the pre-deployment medical
  clearance process with PH/FHM 120-days prior to deployment date or date of first movement
  to complete pre-deployment medical clearance requirements.
  5.4.14. The Airman will complete all deployment and unit requirements per the guidelines
  given by the UDM, except those scheduled to be accomplished at the PDF, if a processing
  line is scheduled.
  5.4.15. Ten duty days prior to processing at the PDF for steady-state operations, the
  squadron commander will ensure all required actions are complete, with the exception of
  those being accomplished at the PDF. For crisis response, actions will be accomplished as
  soon as possible to meet departure timing.
  5.4.16. AFSC Substitution.
      5.4.16.1. The UTC MISCAP statement outlines the capability of the tasked UTC and
      identifies authorized AFSC substitutions unit commanders will use. The UTC MISCAP,
      functional AFIs, USAF WMP-1 Functional Annexes, or the Supported Command
      processing guidance/line remarks/reporting instructions regulate and control authorized
      substitutions.
      5.4.16.2. AFI 10-401 outlines “Any AFSC” substitutions.
      5.4.16.3. When substituting AFSCs that fall outside the scope of the above guidance,
      unit commanders must coordinate the substitution with the deployed commander. This
      will ensure the substitution continues to satisfy the original tasking requirement without
      mission degradation and the designated person can meet the functional requirements of
      the originally tasked AFSC.
      5.4.16.4. For additional AFSC substitution guidance, see AFI 10-401, Chapter 7.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                       155


  5.4.17. Grade/Skill Level Substitution. Like AFSC substitutions, the UTC MISCAP,
  functional AFIs, USAF WMP-1 Functional Annexes, or the Supported Command processing
  guidance/reporting instructions regulate and control authorized grade and skill level
  substitutions. Unless prohibited by these directives, the following grade and skill level
  apply:
     5.4.17.1. When units identify people to fill deployment requirements, enlisted are tasked
     based upon their Control AFSC (CAFSC) and officers are tasked based upon their Duty
     AFSC (DAFSC).
     5.4.17.2. When selecting personnel, the unit maximizes the matching of the required
     AFSC and grade to the person’s DAFSC (for officers) or CAFSC (for enlisted) and grade
     as much as possible. Line remarks further define and/or refine acceptable fills for the
     requirement. NOTE: Deviations could be directed by a tasking’s line remarks.
     5.4.17.3. Enlisted Skill Level Substitutions.
         5.4.17.3.1. Unless prohibited by line remarks or UTC MISCAP, Airmen with two
         skill levels higher or one skill level lower can satisfy enlisted requirements.
         5.4.17.3.2. EXCEPTION: Chief Enlisted Manager (CEM) requirements must be
         filled by a CEM/E-9.
         5.4.17.3.3. EXAMPLES: An Airman having a 3-, 5-, 7-, or 9-skill level can satisfy 5-
         skill level or an Airman having a 5-, 7-, or 9-skill level can satisfy 7-skill level
         tasking requirements.
     5.4.17.4. Enlisted Grade Substitutions.
         5.4.17.4.1. Unless prohibited by line remarks or UTC MISCAP, if the UTC or
         tasking identifies a required grade, the Airman must have that grade or higher grade
         to fill the requirement.
         5.4.17.4.2. EXAMPLE: An Airman with or in a higher grade than E-7 can satisfy an
         E-7 tasking requirement.
         5.4.17.4.3. A CEM/E-9 will only be used to fill a CEM grade requirement.
     5.4.17.5. Officer Grade Substitutions.
         5.4.17.5.1. Unless prohibited by the supported component headquarters through line
         remarks or UTC MISCAP, officer grade requirements will be filled by an officer
         having one grade higher or lower than the required grade.
         5.4.17.5.2. Second and first lieutenants are considered a single grade and can
         substitute in a captain grade requirement, provided they meet the intent of paragraph
         5.4.5.2.
         5.4.17.5.3. EXCEPTIONS:
            5.4.17.5.3.1. Unless prohibited by the supported component headquarters through
            line remarks or UTC MISCAP, a tasked medical commander can be filled by a
            substitute two grades up and two grades down for officers.
            5.4.17.5.3.2. Clinical personnel who are colonels can be tasked to fill non-colonel
 156                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


              requirements. However, for all other AF specialties, a colonel must fill a colonel
              grade requirement unless waived by the supported command.
              5.4.17.5.3.3. EXAMPLES: A captain, major, or lieutenant colonel can satisfy a
              major grade tasking. A lieutenant (1st or 2nd), captain, or major can satisfy a
              captain tasking.
   5.4.18. Volunteer Guidance.
       5.4.18.1. AEF Online (https://aef.afpc.randolph.af.mil/default.aspx) and the DOD
       Civilian Expeditionary Workforce (http://www.cpms.osd.mil/expeditionary) describe
       how active AF personnel (military and civilian) can volunteer for AEF ECS contingency
       taskings.
       5.4.18.2. All volunteers must coordinate their intent to volunteer with their unit
       commander or equivalent to ensure their volunteer status will not adversely impact the
       owning unit’s ability to meet its assigned/committed and AF mission requirements IAW
       AFI 10-401, Chapter 9.
5.5. Personnel Processing.
   5.5.1. Travel Arrangements.
       5.5.1.1. The IDO will review the TPFDD for mode/source of transportation for
       deploying Airmen/units.
       5.5.1.2. If the mode/source (i.e. “AC”) directs AMC contract airlift from AMC
       Gateways, the IDO in conjunction with the IPR will forward the assigned names with
       ULNs and requested dates of travel to the LRS Traffic Management for movement.
       5.5.1.3. The Distribution representative will book the port calls based on the ALD
       provided by the IDO or Plans and Integration Section.
       5.5.1.4. ULNs with mode/source for strategic lift (i.e. “AK”) either out of home station
       or at an aggregate APOE are not given port calls, but will be manifested during passenger
       processing activities.
       5.5.1.5. For large groups, the IDO should consider the GOPAX and/or CCPAX method
       to move individuals. For large groups within driving distances, the IDRC/DCC should
       consider busing to the APOE either by commercial bus or military bus.
       5.5.1.6. If none of these options seem feasible, the IDO will direct LRS Traffic
       Management to arrange commercial airline travel to the APOE only. There are no
       bookings in GATES for sending passengers to the aggregation point.
       5.5.1.7. All movement is projected in the TPFDD. If it becomes necessary that a
       deploying member is not able to deploy on the projected airlift, according to the TPFDD,
       it is imperative that the IDO notifies the respective MAJCOM AEF Cell as soon as
       possible in order to coordinate changes to the TPFDD so that appropriate transportation
       changes can be made.
       5.5.1.8. IAW CJSCM 3122.02D, Appendix F to Enclosure C, LAD = RDD minus port
       handling time (at POD) and transit time (from POD to RDD). This applies to all ULNs.
       The difference between LAD and RDD is the time allotted for JRSOI, in-theater training,
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        157


     Replacement In-place Transfer of Authority (RIPTOA), and Intra-Theater travel from
     POD to destination.
     5.5.1.9. RDDs may cause deploying Airmen to miss in-theater training/processing.
     5.5.1.10. Some ULNs in support of JET/IA requirements require personnel to be in
     theater earlier than the RDD for JRSOI/RIPTOA.
     5.5.1.11. Port calls must be based on meeting LAD at the POD.
         5.5.1.11.1. Port call planning for these JET/IA requirements will be based off LADs
         in order to be able to meet the CCDRs required JRSOI/RIPTOA.
         5.5.1.11.2. The IPRC/DCC will identify all en route reporting requirements to the
         LRS Traffic Management representative who will book appropriate port calls.
  5.5.2. Unit Personnel Assembly.
     5.5.2.1. Personnel will be processed in mass or individually. Every effort will be made
     to mass process personnel in order to provide a final requirements review that ensures
     members are fully prepared. Even if personnel are processed individually, some level of
     mass processing should be incorporated, if possible. That may include eligibility check;
     pre-deployment briefings (e.g. medical, cultural, anti-terrorism, trafficking in persons,
     anti-hijacking, etc.); last chance medical/immunizations check; and issuing orders, airline
     tickets (if applicable), mobility bags, and weapons/ammo (if applicable).
     5.5.2.2. If airlift will pick Airmen up at home station, they will always assemble at least
     3-hours prior to aircraft departure for manifesting and anti-hijack processing.
     5.5.2.3. Local installations may institute longer lead times to meet their specific needs
     and spell this out in their IDP.
     5.5.2.4. When mass processing, deploying Airmen will be assembled in a pre-identified
     area at the unit NLT the time indicated on the LOGMOD Schedule for unit processing.
         5.5.2.4.1. If processing individually, the UDM will determine the assembly time.
         Regardless if mass or individually processing, the unit will always pre-assemble
         personnel prior to departure.
         5.5.2.4.2. ARC personnel must report to home station prior to deployment and should
         depart from the nearest airport to home station.
         5.5.2.4.3. During unit assembly all deploying personnel will be checked to ensure the
         following:
            5.5.2.4.3.1. All personnel deploying meet requirements outlined in the tasking
            order and line remarks.
            5.5.2.4.3.2. They are eligible (DAV codes, duty status, valid security clearance,
            AFSC skill level and any additional requirements per deployment position line
            remarks).
            5.5.2.4.3.3. They have all personal items in order.
         5.5.2.4.4. Units will identify potential eligibility problems allowing the IDRC/DCC
         maximum time to find qualified personnel from existing base resources.
158                                           AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


  5.5.3. PDF Personnel Transportation.
      5.5.3.1. Dependent upon the type, size and timing of the deployment, the IDO will direct
      units to contact the DCC Transportation Representative to schedule/request transportation
      to get personnel to the processing area.
      5.5.3.2. Unit personnel will work through their UDMs to schedule movement to the PDF
      and/or local airport. Early contact will further help ensure individuals are delivered to the
      processing area in sufficient time to meet LOGMOD Schedule processing times.
      5.5.3.3. Responsibilities will be documented in the IDP. NOTE: In those instances
      where deploying Airmen are utilizing commercial transportation through a local airport,
      the unit should deliver Airmen to the airport to ensure they have everything mentioned in
      paragraph 5.5.2. NOTE: Ensure terminal transportation is in IAW AFI 24-301, paragraph
      3.1.1.
  5.5.4. PDF Processing (Unit Move). The key responsibilities of the PDF are:
      5.5.4.1. Advising commanders when personnel are ineligible for deployment.
      5.5.4.2. DELETED
      5.5.4.3. Providing last-minute services (e.g. legal, chaplain, medical, personnel actions,
      etc.) to Airmen (as requested or required).
      5.5.4.4. Responsibility for full control and accountability from the time unit personnel
      arrive at the PDF until personnel are physically loaded on the aircraft (or other
      embarkation movement source).
      5.5.4.5. Establishing a controlled area to hold all deploying personnel.
      5.5.4.6. Ensuring personnel representatives conduct a roll call to see if all of the correct
      individuals are present for processing.
      5.5.4.7. Performing the final eligibility check.
  5.5.5. Pre-Deployment Briefing Waiver.
      5.5.5.1. Enabler forces deploying multiple times within a 12-month period (60/90/120
      day rotations) to the same locations may waiver certain pre-deployment briefings for a
      period of 12 months.
      5.5.5.2. The waiverable briefings are as follows: A&FRC, Legal, Chaplain and Finance.
      PH/FHM briefings are waiverable only when it is determined that the FOL medical
      situation is un-changed.
      5.5.5.3. Local procedures will be established and codified in IDPs to verify how units
      document briefing dates, track currency and how members that have been granted a
      waiver have not exceeded the one-year expiration.
  5.5.6. CED Orders.
      5.5.6.1. AFI 36-3802 directs all AF unit personnel deploying on contingencies, exercises,
      or deployments to receive CED orders.
      5.5.6.2. CED orders are the only type of TDY orders used to deploy AF personnel
      assigned to AF units when use of JOPES is directed.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        159


     5.5.6.3. DCAPES is used to produce CED orders.
     5.5.6.4. An individual from the IPR will be assigned to the orders section during
     deployment processing.
     5.5.6.5. AFI 36-3802 provides specific guidance on producing CED orders.
         5.5.6.5.1. CED orders will be produced according to the timelines specified in the
         LOGMOD Schedule and in sufficient time to be included in the Troop Leader
         package for each chalk or at least (1) duty day prior to personnel departing from
         commercial airports.
         5.5.6.5.2. Ensure the tasked ULN (to include any frag and insert) and ULN position
         are included on the orders.
         5.5.6.5.3. Unclassified orders will be used unless driven by specific plan, message, or
         directive. Changes, amendments, or new orders, as required, are published and issued
         before, during, and after the deployment.
         5.5.6.5.4. No CED orders will be issued until the IDO or designated representative
         ensures the unit(s)/person(s) is/are deploying by mode and source IAW the
         OPLAN/CONPLAN TPFDD or equivalent supporting and supported command
         guidance.
     5.5.6.6. Distribution of orders will be IAW AFI 36-3802 and local procedures.
     5.5.6.7. DELETED
         5.5.6.7.1. DELETED
         5.5.6.7.2. DELETED
         5.5.6.7.3. DELETED
     5.5.6.8. If the orders cannot be completed, a manual passenger manifest will be
     completed prior to the departure of the aircraft.
         5.5.6.8.1. Ample notification of any late orders will be given to the manifesting
         agency.
         5.5.6.8.2. Manual manifests will be followed up with electronic manifests to
         maintain ITV.
     5.5.6.9. DCAPES is essential to inform deployed commanders, MAJCOM, and the Air
     Staff of the deploying force composition. Appropriate accountability actions in DCAPES
     will be accomplished by the IPR for systemized personnel strength accountability.
     5.5.6.10. DELETED
         5.5.6.10.1. DELETED
         5.5.6.10.2. DELETED
         5.5.6.10.3. DELETED
  5.5.7. Individual Personnel Processing.
160                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      5.5.7.1. The IDO will determine how personnel processing will be accomplished.
      Personnel processing may be accomplished using a full/partial processing line or by
      checklist only.
      5.5.7.2. Personnel processing procedures via checklist will be outlined in the
      installation/wing IDP.
      5.5.7.3. The IPR will develop both inprocessing and outprocessing checklists for
      deploying personnel IAW AFI 36-3802, Chapter 4.
         5.5.7.3.1. Once complete, unit/CCs or their designated representative will verify
         mandatory checklist items are completed and direct their deploying members back to
         their appointed UDM(s) for unit assembly prior to the IDRC for final out-processing.
         5.5.7.3.2. Provided tasking is received, ARC personnel should complete all out-
         processing actions during the unit training assembly prior to their scheduled
         departure.
         5.5.7.3.3. DELETED
         5.5.7.3.4. DELETED
      5.5.7.4. Unit/CC’s have a responsibility to send qualified and eligible personnel to
      process for deployment taskings. A unit/CC’s final acknowledgement on the deployment
      checklist for their deploying member(s) is vitally important as a deployed commander
      does not want anyone unqualified or incapable of performing in a deployed capacity that
      may jeopardize mission integrity.
         5.5.7.4.1. Deploying Airmen will ensure they receive CED orders from their IPR
         prior to deploying from home station. NOTE: Distribution of orders will be IAW
         AFI 36-3802, paragraph 7.4.18, the IPR is responsible for out-processing the
         individual; individuals will not deploy from home station prior to receiving CED
         orders and IDO confirmation of transportation allocation.
         5.5.7.4.2. After Airmen have completed all checklist items required for deployment,
         they will be scheduled by the UDM to meet at a pre-identified area at the unit for unit
         processing. The UDM will determine the assembly time.
         5.5.7.4.3. During unit assembly all deploying personnel will be checked to ensure the
         following are in compliance:
             5.5.7.4.3.1. Personnel meet deployment requirements outlined in the tasking
             order.
             5.5.7.4.3.2. DAV codes, valid security clearance, AFSC skill level and any
             additional requirement(s) per deployment position line remarks(s).
             5.5.7.4.3.3. Personal items are in order.
             5.5.7.4.3.4. Completion of all required training and deployment preparation
             requirements.
      5.5.7.5. Personnel Movement.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                         161


         5.5.7.5.1. When utilizing commercial transportation through the local airport, the unit
         will deliver or arrange transportation for their Airmen to meet scheduled lift. In
         either circumstance, and if practical, deploying Airmen should be met by UDM or a
         designated unit representative after the Airman leaves his/her residence and prior to
         arriving at the airport.
         5.5.7.5.2. AFRC units will meet this requirement when practical. Ensure the Airman
         has a contact number to reach the unit in case of emergency and/or a deviation from
         the planned deployment (e.g. personnel, equipment, or bags do not get on arranged
         transportation).
         5.5.7.5.3. If the Airman is scheduled to meet a commercial rotator chartered by AMC
         at an APOE different from their home station, the unit will work with the IDRC and
         Distribution Management Section to ensure appropriate transportation is
         scheduled/provided for the Airman to meet the required show-time of the mission.
         5.5.7.5.4. Ensure terminal transportation is in IAW AFI 24-301, paragraph 3.1.1.
     5.5.7.6. Once Airmen have departed their home installation, UDMs will ensure that the
     local IDRC has updated status on the departure of the Airmen. They will contact the
     IDRC to inform them of departure time and means of departure.
     5.5.7.7. IDRC/IPR representatives will monitor/update DCAPES to show departure and
     arrival status of deployed members. The IPR will provide departure and arrival
     information to the supporting Civilian Personnel Section (CPS) for update to DCPDS.
     This is essential to establish/maintain personnel strength accounting. If DCAPES does
     not reflect arrival of personnel within (7) duty days of departure, IPRs will contact
     servicing PERSCO Teams to request status of deployed personnel.
  5.5.8. Passenger Manifesting.
     5.5.8.1. Passenger manifests will be prepared for each chalk to ensure in-transit visibility
     from point of origin to final destination.
     5.5.8.2. The individuals assigned to this function will be extremely knowledgeable of the
     requirements of DTR 4500.9-R, Parts I and III.
     5.5.8.3. CMOS or GATES (for CONUS AMC strategic aerial ports and overseas AMS
     units) will generate the passenger manifest based on the orders and files received from
     DCAPES for departure on airlift from home station. LRS Traffic Management or
     Passenger Processing personnel will:
         5.5.8.3.1. Manifest and collect emergency contact information directly from
         deploying personnel.
         5.5.8.3.2. Ensure emergency contact information is not sourced from the Service
         Casualty Affairs Officer, Commander’s Support Staff (CSS)/Unit Orderly Room, or a
         similar single POC IAW DTR 4500.9-R, Part III.
         5.5.8.3.3. Facilitate compliance with 49 U.S.C. § 41113, Plans to Address Needs of
         Families of Passengers Involved in Aircraft Accidents, by requiring the collection of
         identifying and emergency contact information called for in 14 CFR, Part 243,
         Passenger Manifest Information.
 162                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


       5.5.8.4. If CMOS or GATES are not available to produce the passenger manifest, a DD
       Form 2131, Passenger Manifest, is used. Fax or email DD Form 2131 to AMC/ITV cell
       (ORG.AMCA4-70@us.af.mil) for ITV purposes.
       5.5.8.5. Required information will be exported to CMOS or GATES from DCAPES.
       5.5.8.6. CMOS or GATES will feed personnel manifests to IGC to provide ITV.
       5.5.8.7. Manifesting passengers during AEF rotations will require chalking of passengers
       to meet the scheduled aircraft mission versus final destination. Airmen could be
       deploying to multiple destinations, but are required to arrive in theater on the same LAD
       through the same POD.
          5.5.8.7.1. In order to meet the CCDRs RDD and maximize aircraft utilization, TACC
          may schedule or aggregate Airmen from multiple origins on a single mission.
          5.5.8.7.2. The IDO or IDRC must ensure Airmen are chalked and exported via the
          DCAPES export file titled “CMOSxxx.file” that can be imported into CMOS and
          GATES.
          5.5.8.7.3. The DCAPES export file is provided to the APOE 72-hours prior to
          mission departure.
          5.5.8.7.4. Updates will be transmitted via e-mail as required with a summary of
          changes and a new/updated “CMOSxxx.file” attached.
          5.5.8.7.5. IDO/IDRC personnel will review the applicable APOE reporting
          instructions, via the AEF On-line website, to determine if and when an XMAN (Excel
          Manifest) file is required to be submitted to the appropriate APOE to facilitate the
          passenger manifesting process at the APOE.

Section 5C—Personnel Equipment/Baggage

5.6. Deploying Personnel Equipment Requirements.
   5.6.1. Minimum Requirements List.
       5.6.1.1. Develop a minimum personnel requirements list for unit personnel.
       5.6.1.2. The supported commander determines any changes in theater clearance
       requirements and, along with HAF FAMs for JET taskings, identifies all additional items
       deploying personnel must take.
       5.6.1.3. The supported commander, at execution, determines whether personnel need
       mobility bags, weapons, ammunition, insect vector control measures, and chemical
       injectors.
       5.6.1.4. Mobility bag, ammunition, and small arms management for active duty units
       will be IAW AFMAN 23-110, AFI 10-2501 and AFI 21-101, Aircraft and Equipment
       Maintenance Management.
       5.6.1.5. ANG and AFRC units will follow the guidance of their higher headquarters.
   5.6.2. Deploying Personal Baggage (Acceptability/Limitations).
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        163


     5.6.2.1. For purposes of this instruction, the term “bag” or “baggage” refers to any soft-
     or hard-sided container with carrying handle(s) containing items necessary for
     personal/duty use for the duration of the deployment.
     5.6.2.2. Personal clothing will be deployed as baggage on the same aircraft transporting
     personnel.
        5.6.2.2.1. Personal clothing will be packed in the type of “checked bags” specified in
        the reporting instructions for the corresponding military or commercial Port of
        Embarkation (POE).
        5.6.2.2.2. Personal luggage/baggage, IPE, and PROGEAR must meet the linear and
        weight requirements described in paragraph 5.6.3.2.
        5.6.2.2.3. Any excess baggage must be authorized on orders.
     5.6.2.3. AOR reporting instructions published by the Supported Commander may limit
     the total number of bags authorized, particularly excess baggage, based upon lift
     availability to, and beddown capabilities at, the ultimate deployed location.
     5.6.2.4. Depending upon the mode of transport (e.g. commercial air segments between
     commercial airports or AMC contract airlift from AMC gateways) selected from origin to
     destination, IDOs, LRS Traffic Management, and deploying units must be aware that
     commercial airlines could further restrict weight, size, and type specifications applicable
     to checked baggage.
     5.6.2.5. IDOs must thoroughly review AOR reporting instructions and consult with the
     installation LRS Traffic Management to verify whether such limitations or additional
     instructions (i.e. special baggage tag requirements), may impact deployment plans or
     execution.
     5.6.2.6. CCDRs are authorized to provide pre-deployed weapons, ammunition, and
     mobility bags at centrally managed and distributed locations within their AOR at ETDCs.
     This could eliminate the need for Airmen to deploy with these assets.
     5.6.2.7. DELETED
     5.6.2.8. It is ultimately the unit commander’s responsibility to ensure unit personnel
     deploy with all required personal items, IPE, and Professional GEAR (PROGEAR), and
     to ensure that all other non-individual issue equipment required for the major operation or
     campaign is properly identified in equipment UTCs.
     5.6.2.9. At no time, will equipment items normally shipped as freight, or deployed as
     cargo be allowed to accompany a deploying individual as part of his or her excess
     baggage authorization, unless specifically stated in CED orders.
     5.6.2.10. Unit commanders must pay particular attention to this point to preclude
     baggage being “bumped” en route due to transport mode weight or space limitations.
     5.6.2.11. Aircraft ACL limitations could exist on AMC contract carrier contingency and
     rotator missions; therefore, excess baggage scrutiny at home station is prudent if
     deploying personnel will travel via this means.
164                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      5.6.2.12. Deploying members must not add any personal or unauthorized items to their
      A, B, C, or D-bags.
      5.6.2.13. In some cases, deploying units require tools or equipment that are too
      large/heavy for movement on commercial passenger aircraft, and not currently listed in a
      UTC’s MISCAP. In each case, the deploying unit is required to arrange shipment of the
      required equipment separate from the deploying unit, and at unit expense. Either a
      complete MISCAP review needs to be accomplished, or procedures for the referenced
      scenario need to be identified to ensure the cargo movement is accomplished as part of
      the supported operation, tracked in an ITV system, and billed to the supported operation’s
      funds.
  5.6.3. Over Weight/Excess Baggage.
      5.6.3.1. Deploying personnel transiting AMC owned or operated terminals are
      authorized one hand carried bag plus a small personal bag e.g. back-pack, laptop, purse,
      etc. and no more than two pieces of personal baggage, mobility/pro-gear bags and
      weapon cannot exceed 400 lbs. Excess baggage must be annotated in the traveler’s
      orders and must specify the weight and/or number of pieces authorized.
      5.6.3.2. Any single bag exceeding the 70 lb. weight limit or 62 linear inches will count as
      two pieces and count as the member’s second authorized piece of personal baggage.
      EXCEPTION: A3, B-4, duffle, and sea bags shall be allowed as one piece up to 80 linear
      inches as long as they do not exceed 100 lbs.
      5.6.3.3. The second bag must still comply with size restrictions and is limited to 70 lbs.
      NOTE: Commercial tickets that contain only CONUS segments might limit checked
      baggage to 50 lbs each before excess baggage charges are assessed.
      5.6.3.4. Baggage exceeding 80 linear inches/100 lbs will not be accepted (Ref: DTR
      4500.9, Part III for additional guidance and future updates. IPE (A, B, C, and D type
      mobility bags)/IPE and PROGEAR are common, acceptable examples of excess baggage.
      5.6.3.5. There is no standard policy between DOD, FAA and TSA for military shipments
      of weapons in checked baggage or as excess baggage.
         5.6.3.5.1. Ammunition and weapons are not permitted in carry-on baggage but,
         depending on the policy of the airline, can be included with checked baggage.
         5.6.3.5.2. Weapons must be unloaded, packed in a locked, hard-sided case and
         declared at check-in. All airline and TSA requirements must be strictly adhered to.
         5.6.3.5.3. All transportation offices should distinguish excess baggage contents as
         weapons when making airline reservations and ensure coordination with the airlines
         and TSA for handling and packaging instructions. It is suggested that advanced
         copies of the weapon declaration forms be completed in advance to streamline check-
         in.
         5.6.3.5.4. Commercial travel offices should provide proper passenger counseling, to
         include familiarization with rules and requirements of the scheduled service airlines
         and TSA.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                          165


Section 5D—Troop Leader

5.7. Troop Leader.
   5.7.1. After processing of personnel is complete, the IDRC/PDF will designate the senior
   ranking individual assigned to a group of two or more personnel that are deploying on the
   same means of transportation to the same deployed location as the troop leader and provide
   this individual with a Troop Leader’s Personnel Accountability Kit (PAK).
   5.7.2. The troop leader must account for and control the deploying force from the time after
   processing through the PDF (or IDRC) until arrival at the final deployed location.
       5.7.2.1. If deployers are traveling via commercial transportation and do not process
       through the PDF, a troop leader will still be appointed to maintain accountability of
       personnel throughout the trip.
       5.7.2.2. In that case, the troop leader will be briefed on responsibilities by the PDF (or
       IDRC) (see also DTR 4500.9-R, Part III, Appendix T).
   5.7.3. The troop leader will confirm transportation allocation and mode/source of
   transportation before departing.
   5.7.4. DELETED
   5.7.5. Troop leaders, of groups traveling commercially, will be provided all identified
   documentation except for documentation related to travel by military airlift.
   5.7.6. The PDF will brief the troop leader to turn this information over to the reception team,
   Logistics Readiness Center (LRC), or the PERSCO team upon arrival at the deployed
   location to track personnel accountability and to support redeployment planning.
5.8. Ineligible Personnel Deployment. Personnel found to be unqualified or who do not meet
the specifications identified in the tasking by the deployed commander will be returned to home
station.

Section 5E—Personnel Record/Data Documentation

5.9. Record Keeping.
   5.9.1. IDRC personnel will keep station file records for all documentation used to deploy
   both personnel and cargo. These records will be kept for the previous year plus the current
   year.
   5.9.2. All station file records will be maintained and disposed of IAW AFMAN 33-363,
   Management of Records.
 166                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


                                          Chapter 6

                                  RECEPTION PROCESS

Section 6A—General

6.1. General.
   6.1.1. Reception is the first part of the overall joint concept of Reception, Staging, Onward
   Movement, and Integration (RSO&I). The reception process is designed to integrate
   incoming units into a mission/combat capable force as soon as possible with the flexibility to
   stage and move units forward. It involves off-loading, documenting, accounting for, and
   bedding down inbound equipment and personnel.
   6.1.2. Reference AFI 10-404 and MAJCOM guidance for specific planning processes,
   timing, decision support tools, beddown reception processes, and team composition.
   6.1.3. See Joint Publication 3-35, Deployment and Redeployment Operations, Chapter VI.
   6.1.4. This chapter will cover reception operations from AF main operating bases and FOLs
   where the AF has reception responsibility.

Section 6B—AETF Planning Concept

6.2. AETF Force Modules.
   6.2.1. Within the AETF Force Modules, the “Open the Base,” “C2,” and “Establish the
   Base” modules are primarily responsible for the efficient and effective reception of personnel
   and equipment and completing the ITV to provide the supported CCDR verification of force
   closure.
   6.2.2. For the purposes of this guidance, the reception process, if accomplished correctly,
   enables an efficient and effective redeployment process.
   6.2.3. The redeployment process supports both the forward deployment of personnel and the
   return of personnel to home station.
6.3. Employment and Reception Planning.
   6.3.1. The key to reception planning starts with the Supported Command. The Supported
   Command must develop a program to accomplish ESPs for those installations in its AOR that
   are intended to be beddown locations with or without a major AF presence.
   6.3.2. The Supported and Supporting MAJCOMs OPRs for Base Support and Expeditionary
   Site Planning establish criteria defining the degree to which bases will develop their BSPs
   and ESPs IAW AFI 10-404.
6.4. Command & Control (C2).
   6.4.1. If opening a base, the senior ranking officer will assume command of the deployed
   Contingency Response Group (CRG), and be responsible for the initial C2 of incoming
   forces until the arrival of the EMSG/CC IAW AFI 51-604.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                       167


      6.4.1.1. The aim is to properly manage the reception process and provide an orderly
      transition from base opening to the establishment of the end state organization.
      6.4.1.2. When receiving forces at established AF locations, the CRG may still deploy to
      support the initial arrival of resources.
      6.4.1.3. The established C2 function will retain responsibility for command and control
      of incoming and employed forces.
      6.4.1.4. The installation commander has overall responsibility for reception of forces at
      established AF installations.

Section 6C—Reception Roles and Responsibilities

6.5. Commander, Expeditionary Mission Support Group (EMSG/CC).
   6.5.1. The EMSG/CC is responsible for establishing the base and overall reception of forces.
   6.5.2. After establishment of the base, the EMSG/CC will control the LRC, contingency
   response center, Installation Control Center, Prime Base Engineer Emergency Force (Prime
   BEEF), and Force Support units.
   6.5.3. These duties require oversight and control over fuels, supply, transportation,
   communications, civil engineer, personnel, services, security/base defense functions, and
   others.
   6.5.4. The EMSG/CC directs the actions of the Reception Control Center (RCC). The
   installation commander directly controls the employment mission and the Expeditionary
   Operations Center (EOC).
6.6. Log C2 Team.
   6.6.1. The Log C2 team’s role is to provide overall control and coordination of reception,
   beddown, staging, onward movement, and redeployment.
   6.6.2. The LOG C2 team:
      6.6.2.1. Manages WRM and coordinates inter-Service, international, and wartime HNS.
      6.6.2.2. Is the focal point for redeployment actions.
      6.6.2.3. The Log C2 Team reports to the EMSG/CC (may be through the LRC or other
      established center).
      6.6.2.4. The Log C2 Team is made up of Logistics Planners and LROs and any
      associated required equipment per applicable UTCs.
   6.6.3. For reception of forces at established AF installations, the DCC, PDF and CDF can
   operate in a dual role as the RCC, Reception Processing Unit (RPU), and Cargo Reception
   Function (CRF) respectively, as bases often deploy and receive forces simultaneously.
 168                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


Section 6D—Reception Workcenters

6.7. Reception Control Center (RCC).
   6.7.1. Provides overall direction and coordination of reception and beddown procedures and
   resolves any problems affecting reception of resources.
   6.7.2. Oversees two functions, the RPU and the CRF. (NOTE: For reception of forces at
   established AF installations, the DCC, PDF and CDF operate in a dual role as the RCC, RPU
   and CRF respectively, as bases often deploy and receive forces simultaneously.)
   6.7.3. Installation/Wing Commanders, or equivalents, will appoint an Installation Reception
   Officer (IRO) in writing IAW AFI 38-101.
   6.7.4. The RCC, if not at an established AF operating location, is created with the arrival of
   the C2 force module. At established AF locations, the RCC is established IAW AFI 10-404.
   Until their arrival, the CRG is responsible for accountability and onward movement of
   arriving forces.
       6.7.4.1. The CRG PERSCO Representative will assume accountability from any in-place
       AFSOC PERSCO Representative or will establish initial accountability for all AF
       personnel and will transfer that accountability to the C2 PERSCO Team upon its arrival.
       6.7.4.2. When a CRG or aerial port is operating at the employment site, the RCC
       representative contacts the appropriate agent to ensure all incoming resources are
       accounted for and customs cleared before moving them to the reception area (Refer to
       AFI 10-404 for more details).
       6.7.4.3. The RCC will report to the LRC or like function, but will not be subsumed by
       that function.
       6.7.4.4. The variety of tasks required to secure the base, build and maintain living and
       operating facilities, provide aircraft fire and rescue support, respond to emergencies, care
       for and feed the population, refuel and resupply aircraft, and beddown transient forces
       would not allow for the focus and concentration required to ensure forces are identified,
       met, accounted for, and integrated.
       6.7.4.5. RCC will monitor the inbound force airlift and the actual arrival times of
       personnel and cargo. See AFI 10-404, Attachment 7, for more on reception processes.
       6.7.4.6. RCC will ensure all personnel are put in contact with their unit of assignment or
       duty sections. At a minimum, the RCC will ensure:
          6.7.4.6.1. They can track incoming units and airlift.
          6.7.4.6.2. Aerial port or CRG, if operating at the deployed locations, receives
          incoming equipment data in GATES.
              6.7.4.6.2.1. If it is the final destination, the manifest will show equipment was
              trucked to the CRF.
              6.7.4.6.2.2. If it is not the final destination, the CRF will manifest equipment
              within CMOS to the next or final destination.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                     169


        6.7.4.6.3. Equipment received is placed in a secure holding area until the owning
        units arrive for pickup.
        6.7.4.6.4. Deployed equipment custodians are required to account for their unit
        equipment through the designated LRS function IAW AFMAN 23-110, Volume 2,
        Part 2, Chapter 22.
        6.7.4.6.5. Arriving personnel are accounted for by PERSCO personnel and briefed
        regarding their mission, work area, local conditions, and command structure.
        6.7.4.6.6. Arriving personnel are assigned lodging.
        6.7.4.6.7. Assigned personnel are met by their work center (if work center is already
        established).
     6.7.4.7. Deployment discrepancies are noted and loaded in AEF Online DPDRT. NOTE:
     Deployment discrepancies for OSI Detachments fall under the purview of AF/OSI/WFR
     (Joint Base Andrews AFB, MD). Formal responses and corrective actions will not be
     counted against the host installation/wing. NOTE: PERSCO’s responsibility for entering
     discrepancies in DPDRT is IAW AFI 36-3802.
     6.7.4.8. The senior AF LRO (e.g. LRS/CC) at the deployed location and the RCC will
     work together to ensure all problems are resolved at the lowest level.
     6.7.4.9. The Air Mobility Control Center at the deployed location will report the number
     of incoming passengers and cargo information to the RCC and coordinate support airlift
     servicing requirements with appropriate agencies.
     6.7.4.10. If reception and deployment occur at a location simultaneously, the senior LRO
     (e.g. LRS/CC) will ensure the proper coordination with all agencies is performed to
     ensure effective utilization of available resources.
     6.7.4.11. Units at the employment location will provide a representative to brief duty
     schedules, chain of command, supervisors, duty locations, and important phone numbers.
     Employed location units will further provide the following briefings or information:
        6.7.4.11.1. Terrorist FPCON and DOD threat level.
        6.7.4.11.2. Applicable SOFA, MOPP, and FPCON cards.
        6.7.4.11.3. Legal (or command) representative will brief ROEs as published by the
        combatant commander.
        6.7.4.11.4. Public Affairs will provide literature on base facilities, mission of the
        base, and the local area, if available.
        6.7.4.11.5. Safety will provide briefings on flightline driving and other local
        conditions.
        6.7.4.11.6. Medical will provide literature on local area health conditions and
        conduct a medical orientation.
        6.7.4.11.7. Security Forces (in coordination with airfield management) will arrange
        for custom clearances.
 170                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


          6.7.4.11.8. Civil Engineer will provide literature on CBRN passive defense
          conditions and necessary Mission-Oriented Protective Posture (MOPP) levels.
          6.7.4.11.9. Communications and Information Postal Services will provide literature
          on procedures for receiving and sending mail and hours of operation.
          6.7.4.11.10. Force Support Squadron Sustainment Flight will provide lodging
          assignments and arrange for extended hours of operation or ground support meals for
          incoming forces as appropriate. Priority will be given to unit integrity and the
          homogeneous lodging of commissioned and enlisted personnel. Additionally, they
          will work closely with PERSCO to document lodging assignments.
          6.7.4.11.11. Finance will provide assistance in cash advances and pay inquiries.
          6.7.4.11.12. Sister Service Representative(s).    If incoming personnel include
          personnel from the Army, Navy, or Marines, these Services will be contacted to
          provide a representative to assist in receiving and processing their personnel and
          cargo.
          6.7.4.11.13. Security Forces representatives will monitor weapons arrival and
          storage.
          6.7.4.11.14. Force Support PERSCO representative is responsible for providing
          guidelines for accounting of all forces according to AFI 36-3802, Supported
          Command processing instructions/reporting guidance, and the deployed commander.
          6.7.4.11.15. AFOSI will provide the local threat update.
          6.7.4.11.16. Security Forces Commander or Defense Force Commander, if not the
          AEF/SF, will ensure the integrated defense posture and any unique procedures or
          awareness information is provided.
          6.7.4.11.17. Chaplain Corps will provide literature or a briefing on privileged
          communication and religious rites and services available to them at the deployed
          location.
       6.7.4.12. When a CRG or element of a CRG is operating at the employment site, the
       RCC contacts the passenger service agent to ensure all passengers are accounted for and
       customs cleared before moving them to the reception area.
6.8. Reception Processing Unit (RPU).
   6.8.1. The RPU is similar to the PDF, but in a reception role. It provides overall control for
   arriving personnel forces and coordinates requirements for processing and onward
   movement.
   6.8.2. In most cases, the RPU should remain separate from the PDF due to sterilization and
   customs issues.
   6.8.3. The RPU accounts for all arriving and departing personnel. All arriving personnel
   will inprocess with this unit.
   6.8.4. The RPU manages the transportation needs of arriving personnel and delivers baggage
   to and from designated locations. The RPU will be augmented by transportation and unit
   personnel to ensure passengers and baggage are delivered to designated locations.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                          171


   6.8.5. The RPU provides shuttle bus maps/routes and arrival and departure times.
6.9. PERSCO Team.
   6.9.1. The PERSCO Team is a part of the RPU and will account for all arriving and
   departing personnel.
   6.9.2. See AFI 36-3802 for a complete description of PERSCO responsibilities. PERSCO
   personnel and their established procedures will be used for documenting arriving personnel.
   6.9.3. If a PERSCO team is not available, a person will be appointed by the troop leader to
   maintain accountability until a PERSCO team arrives (reference AFI 36-3802).
6.10. Cargo Reception Function (CRF).
   6.10.1. The CRF is similar to the CDF, but in a reception role. It provides overall control for
   arriving cargo/equipment and coordinates requirements for processing and onward
   movement.
   6.10.2. In most cases, there is not enough marshaling capacity for a separate CRF and CDF,
   but the collocated operations must physically keep incoming and outgoing cargo separate.
   6.10.3. Provides for movement of cargo from holding areas based on prioritization given by
   the unit representative or troop leader.
   6.10.4. Collects all documentation and dates (e.g. placards, load/packing lists, LOGMOD
   files, etc.) for incoming cargo. Notifies RCC team of inbound surface deliveries, passenger
   movement status, and cargo hold and movement status.
   6.10.5. Establishes a holding area for collecting pallets, nets, dunnage, and RFID tags to be
   put back into the transportation system. NOTE: For employment sites with CRG support, the
   provisional wing/group provides the CRF process.
   6.10.6. Processes cargo for onward movement and provides continued in-transit visibility.
6.11. Reception Team Information Management.
   6.11.1. In-place teams, to include home station personnel, ―Open the Base‖ forces (e.g.
   CRGs), or “C2” and “Establish the Base” forces, can accomplish the reception of resources.
   6.11.2. Reception teams will capture all data and documentation necessary to account for
   arriving resources using the IDS.
   6.11.2.1. Cargo received will be receipted for in GATES or CMOS, cleared through
   customs, and placed in the appropriate holding area pending distribution to the owners or
   onward movement.
   6.11.3. All personnel arriving at the deployed location will centrally process through the
   RPU, ensuring that full accountability is accomplished via standard AF accountability
   systems used by PERSCO Teams.
   6.11.4. The primary tool suite that supports and enables the reception process is the IDS.
   IDS components at a deployed site might not fully duplicate the tool suite used at home
   station. Minimum tools required are LOGMOD, ICODES, GATES and/or CMOS. The full
   suite of tools (LOGMOD, ICODES, and CMOS/GATES) will be the primary systems
   utilized, if available.
 172                                        AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


   6.11.5. In addition, deployed LRS personnel/LROs will use systems required by AFMAN
   23-110 to account for arriving equipment, spares, and, if centrally stored, munitions,
   weapons, IPE and mobility bags. The web-enabled Combat Ammunition System (CAS) will
   be used to account for and manage all munitions and ammunition under all situations and
   conditions IAW AFI 21-201.
   6.11.6. Finally, for visibility of incoming forces, the RCC requires access to the TPFDD and
   airlift schedules. They will require SIPRNET connectivity for access to DCAPES/JOPES,
   BaS&E, and LOGFAC. If these systems are not available, RCC personnel should be able to
   access classified web sites or e-mail as a backup. For incoming airlift schedules, use IGC,
   GDSS, SMS, or similar airlift tracking system.
6.12. Advance Echelon (ADVON) Team Responsibilities.
   6.12.1. The primary responsibilities of the ADVON team are preparation, execution of unit
   employment, and developing employment reception.
   6.12.2. At established locations, these duties are performed by assigned functions within
   LRS, FSS, Operations planning, Airfield Management, Comptroller, CES, SFS, JAG,
   Medical Group, etc.
   6.12.3. Air Component personnel, in-theater CRGs, or units that may be scheduled to deploy
   to austere bases, limited bases, or collocated bases, may perform these duties. These
   activities are performed by Open the Base forces (e.g. CRG), “C2,” and “Establish the Base”
   force modules at newly opened bases.
   6.12.4. An ADVON team is not required for every deployed unit or location. When used,
   the ADVON team or host unit will assist all other units in the beddown process.
   6.12.5. Deployed Commanders ensure           arriving/deployed   personnel   meet   tasking
   requirements to include line remarks.

Section 6E—Reception Record/Data Documentation

6.13. Reception Record Keeping/Data Documentation . The CRG or RCC will collect the
following documentation and data for all incoming resources:
   6.13.1. Incoming Aircraft Commanders package.
   6.13.2. IDS personnel and levy data disk produced from DCAPES.
   6.13.3. Orders with SSNs.
   6.13.4. ICODES data file.
   6.13.5. Passenger manifests.
   6.13.6. Shippers Declarations.
   6.13.7. Cargo Load and Packing lists.
   6.13.8. AF Form 245, Employment Locator and Processing Checklist.
   6.13.9. DD Form 2133, Joint Airlift Inspection Record.
   6.13.10. Aircraft Load Plans.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                  173


  6.13.11. Deployed Medical Records (AF 2766), if brought, for turn-in to deployed Medical
  Treatment Facility (MTF)/Expeditionary Medical Support (EMEDS).
 174                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


                                           Chapter 7

                             REDEPLOYMENT OPERATIONS

Section 7A—General

7.1. General.
   7.1.1. Redeployment is defined as the transfer of forces and materiel to support another joint
   force commander's operational requirements, or to return personnel, equipment, and materiel
   to the home and/or demobilization stations for reintegration and/or out-processing.
       7.1.1.1. Redeployment is NOT “deployment in reverse.”
       7.1.1.2. The redeployment TPFDD could reflect fragmented UTCs or ULNs to be
       incrementally redeployed or forward deployed to retain residual capability at original
       deployed locations requiring the supportability of the remaining forces.
       7.1.1.3. Planners (LRS representatives, etc.) need to plan for movement of parts of units,
       UTCs, or ULNs.
       7.1.1.4. Additionally, redeployment can be far more rapid than the deployment phase,
       which makes redeployment planning all the more critical.
   7.1.2. Early planning is essential to an effective and efficient return of deployed resources or
   forward deployment of combat capability.
       7.1.2.1. Redeployment activities need to begin long before receipt of a redeployment
       order.
       7.1.2.2. Normally, the planning process begins upon arrival at the deployed location, and
       if possible, prior to departing home station. This ensures accountability of all deployed
       resources and that redeployment movement activities comply with CCDR and host
       nation’s customs requirements.
       7.1.2.3. If the overall operation becomes a prolonged engagement, a Rotation of Airmen
       (ROA) plan will require consideration. For ROA execution, redeployment planning will
       begin once the rotation plan has been completed to ensure timely replacement of
       resources, overlap, and training en-route requirements.

Section 7B—Redeployment Process

7.2. Redeployment Process.
   7.2.1. Redeployment Planning.
       7.2.1.1. At the CCDR level, redeployment planning will normally begin when the Joint
       Task Force (JTF) staff gathers to plan an operation.
       7.2.1.2. At the installation level, the IDO and logistics planners assist and advise
       deploying commanders, and their redeployment team members on movement
       responsibilities.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                         175


     7.2.1.3. Redeployment team members will assist the employment location’s logistics
     teams and/or Redeployment Assistance Team (RAT) in executing the movement plan at
     the employment site. A RAT team will consist of logistics planners, air transportation,
     traffic management, PERSCO and unit representatives.
         7.2.1.3.1. A critical link for success is for the employment location’s reception team
         to collect and store all aircraft commander’s packages from arriving airlift missions
         during force closure.
         7.2.1.3.2. The reception team will retain documentation for redeployment. At
