       A3.21.1.8. DD Form 2764, Geneva Convention ID Card for Civilians (N/A for ANG
       units)?
       A3.21.1.9. Two pairs of prescription eyeglasses, if applicable? If necessary due to AOR
       reporting instructions - copy of AFPAM 10-100?
       A3.21.1.10. One hearing aid and two sets of batteries, if applicable?
       A3.21.1.11. Personal clothing and equipment. (NOTE: Personal clothing will be packed
       in duffel bags, barracks bags, B-4 type bags or commercial luggage with rounded corners,
       but not in wheeled containers, footlockers, or trunks unless they have rounded corners to
       preclude damage to other baggage and their contents. Personal baggage limitations are
       two pieces at 70 pounds each, excluding deployment bag and toolboxes. Carry-on
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                           267


      baggage will be limited to one piece not to exceed 45 linear inches in dimension. (Excess
      baggage will be authorized in orders, if required.)
      A3.21.1.12. Individual tool kits, professional kits, and any personal protective equipment
      required to perform duty? Hand-carry one complete operational CWDE ensemble
      onboard deployment aircraft when applicable.
      A3.21.1.13. A 180-day supply of medications if under medical treatment? (Notify PDF
      immunization personnel if you are currently receiving medical treatment or have a
      chronic medical problem).
      A3.21.1.14. Spectacle inserts for gas masks, when applicable?
      A3.21.1.15. AF Form 1297, Temporary Issue Receipt, for cargo couriers if weapons are
      to be issued?
      A3.21.1.16. Completed AF Form 522, USAF Grounds Weapons Training Data,
      detachable portion, (or automated equivalent) if weapons qualified?
      A3.21.1.17. Personal Legal Affairs (e.g. life insurance, will, power of attorney, or other
      legal document)?
      A3.21.1.18. Maintain weight and fitness standards while deployed.
      A3.21.1.19. AFPAM 10-100, Airman’s Manual?
A3.22. Unit Deployment Manager Responsibilities Checklist.           Recommended UDM self
assessment checklist items.
   A3.22.1. Are unit commanders and staff informed of the deployment status of unit
   personnel?
   A3.22.2. Can the unit deployment control center be immediately activated?
   A3.22.3. Is a copy of the IDP available in the unit deployment control center?
   A3.22.4. Is there a continuous training program to familiarize unit personnel with the IDP
   and with specific responsibilities during deployment?
   A3.22.5. Is a current pyramid unit recall notification plan in effect and can unit personnel be
   recalled in the event of telephone or communications failure?
   A3.22.6. Are unit deployment rosters complete and current and updated in LOGMOD?
   A3.22.7. Do qualified individuals fill each deployable UTC position assigned to the unit?
   A3.22.8. Are individuals notified (person-to-person contact) when tasked to deploy?
   A3.22.9. If cargo couriers are required, is the unit deployment roster annotated?
   A3.22.10. Have designated classified couriers been identified?
   A3.22.11. Have procedures been established to ensure individuals are briefed on
   responsibilities for deployment to include:
      A3.22.11.1. Personal clothing and equipment?
      A3.22.11.2. Professional equipment and supplies?
268                                         AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      A3.22.11.3. Accuracy of documents and records necessary for deployments?
      A3.22.11.4. Individuals having their personal affairs in order at all times and have
      informed family members there is a strong probability of very short-notice deployments?
      A3.22.11.5. What Airman & Family Readiness Center programs are available?
      A3.22.11.6. Advising family members to contact the local American Red Cross
      representative if any emergency arises that necessitates return of the individual?
      A3.22.11.7. Responsibility to contact medical personnel when a physical condition is
      detected that might limit capability to perform deployment duties so that an AF Form
      422, Notification of Air Force Member’s Qualification Status, and/or AF Form 469, Duty
      Limiting Condition Report, can be prepared? (NOTE: Emergency-Essential (E-E) federal
      civilians will inform their supervisor if they have a permanent or long-term medical
      problem that would prevent them from deploying).
      A3.22.11.8. Have procedures been implemented to ensure compliance with the following
      requirements:
      A3.22.11.9. Deployment training is documented in unit training records?
      A3.22.11.10. All immunizations for individuals are current at all times?
      A3.22.11.11. Individual's CAC is current at all times?
      A3.22.11.11.1. Individual possesses a set of current ID (Dog) tags (two tags, one short
      chain and one long chain)?
      A3.22.11.12. Individual maintains a current vRED or DD Form 93.
      A3.22.11.13. Individual has all finance affairs (e.g. pay allotments, Direct Deposit, DD
      Form 1337, Pay and Allowances, Authorization/Designation for Emergency, etc.) in
      order?
      A3.22.11.14. Medical and religious personnel have a DD Form 1934 and civilian
      employees other than medical and religious, have a DD Form 2764?
      A3.22.11.15. Do individuals, who are appointed to manage a given set of cargo
      increments, have hazardous cargo training to include maintaining accurate packing and
      load lists, and preparing DD Forms 1387-2 for classified hazardous cargo and DD Form
      2779, Shipper's Declaration for Dangerous Goods Form, for all other hazardous cargo?
      A3.22.11.16. Are personnel ready at the unit assembly area for movement to the
      deployment processing line at the time established on the LOGMOD Schedule?
      A3.22.11.17. Are equipment and supplies properly prepared (using applicable checklists
      and instructions) and delivered to the CDF in-check area according to the Deployment
      Schedule?
      A3.22.11.18. Does the unit conduct personnel eligibility verification(s), clothing
      check(s), and equipment check(s) for each person scheduled for a deployment before the
      individual reports to the PDF?
      A3.22.11.19. Are procedures established for a periodic inspection to verify individual's
      eligibility for deployment (recommend a quarterly inspection at minimum)?

      A3.22.11.20. Has the unit established procedures, checklists, and charts to ensure control
      of deployment personnel, equipment, and supplies?
      A3.22.11.21. Are authorized deployment equipment and supplies maintained in a
      constant state of readiness?

   A3.23.1. Preparation:

      C-17 for planning purposes?

      A3.23.1.7. Are procedures in place to monitor the CCDR’s TPFDD on a continual basis?

      A3.23.2.5. Are LOGMOD Schedules being modified and/or created using the CCDR’s

      A3.23.2.9. Have all required export files been provided to the CDF and PDF?

      A3.23.2.11. Is DCAPES monitored for changes/updates to the TPFDD?

                                             Attachment 5
                           DEPLOYMENT WORKCENTER TRAINING

A5.1. Deployment Work Center Training Requirements. The following table contains a list
of mandatory and recommended training classes for deployment work center personnel, and
augmentees, based on specific roles and responsibilities. Items denoted with an asterisk (*) are
the minimum mandatory training requirements for work center personnel and augmentees. The
IDP will identify and document (by name) those positions within each deployment work center
that require mandatory training based on the expected performance of the duties assigned to each
work center position. MAJCOMs are authorized to supplement to indicate mandatory training
requirements. NOTE: DTR 4500.9-R for non-AMC units.

Table A5.1. Deployment Work Center Training Requirements
                                                            RECORD
              TYPE                   FREQUENCY              KEEPER            REFERENCE(S)
                                                          Workcenter
                                Initial                                AFI 10-403
Workcenter Orientation 1                                  OIC/NCOIC

                                           Attachment 6
                             CARGO CATEGORY CODES (CCC)

A6.1. This code identifies the types of cargo for force or non unit-related cargo requirements.
The cargo category code consist of three characters. Each character position has unique codes
and meanings (Ref: CJCSM 3150.16C). The following tables list valid codes and meanings for
each character position. NOTE: Second character position codes are different between force and
non unit cargo categories.

Table A6.1. First Position CCCs – Identifies CargoType
       Vehicles (wheeled and tracked, self-propelled or non-self-propelled) that are neither
       security nor hazardous cargo (see codes K and L for security and hazardous vehicles) and
A
       are not suitable for road marching on overland deployment legs. See code R for road
       capable vehicles.
       Non-self-deploying aircraft (NSDA) that are uncrated (if self-deployable aircraft will not be
B      deployed under their own power, they are identified as NSDA and their force movement
       characteristics reported).
C      Floating craft.
D      Hazardous non-vehicular cargo. (See code E).
E      Security non-vehicular cargo or non-vehicular cargo that is both security and hazardous.
F      Cargo requiring refrigeration by the mover.
G      Bulk POL (non-packaged)-fuel contained in unit tankers.
H      Bulk granular cargo; crushed rock, sand, etc.
J      Other non-vehicular cargo, including water, packaged POL, crated aircraft, etc.
K      Vehicles designated as security cargo or both security and hazardous cargo.
L      Vehicles designated as hazardous cargo but not security cargo.
M      Ammunition.
N      Nuclear weapons.
P      Chemical munitions.
       Wheeled vehicles (self-propelled or non-self-propelled), neither security nor hazardous
R      cargo, that are suitable for road march on overland deployment legs and capable of convoy
       speeds up to 40 MPH.

Table A6.2. Second Position CCCs – Specifies Cargo Extension
    Non-Air-Transportable Cargo: Cargo that exceeds any of the dimensions 1,453 inches x 216
0
    inches x 156 inches and the width exceeds 144 inches.
    Outsized cargo: Cargo that exceeds the dimensions of oversized cargo and requires the use of
1   aircraft such as a C-5 or C-17 or surface transportation. An item exceeds 1,000 inches long by
    117 inches wide by 105 inches high in any one dimension.
    Oversized cargo: Cargo that exceeds the usable dimension of a 463L pallet loaded to the design
    height of 96 inches, but equal to or less than 1,000 inches in length, 117 inches in width, and 105
2
    inches in height. This cargo is air transportable on aircraft such as the C-5, C-17, C-130, KC-10
    and most civilian contract cargo carriers.
3   Bulk cargo: Dimensions less than that of oversize cargo.
8   Organic cargo: Moved by unit resources.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                        289


Table A6.3. Third Position CCCs – Cargo Containerization
   This cargo is normally carried on a deploying vehicle and is not applicable to non unit-
A  related cargo coded as a CIN. When non unit-related cargo is entered in a ULN, value “A”
   will be used.
   This cargo can be containerized, meets the dimensional criteria for a 20-foot container (225"
B
   X 84" X 82"), and does not exceed a weight of 20 short tons. See NOTE 2.
   This cargo can be containerized, does not meet the dimensional criteria for a 20-foot
C container, but does meet the dimensional criteria for a 40-foot container (468 inches x 84
   inches x 86 inches) and does not exceed a weight of 40 short tons.
D This cargo cannot or will not be containerized.
E Loaded 20-foot containers.
F Loaded 40-foot containers.
G Loaded flat rack.
   Cargo already in containers and can be moved in this configuration. An example of this
H cargo would be a field hospital, which is stored in containerized configuration and moved as
   a container cargo.
NOTE 1: All dimensions are expressed in length X width X height. Width and height pertain to
         aircraft door limitations.
NOTE 2: Interior dimensions of a 20-foot container are 231" X 92" X 87". Containers are used
         for sealift.
NOTE 3: Interior dimensions of a 40-foot container are 473" X 92" X 92". Containers are used
         for sealift.

                                     Attachment 8
       REPORTING UNIT LEVEL UNIT TYPE CODE (UTC) DATA TO JOPES

A8.1. Reporting Unit Level UTC Data to JOPES.
   A8.1.1. At the direction of the parent MAJCOM, wings will electronically pass their
   LOGMOD-generated “DCAPES Schedule Export” files to their MAJCOM.             Parent
   MAJCOMs must make the determination when their units send these files. For example,
   when there are very limited or no changes to the standard UTC, a LOGMOD-generated
   “DCAPES Schedule Export” file would not be required. When there are major end-
   item/increment level changes/tailoring, the LOGMOD-generated “DCAPES Plan Export”
   would be required. When required, ANG units will send their files to NGB/A3X for
   subsequent forwarding to gaining MAJCOMs or direct import into DCAPES.
   A8.1.2. Prior to importing the LOGMOD-generated “DCAPES Schedule Export” or
   “DCAPES Plan Export” files into DCAPES, MAJCOMs will ensure UTCs/ULNs match
   TPFDD UTC/ULNs. Deploying units (with cargo) will only send files for ULNs with
   tailored UTCs.
   A8.1.3. Supporting MAJCOMs must ensure the LOGMOD-generated “DCAPES Schedule
   Export” or “DCAPES Plan Export” file (provided from the base) are imported into DCAPES
   prior to providing TPFDD verification to the supported commander. Once the supported
   commander provides TPFDD validation to USTRANSCOM, the UTC/ULN will be locked
   and cannot be updated.
   A8.1.4. MAJCOMs are authorized to provide additional guidance for MAJCOM specific
   requirements.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                          293

                                        Attachment 20
                     *DEPLOYMENT MEDICAL REQUIREMENTS

A20.1. Deployment medical requirements include all medical requirements prescribed for
deployments in DODIs, AFIs, CCDR reporting instructions, and other applicable policies.
A20.2. Deployment medical requirements span the pre- and post-deployment cycle and include
various requirements, which may vary based on the deployer’s component (e.g., Active Duty,
ARC, Air Force civilian, or contractor). NOTE: MTFs will not process contractors for
deployment, unless the deploying individual’s contract specifically states that medical services
must be provided. The installation/wing must provide reimbursement (e.g., funding and/or
manpower) to the MTF for providing contractually required deployment-related medical
clearance services to deploying contractors. A copy of the contract containing exact medical
specifications must be provided to the PH/Force Health Management Office prior to initiation of
any medical clearance activities or services.
   A20.2.1. DOD civilians are subject to the medical, dental, and psychological requirements
   established by federal law, DODI and the CCDR responsible for the deployment AOR, both
   prior to and including the entire period of their deployment.
   A20.2.2. Civilian Personnel Services (Human Resources) will coordinate with installation
   medical authorities and deployment processing representatives to establish local civilian-
   deployment procedures that comply with this directive. When possible, civilians will be
   integrated into existing pre- and post-deployment medical clearance programs.
A20.3. IAW DOD and Air Force policy, five Deployment Health Assessments (DHAs) must be
completed at specific intervals throughout the deployment cycle. The five DHA requirements
are outlined in figure A20.1.
   A20.3.1. The DHA process includes two steps: 1). Electronic completion of the prescribed
   DHA form via ASIMS Web (paper forms will not be accepted), and 2). A face-to-face
   (person-to-person for ARC personnel) interview with a healthcare provider. NOTE:
   Personnel will remain on their unit’s due/overdue action list in ASIMS Web until they
   complete both steps of the DHA process.
   A20.3.2. IAW DODI 6490.03, Deployment Health, all DOD civilian employees must
   complete pre- and post-deployment health assessments consistent with requirements for
   military personnel to effectively identify and evaluate deployment-related health concerns.
   AF MTFs may be used for administration of DHAs; however, the employee’s organization of
   record is responsible for DHA compliance, tracking, and monitoring.

deployment. Until DHA #1 is completed, the member will remain due for DHAs for the previous
deployment.


A20.4. Compliance with deployment medical requirements of assigned personnel is a
commander’s responsibility. Installation/wing commanders will ensure subordinate-level
commanders maintain IMR and deployment medical requirements on their assigned personnel.
    A20.4.1. While MTFs are responsible for providing access to care, commanders must work
    closely with MTFs to ensure Airmen receive timely care and support for health care needs.
A20.5. Pre-Deployment Medical Clearance
    A20.5.1. The UDM will (upon receipt of deployment tasking):
        A20.5.1.1. Review Medical Profile (AF Form 469, Duty Limiting Condition Report)
        status of deploying members for mobility restrictions and remove members with mobility
        restriction(s) listed on the AF 469 (coded 81 - Pregnancy, 37 - Medical Evaluation Board,
        31 – Illness or Injury) from deployment. UDMs will use ASIMS Web to access profile
        information. NOTE: Members with mobility restrictions annotated on the AF 469
        should not be deployed. Commanders wishing to deploy a Service member on a mobility
        restricting profile can request a medical waiver through the appropriate COCOM. The
        commander should consult the medical senior profile officer for further guidance on
        medical waivers.
        A20.5.1.2. Notify PH/FHM of deployment tasking via certified DRMD, certified tasking
        order, memo signed by commander, or official e-mail).
        A20.5.1.3. Provide PH/FHM a by-name listing of members tasked to deploy. List must
        contain: last name, first name, middle initial, social security number, and estimated
        RDD. NOTE: Only members officially tasked to deploy will be medically cleared by
        PH/FHM.
308                                          AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


      A20.5.1.4. Ensure deploying unit member(s) initiate the pre-deployment medical
      clearance process with PH/FHM 120 days prior to deployment date or date of first
      movement (e.g., training attendance) to complete pre-deployment medical clearance
      requirements. NOTE: Short-notice taskings may require expedited medical clearance.
      Consult with PH/FHM for installation-specific guidance on the expedited medical
      clearance process.
      A20.5.1.5. Advise personnel with any type of medical allergies to obtain the appropriate
      documentation from the MTF in order to acquire a Red Metal (Medical) Alert ID (if
      available).
      A20.5.1.6. Ensure, when identified by PH/FHM through the DMC Module in ASIMS
      Web, deploying Service member promptly completes the DHA #1 (DD Form 2795).
      A20.5.1.7. The DMC Module of ASIMS Web (https://imr.afms.mil/imr/loginunit.aspx)
      will be used to monitor and track unit member’s medical clearance status until completion.
  A20.5.2. The Individual Member will (upon notification by UDM):
      A20.5.2.1. At any point during the clearance process and prior to deployment, notify
      commander of any medical condition(s) that may limit their ability to deploy. NOTE:
      Personnel on a mobility restricting medical profile must see a medical provider prior to
      reporting to PH/FHM for medical clearance.
      A20.5.2.2. When notified by UDM, log on to My IMR in ASIMS Web
      (https://imr.afms.mil/imr/MyIMR.aspx) and complete DHA #1 (DD Form 2795)
      electronically. Paper copies of the DHA will not be accepted by PH/FHM. PRP and PSP
      must complete DHA forms at the MTF. NOTE: Personnel can also access My IMR via
      the AF Portal. Under “Featured Links,” select “Deployment & Readiness,” select
      “Medical Readiness-Deployment Health,” and then select the link for DHA #1 (Pre-
      Deployment Health Assessment, DD Form 2795).
         A20.5.2.2.1. An appointment with a credentialed, trained health care provider is
         required to complete the DHA process.
      A20.5.2.3. Obtain Installation Deployment Out-Processing Checklist from UDM and/or
      IPR. Deployment out-processing must include completion of requirements outlined
      Table A20.2., Pre-Deployment Medical Requirements Checklist.
      A20.5.2.4. Report to PH/FHM to complete deployment medical clearance processing
      IAW CCDR and other reporting instruction requirements.
      A20.5.2.5. Upon completion of medical clearance process, have PH/FHM sign and date
      the Installation Deployment Out-Processing Checklist.
  A20.5.3. Pre-Deployment Medical Clearance for DOD Civilians:
      A20.5.3.1. All DOD civilians entering theater for more than 30 days will be medically
      cleared for deployment prior to departure from their home station (or designated
      deployment processing center). Medical clearances must comply with DODI 6490.07,
      Deployment-Limiting Medical Conditions for Service Members and DOD Civilian
      Employees, DODI, 6490.03, Deployment Health, and respective CCDR Reporting
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                     309


     Instructions. Individuals who fail to comply with these requirements will not be cleared
     to deploy.
     A20.5.3.2. DOD civilians must bring an OF-178, Certificate of Medical Examination, to
     PH/FHM, with Part B completed by the Appointing Officer. DOD civilians who report
     to the MTF without an OF-178 and a completed Part B will be returned to their unit.
     PH/FHM will schedule an appointment (same day if available) with an MTF physician to
     conduct the medical examination and to document any deployment limiting medical
     conditions. Individuals who fail to report to PH/FHM or complete these medical
     requirements will not be cleared to deploy.
     A20.5.3.3. Civilians who wish to deploy, but have a deployment-limiting medical
     condition as defined in DODI 6490.07, must submit medical documentation required for
     waiver to the CCDR (or designee), to determine if the condition can be reasonably
     accommodated in theater. In certain instances, a wavier may not be possible due to
     limited scope of care at a deployed location. Civilians who fail to disclose a diagnosed
     deployment limiting medical condition during the pre-deployment medical clearance
     process, and arrive in theater without waiver, may be returned to home station at their
     own expense. NOTE: Civilians who develop a deployment-limiting medical condition
     while in theater that cannot be resolved must also obtain a medical waiver in order to
     remain in theater. Designated medical authorities may direct the curtailment of a DOD
     civilian’s deployment, if the medical condition cannot be resolved or reasonably
     accommodated.
  A20.5.4. PH/FHM will:
     A20.5.4.1. Create deployment records in the DMC Module of ASIMS Web and
     update/monitor the medical clearance status of deploying members in DMC.
        A20.5.4.1.1. Use the DMC Module of ASIMS Web to track and to monitor Service
        members, DOD civilians, and contractors.
     A20.5.4.2. Provide IDO, IPR and UDM with location-specific medical requirements and
     guidance IAW DODI, CCDR, and reporting instructions.
     A20.5.4.3. Initiate medical clearance process for deploying member (within 120 days
     prior to deployment or date first movement) IAW DODI, CCDR, and reporting
     instructions.
     A20.5.4.4. Verify IMR and medical profile (AF Form 469) status of member.
     A20.5.4.5. Ensure all deployment-specific medical requirements are visible on the
     ASIMS- generated DD Form 2766 print-out before sealing record.
     A20.5.4.6. Provide medical threat briefing to deploying member(s).
     A20.5.4.7. Communicate to member and UDM deployment deficiencies that could limit
     member’s ability to obtain medical clearance for deployment.
     A20.5.4.8. Verify electronic completion of DHA #1 (DD Form 2795).
     A20.5.4.9. Verify all pre-deployment medical clearance requirements are complete, and
     sign the deployer’s installation out-processing checklist (see Table A20.2).

A20.6. Post-Deployment Medical Requirements
   A20.6.1. Pre-Reintegration (Prior to Redeployment)
       A20.6.1.1. The Individual Member will:
          A20.6.1.1.1. Within 30 days of departing theater, log on to My IMR in ASIMS Web
          (https://imr.afms.mil/imr/MyIMR.aspx) and complete the DHA #2 (DD Form
          2796) electronically. PRP and PSP must complete DHA forms at the MTF. NOTE:
          Personnel can also access My IMR via the AF Portal. Under “Featured Links,” select
          “Deployment & Readiness,” select “Medical Readiness-Deployment Health,” and
          then select the link for DHA #2 (Post-Deployment Health Assessment, DD Form
          2796).
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                      313


            A20.6.1.1.1.1. An appointment with a credentialed, trained health care provider is
            required to complete the DHA process.
            A20.6.1.1.1.2. DHA #2 must be completed prior to taking leave en route (see
            section 8.9.8.7.3).
         A20.6.1.1.2. Out-Process through the deployed MTF
  A20.6.2. Home station Reintegration, Recovery, and Reconstitution (after Arrival at Home
  station)
     A20.6.2.1. Commanders will ensure that redeploying personnel complete required
     medical processing immediately upon return from deployment, and prior to release for
     downtime, leave, or demobilization IAW ASD (HA) Policy Memo, 10 Mar 2005.
     A20.6.2.2. The UDM will:
         A20.6.2.2.1. Ensure individual unit members (to include civilians) promptly
         complete all due/overdue post-deployment health requirements identified by
         PH/FHM (e.g. post-deployment health assessments, serum draws, PHAs, dental
         exams, IMR requirements, etc.).
         A20.6.2.2.2. Notify personnel 90 days after return from deployment to complete
         DHA #3 (DD Form 2900). The UDM will ensure the DHA #3 process is completed
         within the required timeframe (90-180 days after return).
         A20.6.2.2.3. Notify personnel to complete DHA #4 (Deployment MHA). The UDM
         will ensure the DHA #4 process is completed within the required timeframe (181-545
         days after return). NOTE: DHA #4 cannot be completed within 90 days of DHA #3.
         A20.6.2.2.4. Notify personnel to complete DHA #5 (Deployment MHA). The UDM
         will ensure the DHA #5 process is completed within the required timeframe (546-910
         days after return). NOTE: DHA #5 cannot be completed within 90 days of DHA #4.
     A20.6.2.3. The Individual Member will:
         A20.6.2.3.1. Report to PH/FHM for in-processing and completion of post-
         deployment medical requirements. Bring DD2766 (Deployment Medical Record),
         and any other deployment-related medical documents. NOTE: In-Processing at
         PH/FHM must be accomplished within five business days of return, and prior to
         taking leave or reconstitution/recuperation (or release of ARC personnel from Active
         Duty).
         A20.6.2.3.2. When notified by UDM, log on to My IMR in ASIMS Web
         (https://imr.afms.mil/imr/MyIMR.aspx) and complete DHA #3 (DD Form 2900)
         electronically. PRP and PSP must complete DHA forms at the MTF. NOTE:
         Personnel can also access My IMR via the AF Portal. Under “Featured Links,” select
         “Deployment & Readiness,” select “Medical Readiness-Deployment Health,” and
         then select the link for DHA #3 (Post-Deployment Health Reassessment, DD Form
         2900).
            A20.6.2.3.2.1. An appointment with a credentialed, trained health care provider is
            required to complete the DHA process.
 314                                        AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013


          A20.6.2.3.3. When notified by UDM, log on to My IMR in ASIMS Web
          (https://imr.afms.mil/imr/MyIMR.aspx) and complete DHA #4 and DHA #5
          (Deployment MHA) electronically. PRP and PSP must complete DHA forms at the
          MTF.
             A20.6.2.3.3.1. An appointment with a credentialed, trained health care provider is
             required to complete the DHA process. NOTE: DHA #4 and DHA #5 are
             required for Active Duty and ARC personnel only. DHA #4 and DHA #5 are not
             included in deployment medical requirements for DOD civilian personnel.
       A20.6.2.4. PH/FHM will:
          A20.6.2.4.1. Complete post-deployment in-processing and associated medical
          requirements.
          A20.6.2.4.2. Review member’s deployment medical record and confirm electronic
          completion of DHA #2 (DD Form 2796). Review the completed DHA #2 for
          recommended referrals. If no referrals are indicated on the DHA #2, ask the member
          if there are any deployment-related health concerns they would like to discuss with a
          provider. PH/FHM will coordinate recommended and requested referrals via
          AHLTA t-con to the member’s PCM. NOTE: If DHA #2 was not completed in
          theater—or not completed electronically in theater—PH/FHM will instruct member
          to complete DHA #2 electronically within 30 days of return from deployment. An
          appointment with a credentialed, trained health care provider is required to complete
          the DHA process.
          A20.6.2.4.3. Verify that the deployment record is accurate and complete and close
          member’s deployment record in ASIMS Web, once all post-deployment health
          requirements have been completed.
          A20.6.2.4.4. Sign member’s Installation Redeployment/In-Processing Checklist.
          A20.6.2.4.5. Support Installation Reintegration Program, as required.
          A20.6.2.4.6. Maintain updated deployment records and ensure that cancellations,
          modifications, and actual deployment dates are entered correctly and in a timely
          manner.
A20.7. Resources
   A20.7.1. MyIMR (https://imr.afms.mil/imr/MyIMR.aspx) provides a listing of the
   individual member’s due/overdue medical requirements. MyIMR also links members to
   web-based health readiness and deployment-related health assessments, such as DHAs and
   the WebHA.
   A20.7.2. AEF Online Commander’s Toolkit (https://aef.afpc.randolph.af.mil/default.aspx)
   provides comprehensive expeditionary and operations information.
   A20.7.3. Unit IMR compliance information (https://imr.afms.mil/imr/LoginUnit.aspx)
   provides commanders and UDMs with rosters of due/overdue medical requirements for unit
   personnel.
AFI10-403_USAFESUP_I 9 DECEMBER 2013                                                       315


  A20.7.4. Deployment Health Knowledge Junction on the Air Force Medical Service
  Knowledge Exchange (https://kx.afms.mil/deploymenthealth) provides policy and
  guidance for all stakeholders in the DHA process.
  A20.7.5. Airman’s        Guide       for      Assisting       Personnel      in      Distress
  (http://airforcemedicine.afms.mil/idc/groups/public/documents/webcontent/knowledgej
  unction.hcst?functionalarea=LeadersGuideDistress&doctype=subpage&docname=CTB
  _205851) educates leaders and wingmen in recognizing distressed personnel, offers general
  guidance for actions to take, and provides a list of helping resources/agencies available for
  assistance.
  A20.7.6. USAF Suicide Prevention Program Website (http://afspp.afms.mil) provides
  information and tools to members of the Air Force community in their efforts to help reduce
  AF suicides.
  A20.7.7. Air         Force        Warrior          Wellness    Facebook         Page
  (www.facebook.com/usairforcewarriorwellness) provides readiness and deployment health
  information for Air Force member and their loved ones.
